Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Rulings on Disposing of Price Before Possession and Voluntary Increases/Reductions
States permissibility of using price before possession and voluntary adjustments with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of the price before possession and explain the permissibility of voluntary increases and reductions in sale transactions, citing the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Price can be used before possession because it is fungible; voluntary adjustments are permissible and commendable.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents four related rulings on post-contract actions: using the price before taking possession, the buyer increasing the price, the seller increasing the commodity, and reducing the price. These are supported by hadiths demonstrating the Prophet's guidance on generosity in transactions. The key principle is that the price (thaman) is fungible (mithli), allowing earlier disposition, and voluntary adjustments are valid based on mutual consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four rulings
Read the initial statement: disposing of price before possession, buyer increasing price, seller increasing commodity, and reducing price. All are declared permissible.
The phrase 'wa yata'allaqu al-istihqaq bi jami'i dhalik' means entitlement attaches to these adjustments.
2
Understand the basis for price disposition
Note that dirhams and dinars are fungible (mithli), so they do not require specific identification; thus, the seller may dispose of the price before physically receiving it.
This contrasts with the general rule that the commodity (muthman) cannot be disposed of before possession.
3
Examine the first hadith proof (Abu Rafi')
The Prophet repaid a borrowed camel with a better one, showing the permissibility and commendability of giving extra. This supports the ruling that a seller may increase the commodity.
Hadith indicates that giving better quality is virtuous and legally valid.
4
Examine the second hadith proof (Suwayd ibn Qays)
The Prophet instructed a weigher to 'weigh and add extra', which analogically applies to giving extra goods or weight. This supports increasing the commodity or price.
The command indicates permissibility; it is not obligatory.
5
Examine the third hadith proof (Hudhayfah)
The hadith about the man who ordered his youths to give respite and forgive the wealthy encourages leniency, relating to reducing the price or granting discounts.
The principle of forgiveness in debts is applied to price reductions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالتَّصَرُّفُ فِي الثَّمَنِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ جَائِزٌ. وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي أَنْ يَزِيدَ الْبَائِعَ فِي الثَّمَنِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْبَائِعِ أَنْ يَزِيدَ لِلْمُشْتَرِي فِي الْمَبِيعِ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَحُطَّ مِنْ الثَّمَنِ. وَيَتَعَلَّقُ الِاسْتِحْقَاقُ بِجَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ. عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ قَالَ: إِذَا بِعْتَ شَيْئًا بِدِينَارٍ، فَحَلَّ الْأَجَلُ، فَخُذْ بِالدِّينَارِ مَا شِئْتَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ النَّوْعِ وَغَيْرِهِ. عَنْ أَبِي رَافِعٍ، قَالَ: اسْتَسْلَفَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بَكْرًا، فَجَاءَتْهُ إِبِلٌ مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ، فَأَمَرَنِي أَنْ أَقْضِيَ الرَّجُلَ بَكْرَهُ، فَقُلْتُ: لم أَجِدْ فِي الْإِبِلِ إِلَّا جَمَلًا خِيَارًا رَبَاعِيًا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «أَعْطِهِ إِيَّاهُ، فَإِنَّ خِيَارَ النَّاسِ أَحْسَنُهُمْ قَضَاءً». حَدَّثَنِي سُوَيْدُ بْنُ قَيْسٍ، قَالَ: جَلَبْتُ أَنَا وَمَخْرَفَةُ الْعَبْدِيُّ، بَنَّا مِنْ هَجَرَ فَأَتَيْنَا بِهِ مَكَّةَ فَجَاءَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَمْشِي فَسَاوَمَنَا بِسَرَاوِيلَ، فَبِعْنَاهُ، وَثَمَّ رَجُلٌ يَزِنُ بِالْأَجْرِ، فَقَالَ لَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «زِنْ وأَرْجِحْ». أَنَّ حُذَيْفَةَ حَدَّثَهُ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تَلَقَّتِ الْمَلَائِكَةُ رُوحَ رَجُلٍ مِمَّنْ كَانَ قَبْلَكُمْ، قَالُوا: أَعَمِلْتَ مِنَ الْخَيْرِ شَيْئًا؟ قَالَ: كُنتُ آمُرُ فِتْيَانِي أَنْ يُنْظِرُوا وَيَتَجَاوَزُوا عَنِ الْمُوسِرِ، قَالَ: فَتَجَاوَزُوا عَنْهُ».
And disposing of the price before possession is permissible. And it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller, and it is permissible for the seller to increase the commodity for the buyer, and it is permissible to reduce the price. And entitlement (istihqaq) attaches to all of that. From Ibn Sirin, he said: When you sell something for a dinar, and the term is due, then take with the dinar whatever you wish of that type or other. From Abu Rafi', he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, borrowed a young camel, then camels from charity came to him, so he ordered me to repay the man his young camel. I said: I did not find among the camels except a superior four-year-old camel. The Prophet said: 'Give it to him, for the best of people are those who are best in repaying.' Suwayd ibn Qays narrated: I and Makhrafah al-Abdi brought cloth from Hajar and came with it to Mecca. The Messenger of Allah came walking, haggled with us over trousers, and we sold them to him. There was a man who weighed for wages. The Prophet said to him: 'Weigh and add extra.' Hudhayfah narrated: The Prophet said: 'The angels received the soul of a man from those before you. They asked: Did you do any good deeds? He said: I used to order my youths to give respite and to forgive the wealthy. So they forgave him.'
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage contains several related rulings. First, the price (thaman) in a sale can be disposed of by the seller before he actually takes possession of it. This is because dirhams and dinars are not specific items; they are fungible (mithli). The hadith from Ibn Sirin, though from a tabi'i, supports this: one may take the dinar and buy something else with it before physically receiving it. Second, the buyer may voluntarily increase the price after the contract, and the seller may give extra goods to the buyer, or either party may reduce the price. These voluntary adjustments are permissible and commendable. The hadith of Abu Rafi' shows the Prophet giving a better camel in repayment, which is an increase in value. The hadith of Suwayd ibn Qays shows the Prophet instructing a weigher to give extra weight when weighing, indicating generosity in transactions. The final hadith of Hudhayfah encourages leniency and forgiveness in debts, which relates to reducing or forgiving amounts. The phrase 'wa yata'allaqu al-istihqaq bi jami'i dhalik' means that the right of entitlement (istihqaq) attaches to all these adjustments; that is, the increased amount or the discount becomes part of the contract's obligations. The rulings are all based on the principle of mutual consent and the encouragement of generosity in trade.

Key Terms
الثمن (al-thaman): The price paid in a sale, typically in currency.
الاستحقاق (al-istihqaq): The legal entitlement or right that attaches to the subject matter of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a seller disposing of the price (thaman) before taking possession of it?
A) It is prohibited because the seller does not physically have it.
B) It is permissible because the price is fungible (mithli).
C) It is permissible only if the buyer agrees.
D) It is makruh tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
The price in a sale is fungible, so it can be disposed of before possession; voluntary increases/reductions are permissible and commendable, with entitlement attaching to adjustments.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Main Ruling: Disposition of Price Before Possession
Ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposition of the price before possession and explain the hadith proof from Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
The price is owned immediately upon contract, so disposition before possession is allowed.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling in the chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah: the seller may dispose of the price (thaman) before physically receiving it. The Hanafi school differentiates between price and commodity, relying on hadith and a usul principle about fungible money. We will analyze the proof and the cross-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Understand that the ruling concerns the seller's right to dispose of the price (thaman) before possession (qabd). The text states it is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'When you sell, measure; when you buy, also measure.' This is cited as evidence.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Determine how this hadith proves the ruling. The command to measure implies the seller has authority over the price even before receiving it, since measuring is an act of disposal.
Also note the supporting hadith of Jabir about two measures.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school generally holds that one cannot dispose of the price before possession, analogizing it to the commodity. Understand the point of ikhtilaf.
5
Identify the usul principle
The principle at the end: dinars and dirhams are not determined by specification, so possession is not necessary for ownership. This is the underlying rationale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْمُرَابَحَةِ وَالتَّوْلِيَةِ فَالتَّصَرُّفُ فِي الثَّمَنِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ جَائِزٌ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي أَنْ يَزِيدَ الْبَائِعَ فِي الثَّمَنِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْبَائِعِ أَنْ يَزِيدَ لِلْمُشْتَرِي فِي الْمَبِيعِ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَحُطَّ مِنْ الثَّمَنِ وَيَتَعَلَّقُ الِاسْتِحْقَاقُ بِجَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ وَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالتَّصَرُّفُ فِي الثَّمَنِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ جَائِزٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ لَهُ إِذَا بِعْتَ فَكِلْ وَإِذَا ابْتَعْتَ فَاكْتَلْ (بخاري شريف بَابُ الْكَيْلِ عَلَى الْبَائِعِ وَالْمُعْطِي، نمبر 2126 / مسلم شريف: بَاب بُطْلَانِ بَيْعِ الْمَبِيعِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ غمبر 1528) وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الطَّعَامِ حَتَّى يَجْرِيَ فِيهِ الصَّاعَانِ، صَاعُ الْبَائِعِ، وَصَاعُ الْمُشْتَرِي» (سنن ابي ماجه: بَابُ النَّهْيِ عَنْ بَيْعِ الطَّعَامِ قَبْلُ مَا لَمْ يُقْبَضٌ، غمبر 2228) وَوَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي أَنْ يَزِيدَ الْبَائِعَ فِي الثَّمَنِ عَنْ أَبِي رَافِعٍ قَالَ: اسْتَسْلَفَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَكْرًا فَجَاءَتْهُ إِبِلٌ مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ فَأَمَرَنِي أَنْ أَقْضِيَ الرَّجُلَ بَكْرَهُ فَقُلْتُ: لم أَجِدْ فِي الْإِبِلِ إِلَّا جَمَلًا خِيَارًا رَبَاعِيًا فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أَعْطِهِ إِيَّاهُ فَإِنَّ خِيَارَ النَّاسِ أَحْسَنُهُمْ قَضَاءً» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي حُسْنِ الْقَضَاءِ، نمبر 3346) وَوَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْبَائِعِ أَنْ يَزِيدَ لِلْمُشْتَرِي فِي الْمَبِيعِ حَدَّثَنِي سُوَيْدُ بْنُ قَيْسٍ قَالَ: جَلَبْتُ أَنَا وَمَخْرَفَةُ الْعَبْدِيُّ بَنَّا مِنْ هَجَرَ فَأَتَيْنَا بِهِ مَكَّةَ فَجَاءَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَمْشِي فَسَاوَمَنَا بِسَرَاوِيلَ فَبِعْنَاهُ وَثَمَّ رَجُلٌ يَزِنُ بِالْأَجْرِ فَقَالَ لَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «زِنْ وَأَرْجِحْ» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الرُّجْحَانِ فِي الْوَزْنِ وَالْوَزْنِ بِالْأَجْرِ، نمبر 3336) وَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَتَعَلَّقُ الِاسْتِحْقَاقُ بِجَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ أَنَّ حُذَيْفَةَ حَدَّثَهُ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «تَلَقَّتِ الْمَلَائِكَةُ رُوحَ رَجُلٍ مِمَّنْ كَانَ قَبْلَكُمْ قَالُوا: أَعَمِلْتَ مِنَ الْخَيْرِ شَيْئًا؟ قَالَ: كُنتُ آمُرُ فِتْيَانِي أَنْ يُنْظِرُوا وَيَتَجَاوَزُوا عَنِ الْمُوسِرِ قَالَ: قَالَ: فَتَجَاوَزُوا عَنْهُ» (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ أَنْظَرَ مُوسِرًا، غبر 2077) أُصُولٌ: شمن دینار و درہم ہو تو متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے لہذا قبضہ سے قبل تصرف جائز ہے۔
Chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. Disposition of the price before possession is permissible. It is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller, and it is permissible for the seller to increase the goods for the buyer, and it is permissible to deduct from the price, and the right of rescission attaches to all of that. Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that disposition of the price before possession is permissible: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to him: 'When you sell, measure; when you buy, also measure.' (Bukhari, chapter on measurement upon the seller and the giver, no. 2126 / Muslim, chapter on invalidity of selling goods before possession, no. 1528) And from Jabir who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of food until two measures pass over it, the seller's measure and the buyer's measure.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on prohibition of selling food before it is taken possession of, no. 2228) And evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller: from Abu Rafi' who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) borrowed a young camel. Then some camels from sadaqah came to him, so he ordered me to repay the man his young camel. I said: I found among the camels nothing but a choice adult camel. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Give it to him, for the best of people are those best in repayment.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on good repayment, no. 3346) And evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that it is permissible for the seller to increase the goods for the buyer: Suwayd ibn Qays narrated: 'I and Makhrafah al-Abdi brought some cloth from Hajar and brought it to Makkah. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came walking and bargained with us for trousers; we sold them to him, and there was a man weighing for wages, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to him: Weigh and give extra.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on giving extra in weight and weighing for wages, no. 3336) Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that the right of rescission attaches to all of that: that Hudhayfah narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The angels received the soul of a man from those before you. They said: Did you do any good deed? He said: I used to order my youth to grant respite and forbear from the wealthy. He said: So they forgave him.' (Bukhari, chapter on granting respite to a wealthy person, no. 2077) Principle: If the price is dinars and dirhams, they are not determined by specification, so disposition before possession is permissible.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. The core ruling (matn) states that it is permissible for the seller to dispose of the price (thaman) before taking physical possession of it. This is because in Hanafi fiqh, contrary to the commodity (muthman), the price becomes the property of the seller immediately upon conclusion of the contract. The principle mentioned in Urdu clarifies this: dinars and dirhams are not determined by specification (they are fungible), so one need not physically have them to own them. The matn then provides three subsidiary rulings: (1) The buyer may voluntarily increase the price for the seller after the contract; (2) The seller may increase the quantity of goods for the buyer; (3) The seller may reduce the price. In all these cases, the buyer's right of rescission (istihqaq) — i.e., the option to return the goods due to a defect or similar — applies fully, even after such adjustments. The author then provides hadith evidence for each ruling. For the main ruling, he cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Jabir about measuring. These hadith, while primarily about the importance of precise measurement, are interpreted as proof that the seller may dispose of the price because the price-commodity (thaman) is treated as owned. For the increase in price, he cites the story of Abu Rafi' where the Prophet repaid a borrowed camel with a better one, showing that voluntary increase is commendable. For the increase in goods, he cites the hadith of Suwayd where the Prophet ordered extra weight, indicating that giving more is permitted. For the retention of the right of rescission despite these changes, he cites the hadith about the man who ordered his youth to give respite and forbear, linking forgiveness in transactions to the idea that adjustments do not cancel the original terms of recourse.

Key Terms
المرابحة (al-murābaḥah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost price and adds a known profit margin.
التصرف (al-tasarruf): Any legal disposition such as sale, gift, or use of property.
القبض (al-qabḍ): Taking physical or legal possession of an item, transferring liability.
الاستحقاق (al-istiḥqāq): The right to claim return of goods due to a defect or option (khiyar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the seller disposing of the price before physically receiving it?
A) It is forbidden.
B) It is permissible.
C) It is only permissible if the price is gold.
D) It depends on the buyer's consent.

Key Takeaway
The price belongs to the seller from the moment of contract, so he may dispose of it before physical possession; this is based on the fungible nature of currency and the hadith of measurement.

Permissibility of Increases and Deductions, and Retention of Rescission Right
Ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on voluntary increases in price or goods, deductions, and the retention of the right of rescission, citing the relevant hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Voluntary increases and deductions are commendable, but they do not cancel the buyer's right to return defective goods.

After establishing the main ruling on disposition of the price, the matn addresses three subsidiary issues: the buyer may voluntarily increase the price, the seller may increase the goods, and the seller may deduct from the price. Importantly, even after such adjustments, the buyer still retains the right of rescission (istihqaq) for defects. Each ruling is supported by a specific hadith showing the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three subsidiary rulings
Note that the text allows: (1) buyer increasing price, (2) seller increasing goods, (3) seller deducting price. And that the right of rescission remains attached in all cases.
2
Analyze the proof for buyer increasing price
The hadith of Abu Rafi' where the Prophet repaid a borrowed camel with a better one. This shows that voluntarily giving more is permissible and even commendable.
3
Analyze the proof for seller increasing goods
The hadith of Suwayd ibn Qays where the Prophet ordered an extra weight when buying cloth. This proves the seller may give more than agreed.
4
Analyze the proof for retention of rescission right
The hadith about the man who ordered his youth to give respite and forbearance. The angels forgave him, linking forgiveness in transactions to the idea that adjustments do not nullify original rights.
5
Understand the legal effect
These adjustments are voluntary and do not affect the contractual obligations; the buyer's option for defects remains intact.

بَابُ الْمُرَابَحَةِ وَالتَّوْلِيَةِ فَالتَّصَرُّفُ فِي الثَّمَنِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ جَائِزٌ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي أَنْ يَزِيدَ الْبَائِعَ فِي الثَّمَنِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْبَائِعِ أَنْ يَزِيدَ لِلْمُشْتَرِي فِي الْمَبِيعِ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَحُطَّ مِنْ الثَّمَنِ وَيَتَعَلَّقُ الِاسْتِحْقَاقُ بِجَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ وَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالتَّصَرُّفُ فِي الثَّمَنِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ جَائِزٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ لَهُ إِذَا بِعْتَ فَكِلْ وَإِذَا ابْتَعْتَ فَاكْتَلْ (بخاري شريف بَابُ الْكَيْلِ عَلَى الْبَائِعِ وَالْمُعْطِي، نمبر 2126 / مسلم شريف: بَاب بُطْلَانِ بَيْعِ الْمَبِيعِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ غمبر 1528) وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الطَّعَامِ حَتَّى يَجْرِيَ فِيهِ الصَّاعَانِ، صَاعُ الْبَائِعِ، وَصَاعُ الْمُشْتَرِي» (سنن ابي ماجه: بَابُ النَّهْيِ عَنْ بَيْعِ الطَّعَامِ قَبْلُ مَا لَمْ يُقْبَضٌ، غمبر 2228) وَوَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُشْتَرِي أَنْ يَزِيدَ الْبَائِعَ فِي الثَّمَنِ عَنْ أَبِي رَافِعٍ قَالَ: اسْتَسْلَفَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَكْرًا فَجَاءَتْهُ إِبِلٌ مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ فَأَمَرَنِي أَنْ أَقْضِيَ الرَّجُلَ بَكْرَهُ فَقُلْتُ: لم أَجِدْ فِي الْإِبِلِ إِلَّا جَمَلًا خِيَارًا رَبَاعِيًا فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أَعْطِهِ إِيَّاهُ فَإِنَّ خِيَارَ النَّاسِ أَحْسَنُهُمْ قَضَاءً» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي حُسْنِ الْقَضَاءِ، نمبر 3346) وَوَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْبَائِعِ أَنْ يَزِيدَ لِلْمُشْتَرِي فِي الْمَبِيعِ حَدَّثَنِي سُوَيْدُ بْنُ قَيْسٍ قَالَ: جَلَبْتُ أَنَا وَمَخْرَفَةُ الْعَبْدِيُّ بَنَّا مِنْ هَجَرَ فَأَتَيْنَا بِهِ مَكَّةَ فَجَاءَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَمْشِي فَسَاوَمَنَا بِسَرَاوِيلَ فَبِعْنَاهُ وَثَمَّ رَجُلٌ يَزِنُ بِالْأَجْرِ فَقَالَ لَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «زِنْ وَأَرْجِحْ» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الرُّجْحَانِ فِي الْوَزْنِ وَالْوَزْنِ بِالْأَجْرِ، نمبر 3336) وَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَتَعَلَّقُ الِاسْتِحْقَاقُ بِجَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ أَنَّ حُذَيْفَةَ حَدَّثَهُ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «تَلَقَّتِ الْمَلَائِكَةُ رُوحَ رَجُلٍ مِمَّنْ كَانَ قَبْلَكُمْ قَالُوا: أَعَمِلْتَ مِنَ الْخَيْرِ شَيْئًا؟ قَالَ: كُنتُ آمُرُ فِتْيَانِي أَنْ يُنْظِرُوا وَيَتَجَاوَزُوا عَنِ الْمُوسِرِ قَالَ: قَالَ: فَتَجَاوَزُوا عَنْهُ» (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ أَنْظَرَ مُوسِرًا، غبر 2077) أُصُولٌ: شمن دینار و درہم ہو تو متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے لہذا قبضہ سے قبل تصرف جائز ہے۔
Chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. Disposition of the price before possession is permissible. It is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller, and it is permissible for the seller to increase the goods for the buyer, and it is permissible to deduct from the price, and the right of rescission attaches to all of that. Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that disposition of the price before possession is permissible: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to him: 'When you sell, measure; when you buy, also measure.' (Bukhari, chapter on measurement upon the seller and the giver, no. 2126 / Muslim, chapter on invalidity of selling goods before possession, no. 1528) And from Jabir who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of food until two measures pass over it, the seller's measure and the buyer's measure.' (Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on prohibition of selling food before it is taken possession of, no. 2228) And evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller: from Abu Rafi' who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) borrowed a young camel. Then some camels from sadaqah came to him, so he ordered me to repay the man his young camel. I said: I found among the camels nothing but a choice adult camel. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Give it to him, for the best of people are those best in repayment.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on good repayment, no. 3346) And evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that it is permissible for the seller to increase the goods for the buyer: Suwayd ibn Qays narrated: 'I and Makhrafah al-Abdi brought some cloth from Hajar and brought it to Makkah. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came walking and bargained with us for trousers; we sold them to him, and there was a man weighing for wages, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to him: Weigh and give extra.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on giving extra in weight and weighing for wages, no. 3336) Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that the right of rescission attaches to all of that: that Hudhayfah narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The angels received the soul of a man from those before you. They said: Did you do any good deed? He said: I used to order my youth to grant respite and forbear from the wealthy. He said: So they forgave him.' (Bukhari, chapter on granting respite to a wealthy person, no. 2077) Principle: If the price is dinars and dirhams, they are not determined by specification, so disposition before possession is permissible.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. The core ruling (matn) states that it is permissible for the seller to dispose of the price (thaman) before taking physical possession of it. This is because in Hanafi fiqh, contrary to the commodity (muthman), the price becomes the property of the seller immediately upon conclusion of the contract. The principle mentioned in Urdu clarifies this: dinars and dirhams are not determined by specification (they are fungible), so one need not physically have them to own them. The matn then provides three subsidiary rulings: (1) The buyer may voluntarily increase the price for the seller after the contract; (2) The seller may increase the quantity of goods for the buyer; (3) The seller may reduce the price. In all these cases, the buyer's right of rescission (istihqaq) — i.e., the option to return the goods due to a defect or similar — applies fully, even after such adjustments. The author then provides hadith evidence for each ruling. For the main ruling, he cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Jabir about measuring. These hadith, while primarily about the importance of precise measurement, are interpreted as proof that the seller may dispose of the price because the price-commodity (thaman) is treated as owned. For the increase in price, he cites the story of Abu Rafi' where the Prophet repaid a borrowed camel with a better one, showing that voluntary increase is commendable. For the increase in goods, he cites the hadith of Suwayd where the Prophet ordered extra weight, indicating that giving more is permitted. For the retention of the right of rescission despite these changes, he cites the hadith about the man who ordered his youth to give respite and forbear, linking forgiveness in transactions to the idea that adjustments do not cancel the original terms of recourse.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): An increase in price or goods voluntarily given after the contract.
الحط (al-ḥaṭṭ): A reduction or deduction from the price.
الاستحقاق (al-istiḥqāq): The right to claim return of goods due to a defect or option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does the buyer's right of rescission (for defects) remain if the buyer voluntarily increases the price after the sale?
A) No, the right is lost because the increase implies satisfaction.
B) Yes, the right remains attached despite the increase.
C) It depends on whether the increase was significant.
D) Only if the increase was not requested by the seller.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary increases and deductions in a sale are permissible and do not cancel the buyer's right to return defective goods; the original contractual protections remain intact.

Deferment of Spot Debts and the Exception of Qard
Ruling that a spot debt can be made deferred except for qard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferment of spot debts and identify the exception of qard, citing the evidence from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
A spot debt can be deferred by agreement, but a loan remains spot and cannot be turned into a deferred obligation.

In sale contracts, the price is either spot or deferred. This lesson examines whether parties can change a spot price into a deferred one after the contract. The Hanafi school upholds this general permissibility but makes a crucial exception for loans (qard). The ruling is supported by a saying of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The matn states that if a spot price is deferred by agreement for a known term, it becomes a deferred debt. Note the condition that the term must be known.
This applies to any spot debt, not just sale prices.
2
Identify the exception
The text explicitly excludes qard (loan). Deferment of a qard is invalid; it remains spot regardless of any agreement.
Qard is a loan of fungible items like money or food.
3
State the evidence
The proof is the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'Qard is spot even if it is for a term.' This is a qawl of a tabi'i, accepted in Hanafi as a secondary source.
Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 20578
4
Explain the wisdom behind the exception
Qard is a gratuitous contract intended for help. Making it deferred would change its nature from a loan to a sale-like credit. The Hanafi view preserves the immediate right of the lender to demand repayment.
Other schools allow deferment by mutual agreement, but Hanafi maintains the original spot character.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ بَاعَ بِثَمَنٍ حَالٍ ثُمَّ أَجَّلَهُ أَجَلًا مَعْلُومًا صَارَ مُؤَجَّلًا وَكُلُّ دَيْنٍ حَالٍ إِذَا أَجَّلَهُ صَاحِبُهُ صَارَ مُؤَجَّلًا إِلَّا الْقَرْضَ فَإِنَّ تَأْجِيلَهُ لَا يَصِحُ وَجْهٌ : (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَكُلُّ دَيْنٍ حَالٍ إِذَا أَجَّلَهُ صَاحِبُهُ صَارَ مُؤَجَّلًا إِلَّا الْقَرْضَ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «وَالْقَرْضُ حَالٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ إِلَى أَجَلٍ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ: الْقَرْضُ حَالٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ إِلَى أَجَلٍ، غمبر 20578) أُصُولٌ: نقد قیمت پر بیچ منعقد ہوئی پھر متعین تاریخ کیساتھ متعین کر دیا تو اب موخر ہو جائے گی۔ لُغَاتٌ: هُبُوبِ الرّيحِ: ہوا کا چلنا، كَالْحَصَادِ: کھیتی کائنا، الدِّيَاسُ: کھیتی گاہنا۔
And whoever sells for a spot price, then defers it for a known term, it becomes deferred. And every spot debt, when its owner defers it, becomes deferred, except for qard (loan), for its deferment is invalid. Evidence: (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that every spot debt, when its owner defers it, becomes deferred except for qard: from Ibrahim who said: 'Qard is spot even if it is for a term.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who say: qard is spot even if for a term, no. 20578) Principle: The sale is concluded at a spot price, then if a specific date is set, it becomes deferred. Vocabulary: hubub al-rih: blowing of wind; ka al-hasad: like reaping; al-diyas: threshing.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that if a person sells for a spot price (thaman haal), i.e., immediate payment, and then both parties agree to defer that price for a known term, the price becomes deferred (mu'ajjal). This applies generally to any spot debt: if the creditor (owner of the debt) agrees to postpone payment, it becomes a deferred debt. The exception is qard (a loan of fungible items like money or food). Deferment of a qard is invalid; that is, if someone lends something, the loan remains spot and payable on demand even if they agree on a term. The proof cited is the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i): 'Qard is spot even if it is for a term.' This indicates that a loan cannot be turned into a deferred obligation; the borrower can be asked to repay at any time. The Urdu principle explains that the original contract was spot; setting a date later makes it deferred. The vocabulary items at the end appear to be from a different context (perhaps explaining terms from hadith about wind, harvest, and threshing) but are included here as part of the commentary.

Key Terms
حَال (ḥāl): An obligation that is due immediately, not deferred.
مُؤَجَّل (muʾajjal): An obligation that is due at a specified future date.
قَرْض (qarḍ): A loan of fungible goods or money, where the borrower returns the equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following cannot be turned into a deferred debt according to the Hanafi school?
A) A spot price in a sale of goods.
B) A loan (qard) of money.
C) A spot debt from a previous transaction.
D) All of the above can be deferred.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, any spot debt can be made deferred by mutual agreement, except for a loan (qard) which remains spot and payable on demand.

Hanafi Ruling on Riba in Measurable and Weighable Items
Ruling with multiple proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riba for makil and mawzun items, identify the illa (cause), and apply the ruling to distinguish permissible from prohibited sales.

Core Idea
Riba occurs in any measurable or weighable item traded for its own kind with excess — the cause is measure/weight plus sameness of genus.

This passage from Al-Quduri lays the foundation for the Hanafi position on riba. The author defines the prohibited transaction and clarifies the legal cause derived from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding this ruling is essential for every Muslim engaged in trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that riba is 'muharram' (prohibited) in every makil (measurable) and mawzun (weighable) item when sold for its own kind with excess. This is the ruling.
The ruling is haram, meaning absolute prohibition.
2
Locate the illa (legal cause)
The author explains the illa is 'al-kayl ma'a al-jins' (measure with genus) or 'al-wazn ma'a al-jins' (weight with genus). This means the prohibited excess applies only when two conditions coexist: same genus and same measurement/weight standard.
If the items are of different genres, or not makil/mawzun, excess does not constitute riba.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The author cites Quran 2:275: 'And Allah has permitted sale and prohibited riba.' This verse is the primary textual basis, but the general wording is specified by the hadith.
The verse is qat'i in thubut and dalala, establishing the principle.
4
Analyze the hadith proofs
Multiple hadiths are provided: (a) Abu Sa'id's hadith listing six commodities that must be exchanged like for like and hand to hand. (b) Fadala's hadith showing gold must be weighed. (c) Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib's hadith limiting riba to gold, silver, or what is measured/weighed and consumed. These establish the 'illa and extend the ruling to all makil/mawzun items.
The Hanafis use the hadith of Fadala to derive that weight is the 'illa for gold, and then generalize to all weighable items via qiyas.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and Hanafi tarjih
The Shafi'i school limits riba to gold, silver, and foodstuffs (makil/mawzun and edible). The Hanafis extend to all makil/mawzun even non-food, because the 'illa is attribute of measurement/weight regardless of edibility.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الرِّبَا
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ : الرِّبَا مُحَرَّمَ فِي كُلِّ مَكِيلٍ وَمَوْزُونٍ إِذَا بِيعَ بِجِنْسِهِ مُتَفَاضِلًا لَ فَالْعِلَّةُ فِيهِ الْكَيْلُ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ، أَوْ الْوَزْنُ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ ٣ وَإِذَا بِيعَ الْمَكِيلُ، أَوْ الْمَوْزُونُ بِجِنْسِهِ مِثْلَا بِمِثْلِ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَإِنْ تَفَاضَلَا لَمْ يَجُز
لوجه: (1) الآية لثبوت الرّبَا مُحَرَّمٌ فِي كُلِّ مَكِيلٍ وَمَوْزُونِ إِذَا بِيعَ بِجِنْسِهِ مُتَفَاضِلًا ﴿وَأَحَلَّ اللَّهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرّبوا ) (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت نمبر 275)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت الرِّبَا مُحَرَّمٌ فِي كُلِّ مَكِيلٍ وَمَوْزُونٍ إِذَا بِيعَ بِجُنْسِهِ مُتَفَاضِلًا عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة. والبر بالبر. وَالشَّعِيرُ بِالشَّعِيرِ وَالتَّمْرُ بِالتَّمْرِ. وَالْمِلْحُ بِالْمِلْحِ مِثَلًا مِثْلِ. يَدًا بِيَدِ. فَمَنْ زَادَ أَوِ اسْتَزَادَ فَقَدْ أَرْبَيَ. الْآخِذُ وَالْمُعْطِي فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ) مسلم شريف : بَاب الصَّرْفِ وَبَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ نَقْدًا،نمبر 1884) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَالْعِلَّةُ فِيهِ الْكَيْلُ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ اسَمِعْتُ فَضَالَةَ بْنَ عُبَيْدِ الْأَنْصَارِيَّ يَقُولُ: أُتي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهو بِخَيْبَرَ، بِقِلَادَةٍ فِيهَا خَرَزْ وَذَهَبٌ وَهِيَ مِنَ الْمَغَانِمِ تُبَاعُ فَأَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالذَّهَبِ الَّذِي فِي الْقِلَادَةِ فَتُرعَ وَحْدَهُ. ثُمَّ قَالَ لَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (الذَّهَبُ بِالذَّهَبِ وَزُنَا بِوَزْنِ مسلم شريف بَاب بَيْعِ الْقِلَادَةِ فِيهَا خَرَزْ وَذَهَبٌ، نمبر 1591) بِوَزْنِ)مسلم
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَالْعِلَّةُ فِيهِ الْكَيْلُ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ اعَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيِّبِ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ قَالَ: «لَا رَبَّا إِلَّا فِي ذَهَب أَوْ فِضَّةٍ أَوْ مِمَّا يُكَالُ أَوْ يُوزَنُ وَيُؤْكَلُ وَيَشْرَبُ» (سنن دار قطني، باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر 2834)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا بِيعَ الْمَكِيلُ، أَوْ الْمَوْزُونُ بِجِنْسِهِ اعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ الله الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والبر بالبر. وَالشَّعِيرُ بِالشَّعِيرِ وَالتَّمْرُ بِالتَّمْرِ. وَالْمِلْحُ بِالْمِلْحِ مِثلًا مِثْلِ. يَدًا بِيَدِ. فَمَنْ زَادَ أَوِ اسْتَزَادَ فَقَدْ أَرْبَيَ الْآخِذُ وَالْمُعْطِي فِيهِ (سَوَاءٌ مسلم شریف: بَاب الصَّرْفِ وَبَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ نَقْدًا، غمبر 1584) اصول : بائع یا مشتری میں سے کسی کے لئے زیادہ کی شرط لگائی ہو اور وہ عوض سے خالی ہو تو اسے رہا کہتے ہیں۔
اصول: احناف کے یہاں سود کی تین علتیں ہیں امبیع اور شمن دونوں ایک ہی جنس ہو ۲ دو وزنی ہو یا کیلی ہو۔
Chapter of Riba. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him: Riba is prohibited in every measurable (makil) and weighable (mawzun) thing, when sold for its own kind with excess. So the cause (illa) in it is measure with genus, or weight with genus. And when the measurable or weighable is sold for its own kind like for like, the sale is allowed; if they differ, it is not allowed. Proof: (1) The verse to establish that riba is prohibited in every measurable and weighable thing when sold for its own kind with excess: {And Allah has permitted sale and prohibited riba} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:275). Proof (2): The hadith to establish that riba is prohibited in every measurable and weighable thing when sold for its own kind with excess: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand. Whoever increases or asks for increase has practiced riba. The taker and the giver are alike.' (Sahih Muslim, Chapter of Sarf and Sale of Gold for Silver, no. 1884). Proof (1): The hadith to establish that the cause is measure with genus: I heard Fadala ibn Ubayd al-Ansari say: A necklace containing beads and gold was brought to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) at Khaybar, from the spoils, and was being sold. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered the gold in the necklace to be removed alone. Then he said to them: 'Gold for gold, weight for weight.' (Sahih Muslim, Chapter of Sale of a Necklace Containing Beads and Gold, no. 1591). Proof (2): The hadith to establish that the cause is measure with genus: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no riba except in gold or silver or in what is measured or weighed and eaten or drunk.' (Sunan Dar Qutni, Chapter of Sales, no. 2834). Proof (1): The hadith to establish that when the measurable or weighable is sold for its own kind: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... (repeat of earlier hadith). Principle: If a condition of excess is stipulated for either the seller or the buyer, and it is without a counter-exchange, then it is called riba. Principle: According to the Hanafis, riba has three causes: (1) the commodity and the price are both of the same genus; (2) both are weighable; (3) or both are measurable.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling with multiple proofs from Quran and Sunnah. The matn from the author declares that riba (usury) is prohibited in every item that is measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) when sold for its own kind with inequality (tafadul). If sold like for like (mithlan bi mithlin), the sale is permitted; if there is excess, it is not. The cause (illa) for the prohibition is the combination of measurement or weight with sameness of genus. The proofs are: (1) Quran 2:275, which permits sale and prohibits riba in general. (2) The well-known hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri listing six commodities: gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt — they must be exchanged hand to hand and like for like; excess constitutes riba. (3) The hadith of Fadala ibn Ubayd about a necklace with beads and gold: the Prophet ordered the gold to be separated and weighed, showing that gold must be exchanged weight for weight. (4) The hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: 'No riba except in gold, silver, or what is measured or weighed and consumed.' The Urdu notes explain: if a condition of extra payment is stipulated without a counter-value, that is riba; and according to the Hanafis, the illa for riba are three: same genus, both weighable or both measurable.

Key Terms
رِبَا (ribā): Usury or interest; specifically, any excess in exchange of two like items that are measured or weighed by weight or measure.
مَكِيل (makīl): Something that is sold by volume (measured), such as grains and liquids.
مَوْزُون (mawzūn): Something that is sold by weight, such as gold, silver, and other metals.
عِلَّة (ʿillah): The legal cause (effective reason) for the ruling; here it is the combination of measurement/weight with sameness of genus.
جِنْس (jins): Genus or kind; sameness of species, e.g. wheat with wheat, gold with gold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, under which condition does riba occur?
A) Only when gold or silver is exchanged with inequality.
B) Whenever a measurable or weighable item is sold for its own kind with an excess, regardless of the type of item.
C) Only when food items are exchanged with excess.
D) Whenever there is any deferred payment in a sale.

Key Takeaway
Riba is haram in every makil or mawzun item when sold for its own kind with excess; the illa is measure/weight plus genus.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Riba Prohibition in Same Genus Measured/Weighed Items
Ruling on riba in sales of same genus measured/weighed items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scenarios of riba based on the presence of genus and the joined meaning (measurement/weight) and state the ruling on disparity and delay for each.

Core Idea
Riba in sale of same genus items is prohibited when measured/weighed; if only one attribute present, delay alone is banned.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational matn from al-Quduri that delineates the conditions for riba in commodity exchanges. Unlike the common understanding that riba only applies to loans, classical Hanafi fiqh extends it to sales of measured and weighed items of the same kind. The central concept is the interplay of two attributes: the genus (jins) and the quality of being measured or weighed (al-ma'na al-madhmūm ilayh). Mastering this tripartite classification is essential for any student of Hanafi muamalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two relevant attributes
The two attributes are the genus (jins) and the 'joined meaning' (al-ma'na al-madhmūm ilayh), which designates the item as being customarily sold by measure (makīl) or weight (mawzūn). Note that both attributes refer to the nature of the commodity, not its quality or value.
2
Learn the ruling when both attributes are present
When the items are of the same genus and both are measured/weighed, any disparity (tafadul) or delay (nasi'ah) is prohibited. This is the classic case of riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah combined.
Example: selling 10 kg of wheat for 12 kg of wheat (same genus, both weighed).
3
Learn the ruling when both attributes are absent
When the items are of different genera and at least one is not measured/weighed (or both are not measured/weighed), both disparity and delay are permissible. There is no riba concern.
Example: selling 10 kg of wheat for 15 liters of oil (different genus, wheat is weighed, oil is measured).
4
Learn the ruling when only one attribute is present
When the items are of the same genus but at least one is not measured/weighed (or both are not measured/weighed), or when the items are of different genera but both are measured/weighed, disparity is permissible but delay is prohibited. This is because genus difference eliminates riba al-fadl, but the common measurement/weight trait still demands hand-to-hand exchange to avoid riba al-nasi'ah.
Example: selling 10 kg of wheat for 10 liters of oil (different genus, both measured/weighed?). Actually oil is measured, wheat weighed; they are both measured/weighed but different genus, so delay is haram but disparity halal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الرِّبَا
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ : الرِّبَا مُحَرَّمَ فِي كُلِّ مَكِيلٍ وَمَوْزُونٍ إِذَا بِيعَ بِجِنْسِهِ مُتَفَاضِلًا فَالْعِلَّةُ فِيهِ الْكَيْلُ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ، أَوِ الْوَزْنُ مَعَ الْجِنْسِ وَإِذَا بِيعَ الْمَكِيلُ، أَوِ الْمَوْزُونُ بِجِنْسِهِ مِثْلًا بِمِثْلٍ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَإِنْ تَفَاضَلَا لَمْ يَجُزْ
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْجَيْدِ بِالرَّدِيءِ مِمَّا فِيهِ الرِّبَا إِلَّا مِثْلًا بِمِثْلٍ وَإِذَا عُدِمَ الْوَصْفَانِ الْجِنْسُ، وَالْمَعْنَى الْمَضْمُومُ إِلَيْهِ حَلَّ التَّفَاضُلُ وَالنَّسَاءُ وَإِذَا وُجِدَا حَرُمَ التَّفَاضُلُ وَالنَّسَاءُ وَإِذَا وُجِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَعُدِمَ الْآخَرُ حَلَّ التَّفَاضُلُ وَحَرُمَ النَّسَاءُ
Chapter of Riba. He (al-Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him: Riba is prohibited in every measured and weighed [item] when sold with its kind with disparity, so the effective cause ('illa) in it is measurement with kind, or weight with kind. And when the measured or weighed [item] is sold with its kind equal for equal, the sale is permissible, and if they are disparate it is not permissible. And it is not permissible to sell the good quality for the poor quality from what contains riba except equal for equal. And when the two attributes are absent: the kind and the joined meaning, then disparity and delay are permissible. And when both are present, then disparity and delay are prohibited. And when one is present and the other absent, then disparity is permissible and delay is prohibited.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn establishes the foundational rules of riba in commercial transactions. The author begins by stating that riba is haram in all items that are sold by measure (makil) or weight (mawzun) when they are sold with their own genus (jins) and there is disparity (tafadul) in quantity. The underlying cause ('illa) for the prohibition is the combination of the genus (jins) and the trait of being measured or weighed. So for example, wheat sold for wheat: both are measured and same genus, so any excess is riba. If the items are sold equal for equal, it is permissible. Then al-Quduri gives a rule about quality: even if the quality differs (e.g., good dates for bad dates), sale is only allowed if equal in measure/weight, because the prohibition is on disparity, not quality. Then he introduces three scenarios based on two attributes: the genus and the 'joined meaning' (al-ma'na al-madhmum ilayh). The 'joined meaning' refers to the trait of being measured or weighed. The three possibilities: if both attributes are absent (different genus and not both measured/weighed), then both disparity and delay (nasi'ah) are permissible. If both are present (same genus and both measured/weighed), then both disparity and delay are prohibited. If only one is present (e.g., same genus but not both measured/weighed, or different genus but both measured/weighed), then disparity is permissible but delay is prohibited, because the genus difference allows disparity, but the measurement/weight similarity requires hand-to-hand exchange to prevent riba al-nasi'ah. This is a key Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الربا (al-ribā): Unlawful increase in exchange of same genus items or delay in such exchange.
المكيل (al-makīl): Items customarily sold by volume measure (e.g., grains, dates).
الموزون (al-mawzūn): Items customarily sold by weight (e.g., gold, silver, wheat).
الجنس (al-jins): Genus or species category (e.g., wheat is one jins, barley another).
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause behind a legal ruling, here the combination of genus and measurement/weight.
المعنى المضمو� إليه (al-ma'nā al-madhmūm ilayh): The joined attribute: for riba, it is the quality of being measured or weighed alongside the genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi matn, under which condition is both disparity (tafadul) and delay (nasi'ah) prohibited?
A) When both genus and the joined meaning (measurement/weight) are present
B) When both genus and the joined meaning are absent
C) When only genus is present
D) When only the joined meaning is present

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of riba in sales hinges on the combination of same genus and the property of being measured or weighed; the three scenarios dictate the permissibility of disparity and delay.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Exchanging Ribawi Items: The Three Scenarios
States the ruling on selling good for bad in ribawi items and the three conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for exchanging ribawi items and apply the Hanafi ruling on excess (tafadul) and deferment (nasaa).

Core Idea
When genus and effective cause align, both excess and deferment are haram; when one is absent, only deferment is haram.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn lays out the foundational rule for bartering ribawi commodities. It introduces two key attributes—genus (jins) and the effective cause ('illah, i.e., weight or measure)—and explains how their presence or absence determines whether excess (tafadul) and deferment (nasaa) are permissible. The hadith proofs illustrate the practical application of these rules, showing that the Prophet ﷺ prohibited unequal exchanges of dates and directed a workaround through cash.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline rule
Read the first sentence: 'It is not permissible to sell good for bad of what contains riba except like for like.' This establishes that when exchanging items of the same ribawi category, equality in quantity is required.
2
Learn the two attributes
Note the two attributes: genus (jins) – the category (e.g., dates, gold); and the attached meaning (al-ma'na al-madmum) – the effective cause, which for Hanafis is being measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun).
3
Map the three scenarios
The text presents three cases based on the presence (+) or absence (-) of these two attributes. (1) Both –: excess and deferment allowed. (2) Both +: both prohibited. (3) One +, one –: excess allowed, deferment prohibited.
Memorize this by making a simple table: rows: jins (same/diff), illa (same/diff); columns: tafadul, nasaa.
4
Examine the proofs for each scenario
The matn provides a hadith for each scenario: e.g., the hadith of Abu Huraira for the baseline rule, the hadith of Abd al-Rahman for exchanging different metals (different genus, same illa), and the hadith of Ubada and Jabir for mixed cases.
The proofs strengthen the authority of the ruling and show it is based on direct sunnah.
5
Understand the practical implication
Apply the rule: if you want to exchange high-quality dates for low-quality dates (same jins, same illa), you must do it in equal measure. To avoid violation, sell low-quality for cash then buy high-quality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الرِّبَا
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْجَيْدِ بِالرَّدِيءِ مِمَّا فِيهِ الرِّبَا إِلَّا مِثَلًا بِمِثْلِ هي وَإِذَا عُدِمَ الْوَصْفَانِ الْجِنْسُ، وَالْمَعْنَى الْمَضْمُومُ إِلَيْهِ حَلَّ التَّفَاضُلُ وَالنَّسَاءُ وَإِذَا وُجِدَا حَرُمَ التَّفَاضُلُ وَالنَّسَاءُ د وَإِذَا وُجِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَعُدِمَ الْآخَرُ حَلَّ التَّفَاضُلُ وَحَرُمَ النَّسَاءُ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْجَيِّدِ بِالرَّدِيءِ مِمَّا فِيهِ الرِّبَا إِلَّا مِثَلًا بِمِثْلٍ \ وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رضي الله عنهما : «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم اسْتَعْمَلَ رَجُلًا عَلَى خَيْبَرَ فَجَاءَهُ بِتَمْرٍ جَنِيبٍ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ : أَكُلُّ تَمْرِ خَيْبَرَ هَكَذَا، قَالَ: لَا وَاللهِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّا لَنَأْخُذُ الصَّاعَ مِنْ هَذَا بِالصَّاعَيْنِ، وَالصَّاعَيْنِ بِالثَّلَاثَةِ. فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ : لَا تَفْعَلْ بِعِ الجُمْعَ بِالدَّرَاهِم، ثُمَّ ابْتَعْ بِالدَّرَاهِم جَنِيبًا.» (بخاري شريف بَابٌ : إِذَا أَرَادَ بَيْعَ تَمْرِ بِتَمْرٍ خَيْرٍ مِنْهُ، نمبر 2201/مسلم شريف: بَاب بَيْعَ الطَّعَامِ مِثْلا يمثل نمبر 1593)
دوجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا عُدِمَ الْوَصْفَانِ الْجِنْسُ، وَالْمَعْنَى الْمَضْمُومُ إِلَيْهِ \ حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ أَبي بَكْرَةَ ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «نَهَى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ الْفِضَّةِ بِالْفِضَّةِ، وَالذَّهَبِ بِالذَّهَبِ، إِلَّا سَوَاءً بِسَوَاءٍ وَأَمَرَنَا أَنْ نَبْتَاعَ الذَّهَبَ بِالْفِضَّةِ كَيْفَ شِئْنَا، وَالْفِضَّةَ بِالذَّهَبِ كَيْفَ شِئْنَا . »» (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ بَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ يَدًا بِيَدِ، نمبر 2182)
توجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا وُجِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَعُدِمَ الْآخَرُ \ عَنْ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ الصَّامِتِ. قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الذهب بالذهب. فَإِذَا اخْتَلَفَتْ هَذِهِ الْأَصْنَافُ، فَبِيعُوا كَيْفَ شِئْتُمْ، إِذَا كَانَ يَدًا بِيَدِ)مسلم شريف: بَاب الصَّرْفِ وَبَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ نَقْدًا،نمبر1587/ سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الحِنْطَةَ بِالحِنْطَةِ مِثْلَا بِمِثْلِ وَكَرَاهِيَةَ التَّفَاضُلِ فِيهِ، نمبر 1240) وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا وُجِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَعُدِمَ الْآخَرُ | نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ دَيْنَا . » » بخاري شريف بَابٌ: بَيْعِ الْوَرِقِ بِالذَّهَبِ نَسِيئَةً، نمبر 2180)
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا وُجِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَعُدِمَ الْآخَرُ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ. قَالَ: جَاءَ عَبْدٌ فَبَايَعَ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى الْهِجْرَةِ. وَلَمْ يَشْعُرُ أَنَّهُ عَبْدٌ. فَجَاءَ سَيِّدُهُ يُرِيدُهُ. فَقَالَ لَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم (بِعْنِيهِ). فَاشْتَرَاهُ بِعَبْدَيْنِ أَسْوَدَيْنِ ( مسلم شريف: بَاب جَوَازِ بَيْعِ الْحَيَوَانِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ، مِنْ جِنْسِهِ، مُتَفَاضِلًا، ، نمبر 1602/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي شِرَاءِ العَبْدِ بِالعَبْدَيْنِ، نمبر 1239) اصول: حدیث میں جن اشیاء کو رہا کے قبیل سے ذکر کیا ہے ان میں عمدہ اور گھٹیا میں بھی تفریق نہ ہو گی۔
Chapter of Riba. It is not permissible to sell good quality for bad quality of what contains riba except like for like. When the two attributes (genus and the attached meaning) are absent, excess and deferment are allowed. When both are present, excess and deferment are prohibited. When one is present and the other absent, excess is allowed and deferment is prohibited. Evidence (1): Hadith for establishing 'It is not permissible to sell good for bad except like for like'... Evidence (1) for establishing 'When the two attributes are absent'... Evidence (1) for establishing 'When one is present and the other absent'...
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on riba. It outlines the fundamental rule for exchanging ribawi items (commodities subject to riba): when selling one quality for another of the same type, the exchange must be equal in quantity. The author then presents three scenarios based on the presence or absence of two attributes: 1) the genus (jins) of the item, and 2) the effective cause (ma'na) attached to it, which for ribawi items is either weight or measure. If both attributes are absent (meaning the items are of different genera and the effective cause does not apply), then excess and deferred payment are both permissible. If both are present (same genus and same effective cause), both excess and deferment are prohibited. If only one is present (e.g., same genus but different effective cause, or different genus but same effective cause), then excess is permissible but deferment is prohibited. The hadith proofs support each case: the hadith of Abu Huraira shows that selling high-quality dates for low-quality dates in unequal amounts is not allowed; instead, one should sell the low-quality dates for cash and then buy high-quality dates. The hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakra shows that gold and silver are subject to riba when exchanged hand-to-hand. The hadith of Ubada ibn al-Samit and others show that when species differ, the exchange is allowed hand-to-hand with any excess.

Key Terms
الرِّبَا (al-ribā): Usury or interest in exchanges, including riba al-fadl (excess in barter) and riba al-nasi'ah (deferment).
الْجِنْسُ (al-jins): The genus or category of a commodity (e.g., dates, wheat).
الْمَعْنَى الْمَضْمُومُ (al-ma'nā al-maḍmūm): The attached meaning, i.e., the effective cause ('illah) for riba: being measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun).
التَّفَاضُلُ (al-tafāḍul): Excess in quantity when exchanging two items of the same genus.
النَّسَاءُ (al-nasā'): Deferred payment or sale on credit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when exchanging dates for dates (same genus, same effective cause as both are measured), what is the ruling on selling 2 kg of high-quality dates for 1 kg of low-quality dates?
A) Permissible because quality differs.
B) Permissible if done hand-to-hand.
C) Not permissible because excess is prohibited when both genus and effective cause are present.
D) Not permissible because deferment is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Riba in barter depends on two attributes: if genus and effective cause are both present, excess and deferment are haram; if only one attribute is present, only deferment is haram.

Ribawi Items: Permanent Classification by Text
States that items declared ribawi by measure or weight remain so forever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ribawi items retain their original classification as measured or weighed regardless of changing customs, and apply it to common items like wheat and gold.

Core Idea
Ribawi items classified by text as measured or weighed remain so forever; only unmentioned items follow custom.

This passage establishes a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh for riba transactions: the classification of an item as measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) is determined by the original textual ruling of the Prophet, not by changing customs. Even if people later begin measuring or weighing differently, the original classification persists. This principle ensures consistency and prevents manipulation of riba rules through custom. For items not mentioned, we turn to local custom to decide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize that the Prophet explicitly forbade excess (tafaadul) in certain items by measure (kayl) and in others by weight (wazn). Items forbidden by measure are termed 'makil', and those forbidden by weight are termed 'mawzun'.
Examples: makil – wheat, barley, dates, salt; mawzun – gold, silver.
2
Grasp the permanence principle
The text uses the word 'abadan' (forever), indicating that this classification does not change even if people abandon the original method of measurement. Custom does not override the textual designation.
This is specific to the six ribawi items explicitly ruled upon.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Wheat remains makil even if sold by weight; gold remains mawzun even if counted by number. The ruling is based on the Prophet's prohibition, not on current practice.
4
Understand the custom rule for unmentioned items
For items not explicitly ruled upon by the Prophet, their classification (makil or mawzun) depends on the prevalent custom (ʿādāt al-nās) in that region.
Custom only applies when there is no textual ruling.
5
Connect to the proof
The hadith from Ibn Umar (Sunan Abi Dawud) states that the standard of weight is that of Mecca and the standard of measure is that of Medina, implying a fixed prophetic standard that does not change.
This hadith supports the permanence of classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ك وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ نَصَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ - صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - عَلَى تَحْرِيمِ التَّفَاضُلِ فِيهِ كَيْلًا فَهُوَ مَكِيلٌ أَبَدًا، وَإِنْ تَرَكَ النَّاسُ الْكَيْلَ فِيهِ مِثْلُ الْحِنْطَةِ وَالسَّعِيرِ وَالتَّمْرِ، وَالْمِلْحِ وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ نَصَّ عَلَى تَحْرِيمِهِ وَزْنًا فَهُوَ مَوْزُونٌ أَبَدًا، وَإِنْ تَرَكَ النَّاسُ الْوَزْنَ فِيهِ مِثْلُ الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ وَمَا لَمْ يَنُصَّ عَلَيْهِ فَهُوَ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى عَادَاتِ النَّاسِ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ نَصَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى تَحْرِيمِ التَّفَاضُلِ فِيهِ كَيْلًا عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الْوَزْنُ وَزْنُ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ، وَالْمِكْيَالُ مِكْيَالُ أَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ» (سنن ابوداود شریف بَابٌ فِي قَوْلِ النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمِكْيَالُ مِكْيَالُ الْمَدِينَةِ، غير 3340)
And everything that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) explicitly forbade excess in by measure is a measured item forever, even if people abandon measuring it, like wheat, barley, dates, and salt. And everything that he explicitly forbade excess in by weight is a weighed item forever, even if people abandon weighing it, like gold and silver. And what he did not explicitly rule on is carried on the customs of the people.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This ruling establishes that the classification of ribawi items is based on the original textual designation by the Prophet (peace be upon him), not on current practice. Wheat, barley, dates, and salt are measured items (makil) because the Prophet forbade excess in them by measure; gold and silver are weighed items (mawzun) because the prohibition was by weight. This designation is permanent: even if people later start selling wheat by weight or gold by number, the original ruling stands. For items not explicitly mentioned, we resort to local custom to determine if they are measured or weighed. The hadith of Ibn Umar, 'The weight is the weight of the people of Mecca, and the measure is the measure of the people of Medina,' indicates that the standard for weight and measure is based on the prophetic practice, and thus these remain the benchmarks.

Key Terms
مَكِيلٌ (makīl): Something that is measured by volume (e.g., bushels, liters).
مَوْزُونٌ (mawzūn): Something that is weighed (e.g., ounces, grams).
عَادَاتُ النَّاسِ (ʿādāt al-nās): Customs of the people regarding measurement or weighing for items not explicitly ruled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wheat that people now sell by weight instead of measure?
A) It is now considered a weighed item and riba rules for weighed items apply
B) It remains a measured item forever because the Prophet classified it as measured
C) It can be sold with excess because the people have changed the method
D) It is no longer subject to riba

Key Takeaway
The original textual classification of ribawi items as measured or weighed is permanent and cannot be changed by later custom.

Contract of Sarf Requires Hand-to-Hand Exchange
States the Hanafi ruling on sarf with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand-to-hand exchange in a sarf contract and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
In currency exchange, immediate hand-to-hand possession is wajib; delay makes it riba.

The Prophet ﷺ prohibited riba in exchanges of gold and silver unless it is hand-to-hand. The Hanafi school applies this to all currency exchanges, requiring immediate delivery in the same session. This lesson examines the ruling and its textual proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the first sentence: the contract of sarf (exchange of currencies) requires that both parties take possession (qabd) of the exchanged items in the same session (majlis). This is a condition for validity.
Sarf refers specifically to exchanging one currency for another (e.g., gold for silver, dollars for euros).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadiths: one from Umar ibn al-Khattab reporting the Prophet's words, and one from Ubada ibn al-Samit. Both emphasize immediate hand-to-hand exchange (haa wa haa) for gold and silver.
The hadiths are from Sahih Muslim, nos. 1586 and 1587.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'إلا هاء وهاء' (except hand-to-hand) indicates that the transaction is only permissible if both parties physically exchange the items on the spot. Any delay transforms the contract into riba.
The same phrase applies to other ribawi items, but the Hanafi interpretation limits immediate handover to currency exchange.
4
Distinguish from other ribawi items
The text says: for other riba-affected items (like wheat, barley, dates), only specification (ta'yin) of the item is required; immediate handover (taqabud) is not necessary. This means a delayed delivery is allowed as long as the items are specified and equal in quantity.
This is a key Hanafi nuance – not all ribawi transactions require spot exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَقْدُ الصَّرْفِ مَا وَقَعَ عَلَى جِنس الْأَثْمَانِ يُعْتَبَرُ قَبْضُهُ وَقَبْصُ عِوَضِهِ فِي الْمَجْلِسِ وَمَا سِوَاهُ مِمَّا فِيهِ الرِّبَا يُعْتَبَرُ فِيهِ التَّعْيِينُ وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ فِيهِ التَّقَابُضُ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَعَقْدُ الصَّرْفِ مَا وَقَعَ عَلَى جِنْسِ الْأَثْمَانِ فَقَالَ طَلْحَةُ بْنُ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ وَهُوَ عِنْدَ عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ : أَرنَا ذَهَبَكَ . ثُمَّ انْتِنَا إِذَا جَاءَ خَادِمُنَا، نُعْطِكَ وَرِقَكَ. فَقَالَ عُمَرُ بن الخطاب : .... فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ الْوَرِقُ بِالذَّهَبِ ربّا إِلَّا هَاءَ وَهَاءَ وَالْبُرُّ بِالْبُرَ رِبًا إِلَّا هَاءَ وَهَاءَ وَالشَّعِيرُ بِالشَّعِيرِ ربّا إِلَّا هَاءَ وَهَاءَ وَالتَّمْرُ بِالتَّمْرِ ربّا إِلَّا هاء وهاء) مسلم شريف: بَاب الصَّرْفِ وَبَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ نَقْدًا ، غمبر 1586)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَعَقْدُ الصَّرْفِ مَا وَقَعَ عَلَى جِنْسِ الْأَثْمَانِ فَبَلَغَ عُبَادَةَ بْنَ الصَّامِتِ فَقَامَ فَقَالَ: إِنِّي سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَنْهَى عَنْ بَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ بِالْفِضَّةِ والبر بالبر والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والملح بِالْمِلْحِ إِلَّا سَوَاءً بِسَوَاءِ. عَيْنًا بِعَيْنٍ( مسلم شريف: بَاب الصَّرْفِ وَبَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ نَقْدًا ،نمبر 1587)
And the contract of sarf concerning the category of currencies: its receipt and the receipt of its countervalue are required in the session. And other than that from what contains riba: specification is required, but hand-to-hand receipt is not required.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two types of ribawi transactions. For sarf (exchange of gold for silver or money for money), both parties must physically take possession of their respective amounts in the same meeting (majlis). This is because the Prophet said, 'Gold for silver is riba unless it is hand-to-hand (haa wa haa).' For other ribawi items (like wheat for dates), the requirement is specification (ta'yin) – i.e., identifying the specific items – but immediate hand-to-hand exchange is not required; a delay is allowed as long as the quantity is equal if the genus is the same. The hadiths of Umar and Ubada confirm the need for immediate exchange in sarf.

Key Terms
الصَّرْف (al-ṣarf): The exchange of one currency for another (e.g., gold for silver), or more generally, the exchange of ribawi items of different genera.
التَّعْيِينُ (al-taʿyīn): Specification of the item being sold, e.g., identifying a particular heap of wheat.
التَّقَابُضُ (al-taqābuḍ): Hand-to-hand receipt; both parties taking physical possession of the exchanged items on the spot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the requirement for a valid contract of sarf (currency exchange)?
A) Only specification of the items is needed
B) Both parties must take possession in the same session
C) The exchange must be equal in quantity but can be deferred
D) Only written documentation is required

Key Takeaway
For a valid sarf contract, both parties must hand over their currencies in the same session; delaying possession turns it into riba.

Prohibition of Selling Wheat for Flour or Sawiq: Riba Prevention via Date Analogy
Ruling with proof and usul notes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wheat for flour or sawiq and explain the analogy from the hadith that demonstrates the prohibition.

Core Idea
Selling wheat for its derivative is haram due to difference in form—like fresh dates for dried—ensuring no riba.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi fiqh regarding the exchange of wheat for its processed forms, such as flour or barley meal. The ruling is derived from a Prophetic analogy on dates. Understanding this solidifies the concept of riba in spot exchanges and highlights the school's caution against unequal exchanges within the same genus.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
Identify that selling wheat for flour or sawiq is prohibited (haram) in the Hanafi school because they are of the same genus (wheat derivatives) but differ in form, leading to potential inequality.
The prohibition is absolute unless the exchange falls under an exception like salam or involves different genera.
2
Trace the proof via analogy
The hadith on fresh and dry dates is used as the proof. The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited exchanging fresh dates for dry dates because fresh dates decrease when dried, making equality uncertain. By analogy, wheat and flour differ in form and volume, so the same prohibition applies.
The analogy is a clear qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on a shared illa: potential riba due to difference in form.
3
Recognize the usul principles
The commentary adds two principles: (1) if both the product and payment are weighed but differ in method and essence, excess is allowed (this applies to different genera); (2) if a measured item is sold by weight as a salam (advance) sale, it is permissible even with deferment.
These principles show the boundaries of the prohibition: it applies only within the same genus with different forms in spot exchanges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْحِنْطَةِ بِالدَّقِيقِ وَلَا بالسويق
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْحِنْطَةِ بِالدَّقِيقِ وَلَا بِالسَّوِيقِ \ وَقَالَ سَعْدٌ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم سُئِلَ عَمَّن اشْتَرَى التَّمْرَ بِالرُّطَبِ ، فَقَالَ: «أَيَنْقُصُ الرُّطَبُ إِذَا يَبِسَ؟» ، فَقَالُوا : نَعَمْ ، فَنَهَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ (سنن دار قطني ، باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر 2996)
اصول: مبیع اور شمن وزنی ہوں لیکن دونوں وزن کا طریقہ الگ ہو اور حقیقت بھی الگ ہو تو کمی بیشی جائز ہے۔ اصول: اگر کیلی چیز وزن کر کے بیع سلم کیا تو جائز ہے اور ادھار بھی جائز ہے۔
And it is not permissible to sell wheat for flour, nor for sawiq (barley meal). Evidence (1): Hadith for establishing 'It is not permissible to sell wheat for flour nor for sawiq': Sa'd said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) being asked about one who bought dates for ripe dates, and he said: 'Does the ripe date decrease when it dries?' They said: Yes. So he forbade that. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Buyu', no. 2996) Principle: If the sold item and the payment are weighed but the method of weighing is different and the reality is different, excess is allowed. Principle: If a measured item is sold by weight as a salam sale, it is permissible and deferment is also permissible.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This ruling prohibits selling wheat (a ribawi item measured by volume) for its derivative flour or sawiq (barley meal, but here considered similar) unless it is equal in measure and immediate. The hadith uses the analogy of fresh dates (rutab) and dry dates (tamr): since fresh dates shrink when dried, exchanging them by weight would involve uncertainty (gharar) and potential riba. Similarly, wheat and flour differ in form and weight per volume, so direct exchange is not allowed. The usul notes add two important principles: 1) If both the commodity and the payment are weighed but the weighing method differs and the essences differ, then excess is permissible (this applies to different genera). 2) If a measured item (makil) is sold by weight as a salam (advance payment) sale, it is permissible and even deferment is allowed because salam involves specified delivery in the future.

Key Terms
الدَّقِيق (al-daqīq): Flour, a derivative of wheat.
السَّوِيق (al-sawīq): Barley meal or a similar grain preparation.
بَيْعُ السَّلَم (bayʿ al-salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is selling wheat for flour prohibited?
A) Because flour is not a ribawi item
B) Because wheat and flour are of different genera
C) Because they differ in form, leading to potential inequality even if weight matches
D) Because flour cannot be measured

Key Takeaway
Selling wheat for its derivative is haram to prevent riba; the analogy of fresh and dry dates is the key proof.

Selling Fresh Dates for Dried Dates Equally
Permits selling fresh dates for dried dates in equal measures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging fresh and dried dates of the same genus and apply the condition of equality to avoid riba.

Core Idea
Equal exchange of same-genus produce is permitted; inequality is riba.

Fresh dates (rutab) and dried dates (tamr) are considered the same genus in Hanafi fiqh. Therefore, any exchange of them must be like-for-like in measure. The Prophet’s prohibition of an unequal exchange confirms that equality is the condition for permissibility. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and its application to similar pairs like grapes and raisins.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its condition
Identify the act (selling fresh dates for dried dates) and the ruling (jāʾiz, permissible) along with the condition (mithlan bi mithl, equal measure).
Equality is in volume or weight, not number.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith in Sunan Dar Qutni (no. 2996) and note its chain (ahad) and text.
The hadith was also used in a previous lesson for wheat/flour.
3
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the prohibition of an unequal transaction implies permissibility when equal. The Prophet asked whether fresh dates shrink when dried; when told yes, he forbade the exchange. Thus if they were equal, it would be allowed.
This is a mafhūm al-mukhālafah (counter-indicative implication).
4
Apply to analogous cases
The same principle applies to grapes (ʿinab) and raisins (rabīb) – they are the same genus, so exchange must be equal.
Other dried fruits like apricots and their fresh form follow similar rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الرُّطَبِ بِالتَّمْرِ مِثْلَا بِمِثْلِ وَكَذَلِكَ الْعِنَبُ بِالرَّبِيبِ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الرُّطَبِ بِالتَّمْرِ مِثْلا بِمِثْلِ 
وَقَالَ سَعْدٌ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ سُئِلَ عَمَّن اشْتَرَى التَّمْرَ بِالرُّطَب ، فَقَالَ: «أَيَنْقُصُ الرُّطَبُ إِذَا يَبِسَ؟» ، فَقَالُوا: نَعَمْ ، فَنَهَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ (سنن دار قطني باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر 2996)
And selling fresh dates for dried dates is permissible like for like (equal measure), and likewise grapes for raisins. Proof (1): the hadith to establish that: And Sa'd said: I heard the Messenger of Allah asked about one who bought dates for fresh dates. He said: 'Does the fresh date decrease when it dries?' They said: Yes. So he forbade that. (Sunan Dar Qutni, chapter on sales, no. 2996).
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This ruling permits the exchange of fresh dates (rutab) for dried dates (tamr) provided the measure is equal (mithlan bi mithl). Similarly, grapes and raisins. The hadith quoted is the same one used earlier to prohibit wheat for flour. Here, the author uses it to underscore that when exchange is equal, it is permissible, but if there is a known deficiency (like fresh dates drying), it becomes riba. Thus, the condition is strict equality of volume at the time of exchange.

Key Terms
الرُّطَبِ (ar-rutab): Fresh dates, moist.
الرَّبِيبِ (ar-rabīb): Raisins (dried grapes).
مِثْلًا بِمِثْلِ (mithlan bi mithl): Equal measure, like for like.
