Condition for Selling Olives for Oil: Avoiding Riba
Ruling on selling olives for oil with condition of excess.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition required for the validity of selling olives for oil and identify the intended proof.

Core Idea
When exchanging a ribawi item for its own genus, equality is required; any excess must be compensated by a different substance.

This lesson addresses a specific sale: exchanging olives (which contain oil) for olive oil. Since oil is a ribawi item (weighable and of the same genus), the Hanafi school imposes a condition to prevent riba: the oil exchanged must exceed the oil content of the seeds. The extra oil is considered payment for the pith (an-najira). This ruling is based on the principle of riba and analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling olives for oil (and sesame for sesame oil). The ruling: not permissible unless a condition is met.
The general rule is that exchanging like-for-like ribawi items requires equality.
2
Recognize the genus and riba issue
Olives and olive oil are considered same genus (jins) because the oil is extracted from the olives. Any excess in the oil exchanged over the oil in the seeds would be riba if not compensated.
The pith is a separate commodity.
3
Understand the condition
The oil exchanged must be greater than the oil contained in the seeds. Mathematically: if seeds contain X oil, you must give at least X+ something. The extra is payment for the pith.
This ensures the oil received equals the oil given and the extra is for non-ribawi item.
4
Evaluate the proof
The text cites a hadith forbidding meat for live animals. This hadith is not directly relevant; it may be a copying error. The actual ruling likely derives from qiyas on the prohibition of riba.
The hadith is from Dar Qutni via Yazid ibn Marwan, considered weak.
5
Apply the condition
In practice, to sell olives for oil, you must estimate or know that the oil given exceeds the oil in the olives. Otherwise, the contract is fasid.
This is a difficult condition, making such sales rare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الزَّيْتُونِ بِالزَّيْتِ وَالسَمْسِمِ بِالشَّيْرَجِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ الزَّيْتُ وَالشَّيْرَجُ أَكْثَرَ مِمَّا فِي الزَّيْتُونِ وَالسَّمْسِمِ فَيَكُونُ الدُّهْنُ مِثْلِهِ وَالزِّيَادَةُ بِالنَّجِيرَةِ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الزَّيْتُونِ بِالزَّيْتِ وَالسّمْسِمِ بِالشَّيْرَجِ 
عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ ، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ اللَّحْمِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ». تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ يَزِيدُ بْنُ مَرْوَانَ (سنن دار قطني، باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر 3056)
And it is not permissible to sell olives for oil, nor sesame for sesame oil, unless the oil (from the olives) and the sesame oil are more than what is in the olives and sesame, so that the oil equals (the oil in the seeds) and the excess is for the pith. Proof (1): the hadith to establish that: From Sahl ibn Sa'd, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade selling meat for live animals.' (Sunan Dar Qutni, no. 3056).
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This ruling addresses the sale of olives for olive oil and sesame for sesame oil. Since oil is a ribawi item (weighable) and the seeds contain oil, they are of the same genus. To avoid riba, the exchange must be such that the amount of oil in the seeds is less than the oil being exchanged, so that the oil received equals the oil in the seeds, and the excess oil is considered compensation for the pith (the solid part). This is a complex condition to ensure no riba. The hadith cited appears mistakenly connected; it is about meat for animals, not directly relevant. The ruling is based on qiyas and custom.

Key Terms
النَّجِيرَةِ (an-najīra): The pith or solid residue of the olive/sesame after pressing.
الشَّيْرَجِ (ash-shayraj): Sesame oil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The oil must be equal to the oil in the olives
B) The oil must be more than the oil in the olives
C) The olives must be dried
D) The exchange must be in cash

Key Takeaway
Selling olives for oil is only valid if the oil given exceeds the oil in the seeds, with the excess compensating the pith, thus avoiding riba.

Selling Different Meats with Excess is Permissible
Permits selling different types of meat with excess due to differing genera.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging different types of meat with excess and identify the principle that different meats are different genera for riba.

Core Idea
Different meats are different genera, so unequal exchange is permissible spot.

In fiqh al-buyu, one key question is whether different types of meat (e.g., beef, lamb, fish) are considered the same genus for riba purposes. The Hanafi school, supported by the practice of early scholars like Imam Malik, rules that they are different genera. Therefore, exchanging them with unequal quantities is permissible as long as the transaction is immediate (hand-to-hand). This lesson unpacks that ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling different meats (e.g., beef for lamb) with an excess in quantity. The ruling is permissible (mubah).
The ruling applies only when the meats are from different animal species.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is a statement from Imam Malik in his Muwatta, where he permits fish meat for beef, camel, sheep, etc., two for one or more, as long as it is hand-to-hand.
Although the source calls it 'qawl al-tabi',' Malik is a Tabi'i and his statement is authoritative in Hanafi fiqh as a reliable transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase is 'two for one' (اثنان بواحد) which demonstrates that excess is allowed. The condition 'hand-to-hand' (يدا بيد) excludes credit sales, which would introduce riba al-nasi'ah.
The underlying principle: riba prohibition requires both same genus and same measure; different genera break the genus condition.
4
Note the usul principle
The Urdu note says: 'different types, selling with excess is permissible.' This is a general usul: for ribawi items, if the 'illah (effective cause) of genus differs, excess is allowed.
The Hanafi school defines the 'illah for riba in food as being measurable by weight or volume and being a staple; meats of different animals are considered different genera.
5
Consider the condition
The permissibility is conditional on the transaction being spot (immediate exchange). If credit enters, it becomes invalid due to riba al-nasi'ah.
This condition is common across all schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعِ اللُّحْمَانِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ بَعْضِهَا بِبَعْضٍ مُتَفَاضِلًا
وجه: (1) قول التابع لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعِ اللُّحْمَانِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ بَعْضِهَا 
قَالَ مَالِكٌ: وَلَا بَأْسَ بِلَحْمِ الحِيتَانِ بِلَحْمِ الْبَقَرِ، وَالْإِبِلِ، وَالْغَنَمِ، وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذلِكَ مِنَ الْوُحُوشِ كُلَّهَا اثْنَانِ بِوَاحِدٍ، وَأَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذلِكَ يَداً بِيَدِ. فَإِنْ دَخَلَ ذلِكَ، الْأَجَلُ، فَلَا خَيْرَ فِيهِ، (مؤطا امام مالك، بَيْعُ اللَّحْمِ باللحم، نمبر 2419)
اصول: مختلف جنس ہوں تو کمی بیشی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے۔
And selling different meats, some for others, with excess is permissible. Proof (1): statement of a follower (Tabii) to establish it: Malik said: 'There is no harm in selling fish meat for beef, camel, sheep, and similar from wild animals, all of them, two for one, or more, hand to hand. But if credit enters into that, there is no good in it.' (Muwatta Imam Malik, chapter on selling meat for meat, no. 2419). Principle: If they are of different types, selling with excess is permissible.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This ruling states that different types of meat (e.g., beef, lamb, fish, poultry) are considered different genera for riba purposes. Therefore, they can be exchanged in unequal quantities (mutafadilan) as long as the transaction is hand-to-hand (spot). The quotation from Imam Malik supports this. The Urdu usul principle reiterates: when items are of different types, excess is permissible. This is because riba prohibition applies only within the same genus.

Key Terms
مُتَفَاضِلًا (mutafāḍilan): With excess; unequal quantities.
اللُّحْمَانِ (al-luḥmān): Meats (plural of lahm).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Different meats are different genera, so unequal exchange spot is permissible; credit invalidates the transaction.

Selling Meat for a Living Animal: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the ruling and intra-madhhab disagreement on exchanging meat for a live animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on selling meat for a living animal and explain the evidence and reasoning behind the intra-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit; Muhammad restricts — the same hadith is read differently.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the permissibility of exchanging meat (a food item) for a living animal. The disagreement turns on how to handle a prophetic prohibition and the role of transactional consideration (al-i'tibar). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to navigate ikhtilaf within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the majority Hanafi view
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: selling meat for a living animal is permissible.
They are the majority among the three imams.
2
Identify Imam Muhammad's objection
State that Muhammad only permits it on the basis of consideration (al-i'tibar), meaning the animal's value must be separately evaluated.
This is a stricter condition.
3
Examine the proof cited
The text presents a hadith prohibiting the sale of meat for a living animal. Note that it is a solitary narration (gharib) by Yazid ibn Marwan.
The hadith's weakness is key to understanding the Hanafi preference.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf likely considered the hadith weak (due to Yazid) or interpreted it as applying to a deferred exchange, not a spot transaction. Istihsan may also override the apparent prohibition.
The Hanafi school does not reject the hadith outright, but weighs it against other principles.
5
Determine the practical difference
The mufta bihi position is permissibility, but caution may follow Muhammad's view.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence of the disagreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الرِّبَا ١٠ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ اللَّحْمِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا عَلَى وَجْهِ الاعتبار وَجْه : (1) الْحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ اللَّحْمِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ ، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ اللَّحْمِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ». تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ يَزِيدُ بْنُ مَرْوَانَ (سنن دار قطني، باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر 3056)
Chapter of usury. 10. And the sale of meat for a living animal is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: It is not permissible except upon the basis of consideration. Evidence: (1) The hadith to prove that the sale of meat for a living animal is permissible according to Abu Hanifa: From Sahl ibn Sa'd, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prohibited the sale of meat for a living animal.' It was narrated only by Yazid ibn Marwan (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Transactions, number 3056).
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on exchanging meat (which is a food item) for a living animal (which is not food in the same sense). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit the transaction, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it unless it is done as a 'consideration transaction' (i.e., the animal is valued separately). The proof adduced is a hadith from Sahl ibn Sa'd that prohibits selling meat for a living animal, but the Hanafi position (represented here by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) may override this because the hadith is narrated only by Yazid ibn Marwan, who is considered weak by some, or because the prohibition is interpreted as directed at a specific type of transaction. The commentary does not elaborate further, but the inclusion of this hadith indicates the evidence used by the opponents of the permissibility ruling.

Key Terms
الاعتبار (al-i'tibar): Consideration; in this context, it means that the exchange is based on the value of the animal as a consideration, not as a direct barter of food for non-food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is absolutely permissible.
B) It is not permissible except on the basis of consideration.
C) It is prohibited in all cases.
D) It is permissible if the animal is sick.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of selling meat for a living animal in the Hanafi school rests on the weakness of the prohibitive hadith and the principle of istihsan.

Selling Different Types of Meat in Unequal Amounts
States the permissibility of exchanging different meats in unequal quantities, with evidence and condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging different types of meat in unequal quantities and identify the condition required for its validity.

Core Idea
Different meats are different species; only same-species foods trigger riba in exchange.

In this passage, Al-Quduri presents a permission: you may swap different meats in unequal amounts. The key is that they belong to different species. The evidence comes from the practice of early Muslims, allowing even two for one as long as the exchange is immediate (hand-to-hand). This ruling clarifies the boundary of riba in food exchanges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is selling or exchanging different types of meat in unequal quantities. The ruling stated is 'yajuz' (it is permissible). Determine the hukm level: mubah.
The permissibility is conditional, as we will see.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a narration from Imam Malik in the Muwatta, quoting a Tabi'i (or Imam Malik himself) stating: 'There is no harm in selling fish meat for beef, camel, sheep, and similar game animals, two for one or more than that hand to hand. If credit enters, then there is no good in it.' Identify the source and type of proof.
This is a qawl sahabi or qawl tabi'i, used as supporting evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The phrase 'la ba'sa' indicates permissibility. The explicit permission to exchange two for one (unequal) shows that inequality is allowed. The condition 'hand to hand' (spot) is crucial; credit would ruin the transaction.
The absence of the word 'riba' implies that riba is not a concern across species.
4
Note the condition and its significance
The passage explicitly states that if credit enters, it is not good. Thus, the permissibility hinges on immediate exchange. Understand why credit is problematic: deferring the exchange could involve uncertainty or resemble riba even between different species.
This condition applies to all exchanges of ribawi items, even across species.
5
Apply the usul principle
The underlying principle is that riba (usury) only applies within the same genus (jins) of weight or volume-measured food items. Different meats are considered different species, so inequality is allowed. Confirm this with the Urdu summary: 'mukhtalif jins hon to kami beshi ke saath bechna jaiz hai'.
This principle governs many transactions in Islamic commercial law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعِ اللُّحْمَانِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ بَعْضِهَا بِبَعْضٍ مُتَفَاضِلًا وَجْه: (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِ لِثُبُوت وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعِ اللُّحْمَانِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ بَعْضِهَا قَالَ مَالِكٌ: وَلَا بَأْسَ بِلَحْمِ الحِيتَانِ بِلَحْمِ الْبَقَرِ، وَالْإِبِلِ، وَالْغَنَمِ، وَمَا أَشْبَهَ ذلِكَ مِنَ الْوُحُوشِ كُلَّهَا اثْنَانِ بِوَاحِدٍ، وَأَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذلِكَ يَداً بِيَدِ. فَإِنْ دَخَلَ ذلِكَ، الْأَجَلُ، فَلَا خَيْرَ فِيهِ، (مؤطا امام مالك، بَيْعُ اللَّحْمِ باللحم، نمبر 2419) أُصُول: مختلف جنس ہوں تو کمی بیشی کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے۔
And the sale of different types of meat, some in exchange for others, is permissible in unequal amounts. Evidence: (1) The saying of a Tabi'i to prove that it is permissible to sell different types of meat: Malik said: There is no harm in selling fish meat for beef, camel, sheep, and similar game animals, two for one or more than that hand to hand. If credit enters into that, then there is no good in it. (Muwatta Imam Malik, Sale of Meat for Meat, number 2419). Principle: If they are of different species, then selling with excess or deficiency is permissible.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage rules that selling different types of meat (e.g., fish, beef, lamb) in unequal quantities is permissible because they are different species (jins). The evidence is from Imam Malik's Muwatta, citing the opinion of a Tabi'i (or Imam Malik himself) that such exchange is allowed hand-to-hand, even if two for one. The key condition is that the exchange must be spot (hand-to-hand); if credit is introduced, it becomes invalid. The Urdu principle at the end summarizes: when the species differ, exchanging in unequal amounts is permissible. This is consistent with the Hanafi view that riba only applies within the same genus of food items.

Key Terms
مُتَفَاضِلًا (mutafādilan): Unequally; one exceeding the other in quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition is necessary for exchanging different meats in unequal amounts?
A) The meats must be from the same animal.
B) The exchange must be hand-to-hand (spot).
C) The quantities must be equal.
D) The meats must be cooked.

Key Takeaway
Selling different types of meat in unequal amounts is permissible as long as the exchange is immediate; the meats are considered different species, so riba does not apply.

Selling Milk of Different Animals and Bread for Wheat or Flour
Extends the ruling of different meats to milk of different animals and bread for wheat/flour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school permits the sale of bread for wheat in unequal amounts and apply the principle of genus difference to similar transactions.

Core Idea
Milk from different animals and bread versus wheat are different genera, so unequal exchange is permitted.

In the previous lesson, you learned that different meats can be exchanged in unequal amounts. This lesson extends that principle to two new cases: milk from cows and sheep, and bread exchanged for wheat or flour. The proof is a hadith that allows exchanging barley for dates however one wishes. The key is that these items belong to different species or are processed differently, so riba rules of equality do not apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two new cases
The passage introduces two scenarios: exchanging milk from different animals (cows and sheep) and selling bread for wheat or flour. Note that these are extensions of the previous principle for different meats.
2
Recognize the underlying principle: genus difference
The permissibility of disparity (tafadul) hinges on the items being from different genera (jins). In Hanafi fiqh, if items are of the same genus and both are ribawi (food or currency), equality is required; if different genera, disparity is allowed.
Milk from cows and sheep are considered different species. Bread is considered a different genus from wheat because processing changes its nature.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit quotes the Prophet (peace be upon him) allowing the sale of barley for dates 'however you wish, hand to hand.' Barley and dates are different genera, so disparity is permitted. The same logic applies to the cases at hand.
The hadith is narrated in Sunan al-Tirmidhi (1240). The phrase 'however you wish' indicates permissibility of disparity.
4
Note the condition of hand-to-hand delivery
Even when disparity is allowed, the exchange must be conducted hand-to-hand (yadan bi-yad). Deferred payment or credit would introduce riba, as the items are still ribawi (food).
The hadith explicitly mentions 'yadan bi-yad' (hand to hand).
5
Understand why bread is different from wheat
In Hanafi fiqh, bread (khubz) is considered a different genus from wheat (hintah) or flour (daqeeq) because the processing (baking) transforms it into a new substance. Thus, they are treated as different ribawi items, allowing unequal exchange.
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider them the same genus, requiring equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ كَذَلِكَ أَلْبَانُ الْبَقَرِ، وَالْغَنَمِ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَبْزِ بِالْحِنْطَةِ وَالدَّقِيقِ مُتَفَاضِلًا وَجْه : (۱) الْحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَكَذَلِكَ أَلْبَانُ الْبَقَرِ ، وَالْغَنَمِ عَنْ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ الصَّامِتِ...... وَبِيعُوا الشَّعِيرَ بِالتَّمْرِ كَيْفَ شِئْتُمْ يَدًا بِيَدِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الْحِنْطَةَ بِالحِنْطَةِ مِثَلًا بِمِثْلٍ وَكَرَاهِيَةَ التَّفَاضُل فِيهِ، نمبر (1240)
And similarly, the milk of cows and sheep (are treated the same), and the sale of bread for wheat and flour is permissible in unequal amounts. Evidence: (1) The hadith to prove the same for milk of cows and sheep: From Ubadah ibn al-Samit... 'And sell barley for dates however you wish, hand to hand.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Chapter: What has come about wheat for wheat like for like and the disapproval of excess in it, number 1240)
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage extends the previous principle to two additional cases: first, milk of different animals (cows and sheep) can be exchanged in unequal amounts because they are different species; second, bread (khubz) can be sold for wheat (hintah) or flour (daqeeq) in unequal amounts. The proof is a hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit where the Prophet (peace be upon him) allowed selling barley for dates however one wishes hand-to-hand. This indicates that different food items (different genera) can be exchanged with disparity. The Hanafi school analogizes: since wheat and bread are different (one is processed, the other is raw), they are considered different species for riba purposes. Similarly, milk from different animals are different species. The condition of hand-to-hand exchange remains.

Key Terms
الْخَبْزُ (al-khubz): Bread; here considered a processed food item distinct from its raw ingredients (wheat, flour).
تَفَاضُل (tafadul): Disparity; exchanging unequal amounts of two items.
يَدًا بِيَدٍ (yadan bi-yad): Hand-to-hand; immediate exchange without delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how can bread be sold for wheat?
A) Only in equal amounts.
B) In unequal amounts.
C) Only if credit is given.
D) Only if both are measured by weight.

Key Takeaway
Different genera allow unequal exchange; bread and wheat are different genera in Hanafi fiqh.

No Riba Between Master and Slave or Between Muslim and Harbi in Dar al-Harb
States the absence of riba in certain relationships and contexts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two exceptional contexts where riba does not apply in Hanafi fiqh and identify the proofs (qawl sahabi, hadith, ayah) that support each exception.

Core Idea
Riba applies only between free Muslims in Dar al-Islam; master-slave and Muslim-harbi in Dar al-Harb are exceptions.

The Hanafi school recognizes that the prohibition of riba is not absolute in all circumstances. This passage explores two specific exceptions: transactions between a master and his slave, and between a Muslim and a harbi (non-Muslim enemy) in Dar al-Harb. The author cites multiple proofs from the Quran, Hadith, and Companion practice to justify these exceptions, grounding them in the principle that riba is only prohibited when parties are fully independent and subject to Islamic jurisdiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Exceptional Contexts
Read the opening statement: 'لا ربا بين المولى وعبد ولا بين المسلم والحربي في دار الحرب'. Note that the exception applies to (1) master-slave relationship and (2) Muslim-harbi transaction in Dar al-Harb.
The exception does not apply to other relationships like Muslim-Muslim in Dar al-Islam.
2
Examine the First Proof (Qawl Sahabi)
The author cites the practice of Ibn Abbas, who sold fruit before ripening to his slave. Recognize this as a qawl sahabi, a Hanafi source of law. Ask: How does selling unripe fruit to a slave demonstrate no riba?
Ibn Abbas explicitly said 'ليس بين العبد وسيده ربا'.
3
Analyze the Second Proof (Hadith from Makhul)
The hadith states 'لا ربا بين أهل الحرب'. Note the author's uncertainty about the exact wording. This hadith directly supports the exception for harbis.
The chain includes Makhul, a tabi'i; the hadith is mursal, but used as evidence.
4
Consider the Third Proof (Quranic Verse 2:278)
The verse commands believers to abandon riba. Hanafis argue that 'believers' here refers to Muslims in Dar al-Islam, implying that the prohibition is limited to that context.
The verse is general, but Hanafis apply it specifically through the other proofs.
5
Understand the Fourth Proof (Hadith of Jabir)
The hadith from the Farewell Pilgrimage abolishes riba of the Jahiliyyah, starting with Abbas's riba. This shows that riba prohibition was addressed to Muslims, not to transactions with non-Muslims or slaves.
This hadith emphasizes the Islamic legal context.
6
Synthesize the Underlying Principles
The Urdu principles explain the rationale: if property belongs to the same entity (master-slave), riba cannot exist; and if two items are the same in essence but differ in name/benefit, they can be treated as separate types, avoiding riba.
These principles derive from the concept of legal capacity (ahliyyah) and jurisdiction (dar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ، وَالْحَرْبِيِّ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَجْه : (1) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوت وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ كَانَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ يَبِيعُ عَبْدًا لَهُ الثَّمَرَةَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَبْدُوَ صَلَاحُهَا، وَكَانَ يَقُولُ: «لَيْسَ بَيْنَ الْعَبْدِ وَسَيِّدِهِ رَبَّا» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ : لَيْسَ بَيْنَ عَبْدِ وَسَيّدِهِ، وَالْمُكَاتِبِ وَسَيِّدِهِ رِبًا ، نمبر 14378/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ: لَيْسَ بَيْنَ الْعَبْدِ وَسَيِّدِهِ رِبًا، نمبر 20042) وَجْه: ((۲) الْحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ عَنْ مَكْحُولٍ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «لَا رِبَا بَيْنَ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ». وَأَظُنُّهُ قَالَ : « وَأَهْلِ الْإِسْلَامِ» (فتح باب العناية بشرح النقاية، (لا ربا بين مسلم وحربي في دار الحرب)، ص نمبر 367) وَجْه: (3) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوت وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آَمَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَذَرُوا مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ الرِّبَا إِنْ كُنْتُمْ مُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2 آیت نمبر 278) وَجْه : (4) الْحَدِيث لِثُبُوت وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ قَالَ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ. فَسَأَلَ عَنِ الْقَوْمِ ...... وَرِبَا الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ مَوْضُوع. وَأَوَّلُ رِبًا أَضَعُ رِبَانَا رِبَا عَبَّاسِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِبِ. فَإِنَّهُ مَوْضُوع (مسلم شریف: بَاب حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، نمبر1218/سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، نمبر 1905) أُصُول: اصل اور حقیقت کے اعتبار سے ایک ہوں لیکن نام اور منافع میں ہو تو اس کو الگ الگ شمار کیا جائے گا۔ أُصُول: کسی بھی اعتبار سے اپنا ہی مال ہو تو سود متحقق نہیں ہو گا۔
And there is no riba between a master and his slave, nor between a Muslim and a harbi in the land of war. Evidence: (1) The saying of a Companion to prove that there is no riba between a master and his slave: Ibn Abbas used to sell a slave of his the fruit before it ripened, and he used to say: 'There is no riba between a slave and his master.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab: There is no riba between a slave and his master... number 14378; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, number 20042) Evidence: (2) The hadith to prove that there is no riba between a master and his slave and between a Muslim... From Makhul from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he said: 'There is no riba between the people of war.' And I think he said: 'and the people of Islam.' (Fath Bab al-Inayah fi Sharh al-Nuqayah, page 367) Evidence: (3) The verse to prove that there is no riba between a master and his slave and between a Muslim: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah and give up what remains [due to you] of interest, if you should be believers.' (Surah al-Baqarah, verse 278) Evidence: (4) The hadith to prove that there is no riba between a master and his slave and between a Muslim: He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah. He asked about the people... and the riba of the Jahiliyyah is abolished. The first riba I abolish is the riba of Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib; indeed it is abolished. (Sahih Muslim: Chapter of the Farewell Pilgrimage, number 1218; Sunan Abi Dawud, number 1905) Principles: If they are the same in origin and reality but differ in name and benefit, they will be considered separate. Principle: In any respect, if it is one's own property, riba is not actualized.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage addresses two exceptional contexts where riba (usury) does not apply: (1) between a master and his slave, and (2) between a Muslim and a harbi (non-Muslim enemy) in the land of war (Dar al-Harb). The Hanafi school holds that the prohibition of riba applies only when the parties are free and Muslim, and the transaction is in Dar al-Islam. The proofs include: the practice of Ibn Abbas (qawl sahabi) who would sell fruit before ripening to his slave, saying there is no riba between them; a hadith from Makhul stating no riba between the people of war; the general Quranic verse commanding believers to abandon riba (implying it addresses Muslims in Dar al-Islam); and the hadith from Jabir about abolishing riba in the Farewell Pilgrimage, which focuses on Muslim transactions. The Urdu principles at the end explain the rationale: when two items are the same in origin and reality but differ in name or benefit, they can be considered separate types; and when property belongs to the same entity (like master and slave), riba cannot exist because the slave's property ultimately belongs to the master.

Key Terms
الْحَرْبِيُّ (al-harbi): A non-Muslim with whom Muslims are in a state of war, residing in Dar al-Harb.
دَارُ الْحَرْبِ (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control and not under Islamic rule, usually in a state of war with Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Between two Muslims in Dar al-Islam.

C) Between a Muslim and a dhimmi in Dar al-Islam.
D) Between two free Muslims in Dar al-Harb.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, riba is not prohibited in transactions between a master and his slave or between a Muslim and a harbi in Dar al-Harb, due to lack of full legal capacity and jurisdiction.

Exceptions to Riba: Master-Slave and Dar al-Harb
States rulings on riba exceptions with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no riba exists between a master and his slave or between a Muslim and a harbi in dar al-harb, and identify the proofs (hadith, qawl sahabi, Quran) that support this exception.

Core Idea
No riba when one party owns the other or when transacting with an enemy in hostile territory.

The prohibition of riba is a cornerstone of Islamic finance, but it is not absolute. The Hanafi school recognizes specific contexts where the rationale for riba disappears. This lesson examines two such exceptions: transactions between a master and his slave, and between a Muslim and a harbi (enemy combatant) in enemy territory. We will explore the textual proofs that ground these rulings, including hadith, the practice of a Companion, and the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings
Locate the three distinct rulings in the matn: (1) the permissibility of selling bread for wheat or flour in excess, (2) no riba between master and slave, (3) no riba between Muslim and harbi in dar al-harb.
The first ruling (bread for wheat/flour) is peripheral; focus on the two exceptions.
2
Analyse the proofs for 'no riba between master and slave'
The text cites the action and saying of Ibn Abbas (qawl sahabi) and a hadith from Makhul. Understand how these proofs establish the exception.
Ibn Abbas used to sell fruit from a slave's tree before it ripened, indicating no riba.
3
Analyse the proofs for 'no riba in dar al-harb'
The text cites a hadith related by Makhul: 'No riba between the people of war.' This is supported by the general principle from Quran 2:278 and the Farewell Sermon where riba was abolished.
The hadith from Makhul is recorded in Fath Bab al-'Inayah.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The Urdu principle at the end states: 'If it is one's own property in any respect, riba is not actualized.' This explains the master-slave case (slave's property ultimately belongs to master). For dar al-harb, the lack of enforcement of Islamic law removes the riba prohibition.
The principle of ownership and authority underpins the exceptions.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that riba applies in all cases, including master-slave and dar al-harb. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in transactions.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions have strong proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الرِّبَا
وَكَذَلِكَ أَلْبَانُ الْبَقَرِ، وَالْغَنَمِ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَبْزِ بِالْحِنْطَةِ وَالدَّقِيقِ مُتَفَاضِلًا ۱۵ وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ وَالْحَرْبِيِّ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ
وَجْه : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَكَذَلِكَ أَلْبَانُ الْبَقَرِ، وَالْغَنَمِ اعَنْ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ الصَّامِتِ...... وَبِيعُوا الشَّعِيرَ بِالتَّمْرِ كَيْفَ شِئْتُمْ يَدًا بِيَدِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الْحِنْطَةَ بِالحِنْطَةِ مِثَلًا بِمِثْلٍ وَكَرَاهِيَةَ التَّفَاضُل فِيهِ، نمبر (1240)
وَجْه : (۱) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ كَانَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ يَبِيعُ عَبْدًا لَهُ الثَّمَرَةَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَبْدُوَ صَلَاحُهَا، وَكَانَ يَقُولُ: «لَيْسَ بَيْنَ الْعَبْدِ وَسَيِّدِهِ رَبَّا» (مصنف عبد الرزاق بَابٌ : لَيْسَ بَيْنَ عَبْدِ وَسَيّدِهِ، وَالْمُكَاتِبِ وَسَيِّدِهِ رِبًا ، نمبر 14378/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ: لَيْسَ بَيْنَ الْعَبْدِ وَسَيِّدِهِ رِبًا، نمبر 20042)
وَجْه: ((۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ اعن مكحول عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «لا ربا بين أهل الحرب». وأظنه قال : « وأهل الإسلام فتح باب العناية بشرح النقاية،(لا ربا بين مسلم وحربي في دار الحرب)، ص نمبر 367)
وَجْه: (3) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ اليَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَذَرُوا مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ الرِّبَوا إِن كُنتُم مُّؤْمِنِينَ﴾(سورة البقرة، 2 أيت نمبر 278)
وَجْه : (۴) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا رِبَا بَيْنَ الْمَوْلَى وَعَبْدِهِ وَلَا بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِ أَقَالَ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ. فَسَأَلَ عَنِ الْقَوْمِ ...... وَرِبَا الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ مَوْضُوع. وَأَوَّلُ رِبًا أَضَعُ رِبَانَا رِبَا عَبَّاسِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِبِ. فَإِنَّهُ مَوْضُوع مسلم شریف: بَاب حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، نمبر1218/سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، نمبر 1905)
اصول: اصل اور حقیقت کے اعتبار سے ایک ہوں لیکن نام اور منافع میں ہو تو اس کو الگ الگ شمار کیا جائے گا۔ اصول: کسی بھی اعتبار سے اپنا ہی مال ہو تو سود متحقق نہیں ہو گا۔
Chapter of Riba. And likewise the milk of cows and sheep. And it is permissible to sell bread for wheat and flour in excess. And no riba between a master and his slave, nor between a Muslim and a harbi in dar al-harb. Proof (1): The hadith for the establishment of 'and likewise the milk of cows and sheep': from 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit... 'and sell barley for dates as you wish hand to hand.' Proof (1): The saying of a companion for the establishment of 'and no riba between a master and his slave and between a Muslim': Ibn 'Abbas used to sell fruit of a slave he owned before it ripen and he said: 'There is no riba between a slave and his master.' Proof (2): The hadith for the establishment of 'and no riba between a master and his slave and between a Muslim': from Makhul from the Messenger of Allah that he said: 'No riba between the people of war.' And I think he said: 'and the people of Islam.' (Fath Bab al-'Inayah) Proof (3): The verse for the establishment of... 'O you who believe, fear Allah and leave what remains of riba if you are believers.' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:278) Proof (4): The hadith for the establishment of... He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn 'Abdillah... and the riba of Jahiliyyah is abolished. And the first riba I abolish is our riba, the riba of 'Abbas ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib, for it is abolished. (Muslim, Abi Dawud) Principle: If they are one in origin and reality but differ in name and benefit, they are considered separate. Principle: If it is one's own property in any respect, riba is not actualized.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri presents multiple rulings on riba. First, the ruling that milk from cows and sheep (considered food items) follow the same riba rules as their source grains? Actually the text says 'and likewise the milk of cows and sheep' meaning the same rule applies to milk as to the animals' other products? The second ruling permits selling bread for wheat or flour even if unequal, because bread is a different commodity. The third major ruling states that there is no riba between a master and his slave, and between a Muslim and a non-Muslim (harbi) in dar al-harb (enemy territory). The proofs provided include hadith from 'Ubadah, the practice of Ibn 'Abbas, a hadith from Makhul, Quran 2:278, and the Farewell Sermon. The Urdu principles at the end clarify that if property is essentially one's own, riba does not apply.

Key Terms
الرِّبَا (al-ribā): Unlawful increase in exchange transactions, specifically in certain commodities (ribawi items) or deferred payment.
الْمَوْلَى (al-mawlā): Master, owner of a slave.
دَارِ الْحَرْبِ (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim control with which Muslims are in a state of war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is there no riba between a Muslim and a non-Muslim?
A) When the non-Muslim is a dhimmi in dar al-Islam
B) When the Muslim is a slave
C) When the non-Muslim is a harbi in dar al-harb
D) Never, riba applies to all transactions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts master-slave and harbi transactions from riba due to ownership unity and territorial jurisdiction.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Salam Contract: Permissibility in Standardized Goods, Prohibition in Animals
Defines salam contract, its permissibility in measurable items, and prohibition in animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a valid salam contract and identify which types of goods are excluded, with supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Salam is valid only for goods that can be standardized by measure, weight, or count; animals are excluded due to uncertainty.

The salam contract allows a buyer to pay now for goods to be delivered later, providing liquidity and price stability. However, not all goods qualify. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on permissible and prohibited subjects of salam, supported by textual proofs, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the first sentence: 'Salam is permissible in measurable items, weighable items, and countable items that do not vary.' This is the core ruling. Note the categories and the exclusion of animals.
The author explicitly lists permissible categories and the prohibited category.
2
Analyze the conditions implied by the hadith
The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas requires a known measure, known weight, and known term. These are essential conditions for salam. Consider why these remove uncertainty (gharar).
The conditions are derived from the Sunnah, not explicitly stated in the matn.
3
Examine the proofs for permissibility
Three proofs are cited: Quran 2:282 (general permission for deferred contracts), the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas (specific conditions), and the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr (a practical precedent). Understand the wajh al-dalalah of each.
The Quranic verse is general; the hadith specifies the conditions.
4
Investigate the prohibition in animals
The author cites the hadith of Samurah forbidding the sale of animal for animal on credit. This is used as proof that salam in animals is invalid. How does this hadith apply?
The prohibition is based on the risk of gharar (uncertainty) due to variation in animals.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab dispute
The text mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i uses the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr to argue that salam in animals is permissible. How does the Hanafi school respond? Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The dispute hinges on whether the need for standardization overrides the general permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ السَّلَمِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - : 1- السَّلَمُ جَائِزٌ فِي الْمَكِيلَاتِ، وَالْمَوْزُونَاتِ وَالْمَعْدُودَاتِ الَّتِي لَا تَتَفَاوَتُ كَالْجُوْزِ، وَالْبَيْضِ وَالْمَزْرُوعَاتِ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَلَا فِي أَطْرَافِهِ وَلَا فِي الْجُلُودِ عَدَدًا
وَجْه: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ السَّلَمُ جَائِزٌ فِي الْمَكِيلَاتِ وَالْمَوْزُونَاتِ يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا تَدَايَنتُم بِدَيْنِ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مُسَمًّى فَاكْتُبُوهُ (سورة البقرة، 2 أيت نمبر 282)
وَجْه (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ السَّلَمُ جَائِزٌ فِي الْمَكِيلَاتِ، وَالْمَوْزُونَاتِ أَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمَدِينَةَ وَهُمْ يُسْلِفُونَ بِالتَّمْرِ السَّنَتَيْنِ وَالثَّلَاثَ، فَقَالَ: مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلٍ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ» (بخاري شريف بَابُ السَّلَم فِي وَزْنٍ مَعْلُومٍ، نمبر 2240/مسلم شریف: باب السلم،نمبر 1604)
وَجْه : (۳) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ السَّلَمُ جَائِزٌ فِي الْمَكِيلَاتِ، وَالْمَوْزُونَاتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو: «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يُجَهِزَ جَيْشًا فَنَفِدَتْ الإِبلُ فَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ فِي قِلَاصِ الصَّدَقَةِ»، فَكَانَ يَأْخُذُ الْبَعِيرَ بِالْبَعِيرَيْنِ إِلَى إِبِلِ الصَّدَقَةِ (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الرُّخْصَةِ فِي ذَلِكَ، 3357/)
وَجْه: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَلَا فِي أَطْرَافِهِ عَنْ سَمُرَةَ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ بَيْعِ الْحَيَوَانِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ نَسِيئَةً (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ بَيْعِ الْحَيَوَانِ بِالحَيَوَانِ نَسِيئَةً، نمبر 1218/سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ نَسِيئَةً، نمبر 3356)
وَجْه (۱) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَلَا فِي أَطْرَافِهِ أَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو: «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يُجَهِزَ جَيْشًا فَنَفِدَتْ الْإِبِلُ فَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ فِي قِلَاصٍ الصَّدَقَةِ»، فَكَانَ يَأْخُذُ الْبَعِيرَ بِالْبَعِيرَيْنِ إِلَى إِبِلِ الصَّدَقَةِ (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الرُّحْصَةِ فِي ذَلِكَ، نمبر 3357)
اصول: قیمت ابھی لے لے اور مبیع کچھ دن بعد لے تو یہ بیع سلم کہلاتا ہے۔ اصول : بیع سلم جائز ہے میلات، موزونات، مزروعات، معدودت اور ان میں جن کے صفات اور صنعت من کرنے سے چیزیں متعین ہوتی ہیں۔
Chapter of Salam. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him: Salam is permissible in measurable items, weighable items, and countable items that do not vary, like walnuts, eggs, and crops. And salam is not permissible in animals, nor in their parts, nor in skins by count. Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of 'salam is permissible in measurable and weighable items': 'O you who believe, when you contract a debt for a specified term, write it down.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:282) Proof (2): The hadith for the establishment of 'salam is permissible in measurable and weighable items': from Ibn 'Abbas who said: 'The Prophet came to Medina and they were paying in advance for dates for two or three years. He said: Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be for a known measure, a known weight, and a known term.' (Bukhari, Muslim) Proof (3): The hadith for the establishment of 'salam is permissible in measurable and weighable items': from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr that the Messenger of Allah ordered him to equip an army, and the camels were exhausted, so he ordered him to take from the camels of sadaqah, and he would take one camel for two camels to be paid from the sadaqah camels. (Abu Dawud) Proof (1) [for prohibition]: The hadith for the establishment of 'salam is not permissible in animals nor in their parts': from Samurah that the Prophet forbade the sale of animal for animal on credit. (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) Proof (1) [another]: The proof of al-Shafi'i is the hadith for the establishment of... [same hadith as above]. Principle: If one takes the price now and takes the goods later, this is called bay' salam. Principle: Bay' salam is permissible for measurable, weighable, cultivable, countable items, and those that can be determined by description and specification.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri defines the salam contract (forward sale). The author states that salam is valid for items that can be measured (makilat), weighed (mawzunat), and counted (ma'dudat) provided they do not vary significantly, e.g., walnuts, eggs, and crops. This is because such items can be precisely described and thus do not lead to uncertainty. Salam is not valid for animals, their body parts, or skins by count, due to the prohibition of deferred sale of animals (bai' al-hayawan bi al-hayawan nasiah). The proofs include Quran 2:282 (general permission for deferred contracts), the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas specifying known measure/weight/term, and the hadith of Samurah forbidding animal-for-animal credit sales. An additional hadith from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr is cited, which Imam al-Shafi'i uses to argue against salam in animals, but the Hanafi interpretation distinguishes between the specific permission for salam in measurable items and the general prohibition of deferred animal sales.

Key Terms
السَّلَم (al-salam): A forward sale where the price is paid immediately for a commodity to be delivered at a future date.
الْمَكِيلَاتُ (al-makīlāt): Items that are customarily sold by measure (e.g., grains).
الْمَوْزُونَاتُ (al-mawzūnāt): Items customarily sold by weight (e.g., precious metals, spices).
الْمَعْدُودَاتُ (al-ma'dūdāt): Items customarily sold by count (e.g., eggs, nuts).
الْحَيَوَان (al-ḥayawān): Animals; prohibited as subject of salam.
نَسِيئَة (nasī'ah): Credit sale; deferred payment or delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A specific cow to be delivered in two months
B) 100 kg of dates to be delivered after harvest
C) The skin of a goat counted by number (10 goat skins)
D) A share in a herd of camels without specifying which

Key Takeaway
Salam is a specialized contract valid only for standardized goods; animals and their parts are excluded due to the risk of uncertainty (gharar).

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Salam Sale: Permissible Items and Prohibited Animals
States permissibility and prohibition of salam with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on salam in measurable, weighable, and countable items versus animals, and identify the proofs used to support the ruling.

Core Idea
Salam is valid only when the subject matter is precisely describable — animals are excluded because individual variation creates gharar.

In this passage from al-Quduri, we learn the Hanafi position on salam (advance payment sale). The author sets clear boundaries: salam is permissible for standardized goods but prohibited for animals and their parts. We will examine the proof texts and understand why the Hanafi school draws this line, and how it differs from the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is salam (advance payment sale). Ruling: permissible (jā'iz) for items sold by measure, weight, or count that do not vary (e.g., walnuts, eggs). Prohibited (lā yajūz) for animals, their parts, and hides by count.
The distinction hinges on whether the item can be precisely specified to avoid uncertainty (gharar).
2
Locate the dalil for permissibility
The author cites Quran 2:282 (the debt verse) and the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be for a known measure, a known weight, until a known term.'
These proofs establish the general permissibility of salam with precise terms.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for prohibition
For animals, the author uses the hadith of Samurah forbidding the sale of animal for animal on credit. This analogically extends to salam in animals because the same uncertainty exists.
The key is that animals vary individually, so their exact specifications cannot be guaranteed at the time of delivery.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school
Imam al-Shafi'i permits salam in animals, citing the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr where the Prophet allowed taking one camel for two camels on credit for army equipment.
The Hanafis respond that the hadith is specific to that situation, not a general permission.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) in the school. The prohibition is based on the principle of avoiding gharar, and the explicit prohibition in the hadith of Samurah is seen as stronger evidence.
Thus, in practice, Hanafi fiqh does not permit salam in animals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ السَّلَمِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - : السَّلَمُ جَائِزٌ فِي الْمَكِيلَاتِ، وَالْمَوْزُونَاتِ وَالْمَعْدُودَاتِ الَّتِي لَا تَتَفَاوَتُ كَالْجُوْزِ، وَالْبَيْضِ وَالْمَذْرُوعَاتِ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَلَا فِي أَطْرَافِهِ وَلَا فِي الْجُلُودِ عَدَدًا.
وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت السَّلَمُ جَائِزٌ فِي الْمَكِيلَاتِ وَالْمَوْزُونَاتِ: يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا تَدَايَنتُم بِدَيْنِ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مُّسَمًّى فَاكْتُبُوهُ (سورة البقرة، 282)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت السَّلَمُ جَائِزٌ فِي الْمَكِيلَاتِ، وَالْمَوْزُونَاتِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْمَدِينَةَ وَهُمْ يُسْلِفُونَ بِالتَّمْرِ السَّنَتَيْنِ وَالثَّلَاثَ، فَقَالَ: مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلٍ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ السَّلَم فِي وَزْنٍ مَعْلُومٍ، نمبر 2240/مسلم شریف، باب السلم، نمبر 1604)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَلَا فِي أَطْرَافِهِ: عَنْ سَمُرَةَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ بَيْعِ الْحَيَوَانِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ نَسِيئَةً (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ بَيْعِ الْحَيَوَانِ بِالحَيَوَانِ نَسِيئَةً، نمبر 1218/سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ بِالْحَيَوَانِ نَسِيئَةً، نمبر 3356)
وجه (۱) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَلَا فِي أَطْرَافِهِ: عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يُجَهِزَ جَيْشًا فَنَفِدَتْ الْإِبِلُ فَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ فِي قِلَاصٍ الصَّدَقَةِ، فَكَانَ يَأْخُذُ الْبَعِيرَ بِالْبَعِيرَيْنِ إِلَى إِبِلِ الصَّدَقَةِ (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الرُّحْصَةِ في ذَلِكَ، نمبر 3357)
Chapter of Salam. He (the author) said - may God have mercy on him: Salam is permissible in measurable items, weighable items, and countable items that do not vary, like walnuts, eggs, and measurable (length-wise) items. Salam is not permissible in animals, nor in their parts, nor in hides by count. Evidence (1): The verse for establishing that salam is permissible in measurable and weighable items: 'O you who have believed, when you contract a debt for a specified term, write it down' (Surah al-Baqarah, 282). Evidence (2): The hadith for establishing that salam is permissible in measurable and weighable items: from Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, he said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, came to Medina and they were paying in advance for dates for two and three years. He said: 'Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be for a known measure, a known weight, until a known term' (Bukhari, chapter on salam in known weight, no. 2240; Muslim, chapter on salam, no. 1604). Evidence (1): The hadith for establishing that salam is not permissible in animals nor their parts: from Samurah, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, forbade the sale of animal for animal on credit (Tirmidhi, no. 1218; Abu Dawud, no. 3356). Evidence (1): The proof of al-Shafi'i from the hadith for establishing that salam is not permissible in animals nor their parts: from Abdullah ibn Amr, that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, ordered him to equip an army and the camels ran out, so he ordered him to take from the charity camels, and he would take one camel for two camels until the charity camels (Abu Dawud, no. 3357).
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from the commentary on al-Quduri. The author begins by stating the ruling that salam (advance payment sale) is valid for items that are measured by volume, weight, or count, provided they are not subject to significant variation between individuals, such as walnuts, eggs, and items measured by length. This is because the key condition of salam is that the subject matter must be precisely describable to avoid gharar (uncertainty). Then he states that salam is invalid for animals, their body parts, and hides when sold by count. The proof for permissibility is drawn from the Quranic verse (2:282) which encourages writing down deferred debts, and the well-known hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet permitted salam with specified measure, weight, and term. For prohibition, the author cites the hadith of Samurah prohibiting the sale of animal for animal on credit, which analogically extends to salam in animals since the same uncertainty exists. He also mentions the Shafi'i proof from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr, which the Hanafis reinterpret or use differently. The inter-madhhab dispute is alluded to: Imam Shafi'i uses the hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr to argue that salam in animals is permissible, but the Hanafi position maintains prohibition based on the explicit prohibition of animal-for-animal credit sales. The Hanafi reliance is on the general principle that salam requires the subject matter to be available and precisely specified, which animals cannot guarantee due to individual differences.

Key Terms
السَّلَم (al-salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance for a specified commodity to be delivered at a future date.
الْمَكِيلَات (al-makīlāt): Items sold by volume measure, e.g., grains, liquids.
الْمَوْزُونَات (al-mawzūnāt): Items sold by weight.
الْمَعْدُودَات (al-ma'dūdāt): Countable items that do not vary significantly, like walnuts and eggs.
الْجُزُور (al-juzūr): Not directly in text; related to animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is salam not permissible in animals?
A) Because animals cannot be sold on credit at all.
B) Because animals vary individually making precise specification impossible, leading to gharar, as supported by the hadith of Samurah.
C) Because the Quran explicitly prohibits it.
D) Because the Prophet never engaged in salam for animals.

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid only for standardized items that can be precisely described; animals and their parts are excluded due to gharar.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Conditions for Valid Salam Sale
Lists conditions for validity of salam sale, including timing and specifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid salam contract and explain why salam must be deferred and not tied to a specific source according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Salam must be deferred with known genus, type, quality, measure, weight, and term — uncertainty in any essential element invalidates.

Salam is a unique sale where payment is made upfront for future delivery. Its validity hinges on precise conditions to eliminate gharar (uncertainty). This passage from al-Quduri outlines the essential rules: the commodity must be available from contract to delivery, delivery must be deferred, and specifications must be clearly defined with known genus, type, and quality. The Hanafi school derives these from the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the incident of Ibn Umar. We will examine each condition and the Shafi'i disagreement on spot salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of continuous existence
The muslam fīhi must exist from the time of contract until the time of maturity. This ensures the commodity is generally available and not dependent on a specific source that may fail.
Continuous existence means potential availability, not physical presence at contract.
2
Understand the requirement of deferment
Salam must be deferred; spot salam (immediate delivery) is invalid. The hadith requires a 'known term', so immediate delivery would negate the salam nature.
Shafi'i allows spot salam if the commodity is present, but Hanafi insists on deferment.
3
Recognize prohibitions on uncertain specifications
Salam cannot use a specific person's measure or arm length, nor be tied to a specific village's food or a specific tree's dates. These introduce uncertainty.
Standard measures and weights must be used to avoid gharar.
4
List the seven conditions partially enumerated
The passage states three of the seven conditions: known genus (jins), known type (naw'), known quality (sifa). The full list includes known measure, known weight, known term (ajal), and known place of delivery.
All seven must be mentioned in the contract.
5
Apply the evidence from hadith
The Prophet's command to return money when a specific palm tree failed (hadith of Ibn Umar) shows the prohibition of tying salam to a specific source. The hadith of Ibn Abbas (known measure, weight, term) supports the requirement for specification.
These dalils are used by Hanafi to derive the conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ حَتَّى يَكُون الْمُسْلَمُ فِيهِ مَوْجُودًا مِنْ حِينِ الْعَقْدِ إِلَى حِينِ الْمَحِلِ. وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ إِلَّا مُؤَجَّلًا. وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ بِمِكْيَالِ رَجُلٍ بِعَيْنِهِ وَلَا بِذِرَاعَ رَجُلٍ بِعَيْنِهِ وَلَا فِي طَعَامِ قَرْيَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا وَلَا فِي تَمْرِ نَخْلَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا. وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ إِلَّا بِسَبْعِ شَرَائط تُذْكَرُ فِي الْعَقْدِ: جِنْسٌ مَعْلُومٌ وَنَوْعٌ مَعْلُومٌ وَصِفَةٌ مَعْلُومَةٌ.
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا فِي الْخَطَبِ حُزَمًا وَلَا فِي الرَّطْبَةِ جُرُزًا: فَقَالَ: مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلِ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ (بخاري شريف بَابُ السَّلَمِ فِي وَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ، نمبر 2240/مسلم شریف: باب السلم،نمبر 1604)
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ حَتَّى يَكُون الْمُسْلَمُ فِيهِ مَوْجُودًا: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا، أَسْلَفَ رَجُلًا فِي نَخْلٍ فَلَمْ تُخْرِجْ تِلْكَ السَّنَةَ شَيْئًا فَاخْتَصَمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ، فَقَالَ: مَ تَسْتَحِلُّ مَالَهُ ارْدُدْ عَلَيْهِ مَالَهُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: لَا تُسْلِفُوا فِي النَّخْلِ حَتَّى يَبْدُوَ صَلَاحُهُ (سنن ابوداود شریف، باب فِي السَّلَم فِي ثَمَرَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا، نمبر 3467/بخاري شريف بَابٌ فِي السَّلَم فِي ثَمَرَةٍ بعينها، نمبر 2247)
وجه : (۱) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ إِلَّا مُؤَجَّلًا: فَقَالَ: مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلِ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ (بخاري شريف بَابُ السَّلَم فِي وَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ، 2240)
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلا فِي طَعَامِ قَرْيَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا وَلَا فِي نَخْلَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا، أَسْلَفَ رَجُلًا فِي نَخْلِ فَلَمْ تُخْرِجْ تِلْكَ السَّنَةَ شَيْئًا فَاخْتَصَمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ فَقَالَ: بِمَ تَسْتَحِلُّ مَالَهُ ارْدُدْ عَلَيْهِ مَالَهُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: لَا تُسْلِفُوا فِي النَّخْلِ حَتَّى يَبْدُوَ صَلَاحُهُ (سنن ابوداود شريف،بَابٌ فِي السَّلَم فِي ثَمَرَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا، 3467/بخاري شريف بَابٌ فِي السَّلَم فِي ثَمَرَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا، 2247)
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ إِلَّا بِسَبْعِ شَرَائط: فَقَالَ : مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلٍ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ، إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ (بخاري شريف بَابُ السَّلَم فِي وَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ، نمبر 2242)
And salam is not permissible unless the subject matter of salam exists from the time of contract until the time of maturity. And salam is not valid except when deferred. And salam is not valid using the specific measure of a man, nor using the specific arm length of a man, nor in the food of a specific village, nor in the dates of a specific palm tree. And salam is not valid except with seven conditions mentioned in the contract: known genus, known type, known quality.
Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing 'and not in firewood bundles nor in fresh dates batch': He said: Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be for a known measure, known weight, until a known term (Bukhari, chapter on salam in known weight, no. 2240; Muslim, chapter on salam, no. 1604).
Evidence : (1) The hadith for establishing 'and salam is not permissible unless the subject matter exists': from Ibn Umar, that a man paid in advance to another man for dates from a palm tree, and that year the tree did not produce anything, so they brought their dispute to the Prophet, who said: 'How do you consider his wealth lawful? Return his money to him,' then said: 'Do not pay in advance for dates until their ripeness appears' (Abu Dawud, no. 3467; Bukhari, no. 2247).
Evidence : (1) The proof of al-Shafi‘i from the hadith for establishing 'salam is not valid except when deferred': He said: Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be for a known measure, known weight, until a known term (Bukhari, chapter on salam in known weight, 2240).
Evidence : (1) The hadith for establishing 'and not in the food of a specific village nor in a specific palm tree': from Ibn Umar, that a man paid in advance to another man for a palm tree, and that year the tree did not produce anything, so they brought their dispute to the Prophet, who said: 'How do you consider his wealth lawful? Return his money to him,' then said: 'Do not pay in advance for dates until their ripeness appears' (Abu Dawud, no. 3467; Bukhari, no. 2247).
Evidence : (1) The hadith for establishing 'salam is not valid except with seven conditions': He said: Whoever pays in advance for something, let it be for a known measure, known weight, until a known term (Bukhari, chapter on salam in known weight, no. 2242).
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the conditions of salam. The author lists several prohibitions and requirements. First, the commodity ('muslam fīh') must exist continuously from the time of contract until delivery; if it perishes, the contract fails. Second, salam must be for a deferred delivery — spot salam is invalid because it would be a regular sale, not a salam. Third, the measure or weight used must be a standard (like a known measure or weight), not tied to a specific person's container or arm, to avoid uncertainty. Similarly, salam cannot be tied to a specific source (like 'the food of a particular village' or 'dates of a specific tree'), because that introduces risk of non-availability. Finally, he states that salam requires seven conditions to be mentioned in the contract, and he lists three: known genus (jins), known type (naw‘), and known quality (ṣifa). The seven total conditions are not fully enumerated here but are detailed in other Hanafi texts. The proofs are drawn from the same hadith of Ibn Abbas and the incident of Ibn Umar with the date palm. The Shafi‘i position is mentioned regarding the necessity of deferment, but the Hanafi view is that deferment is a condition (salam cannot be spot). The prohibition of salam in specific produce is supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet ordered returning the price because the crop failed, indicating the need for the commodity to be generally available and not tied to a specific source.

Key Terms
الْمُسْلَمُ فِيهِ (al-muslam fīhi): The commodity being purchased in a salam contract, which must be delivered in the future.
الْمَحِل (al-mahill): The time of delivery (maturity) of the salam commodity.
الْجِنْس (al-jins): The general category of the commodity (e.g., wheat, dates, cloth).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a valid salam contract?
A) A contract to deliver 100 kg of wheat of known type and quality in 3 months, using standard measures.
B) A contract to deliver dates from a specific palm tree in the next harvest season.
C) A contract to deliver 50 metres of cloth of known quality and type in 2 months, specifying the place of delivery.
D) A contract where the buyer pays now for 10 sacks of rice to be delivered at a known future date, using the seller's personal bag as measure.

Key Takeaway
Salam validity requires seven precise conditions including deferment, standard measures, and avoidance of specific sources to prevent gharar; failure renders the contract batil.

Salam Must Be Deferred and Prohibited in Specific Items
Rulings that salam must be deferred and not tied to specific persons or places.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid salam contract and explain why tying it to specific persons or sources invalidates it.

Core Idea
Salam requires known measure, weight, and a deferred term — uncertainty about quantity or source invalidates the contract.

This lesson examines two essential conditions of the salam contract from the Hanafi matn: deferment and avoidance of specificity in measurement or origin. The hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) provides the proof, and while both Hanafis and Shafi'is agree on deferment, the Hanafis additionally prohibit referencing specific individuals or locations to eliminate gharar (uncertainty).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two main rulings from the matn: salam must be deferred (mu'ajjal) and cannot be tied to a specific person's measure or a specific source.
The matn lists four specific prohibitions: specific man's measure, specific man's arm, specific village's food, specific palm tree's dates.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The commentary notes that Imam al-Shafi'i uses the same hadith to argue for the deferment condition. The Shafi'i school agrees on deferment but may have different views on specificity.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The hadith 'Whoever gives a loan in something, then in a known measure, a known weight, to a known term' is cited. Shafi'is use it to require deferment.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school uses the same hadith but interprets 'known measure and weight' as requiring generic description, not referencing specific individuals or locations. They add prohibitions to avoid gharar.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Both schools require deferment; the practical difference is that Hanafis invalidate salam contracts tied to specific sources, while Shafi'is may allow them if the description is sufficient.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ إِلَّا مُؤَجَّلًا وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ بِمِكْيَالِ رَجُلٍ بِعَيْنِهِ وَلَا بِذِرَاعِ رَجُلٍ بِعَيْنِهِ وَلَا فِي طَعَامِ قَرْيَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا وَلَا فِي تَمْرِ تَخْلَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا. د. وجه : (۱) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ إِلَّا مُؤَجَّلًا. وَقَالَ: مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلٍ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنٍ مَعْلُومٍ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ.
And salam is not valid except deferred, and salam is not valid with the measure of a specific man nor with the arm of a specific man nor in the food of a specific village nor in the dates of a specific palm tree. And he said: 'He who gives a loan in something, then in a known measure, a known weight, to a known term.'
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents two key rulings from the Hanafi matn on salam. First, salam must be deferred (mu'ajjalan); it cannot be a spot sale. Second, salam is invalid when tied to a specific person's measuring tool or a specific location's produce, as this leads to uncertainty (gharar). The commentary then provides the proof from hadith: the Prophet (PBUH) instructed that salam must be in known measure, weight, and term. It also notes that Imam al-Shafi'i uses the same hadith to argue for the deferment condition, indicating a point of agreement between the schools.

Key Terms
السَّلَم (as-salam): A sale where payment is made in advance for a deferred delivery of a specified commodity.
مُؤَجَّلًا (mu'ajjalan): Deferred; the delivery of the salam commodity must be at a future date, not immediate.
تَخْلَةٍ (takhlah): A specific palm tree; salam in the fruit of a particular palm is invalid due to uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is salam invalid when tied to a specific man's measuring cup?
A) Because the man may not be available at delivery.
B) Because it introduces uncertainty (gharar) about the exact quantity.
C) Because the man's cup may change size.
D) Because salam requires known measure, weight, and term.

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid only when deferred and when the commodity is described in known generic terms, not tied to specific individuals or locations.

Existence of Salam Commodity: A Condition for Validity
Ruling that salam commodity must exist continually

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the salam commodity must exist from contract to delivery and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Salam is invalid if the commodity does not exist continuously from contract to delivery.

Salam is a forward sale where the seller delivers the commodity at a future date in exchange for immediate payment. The Hanafi school insists that the subject matter must be in existence from the moment of contract until delivery to eliminate gharar (uncertainty). In this lesson, we examine the textual proof and the legal reasoning behind this condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
The passage opens with a prohibition: salam is not permissible unless the muslam fihi is present from contract to delivery. Identify the legal ruling (invalid/fasid) and the condition (existence).
The phrase 'mawjudan' indicates the commodity must be extant, not merely producible.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
Find the hadith cited: Ibn Umar narrates a case of salam in date palms that yielded no fruit. The Prophet (PBUH) ordered the return of the money.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Bukhari; it is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Analyze the Evidence (Wajh al-Dalalah)
Examine how the hadith proves the condition. The Prophet's command to return the money shows that if the commodity does not exist at delivery, the contract is invalid. The additional prohibition 'do not lend until the fruit ripens' further indicates that salam in something not yet existing is prohibited.
The analogy: if the fruit does not exist, the contract leads to gharar, a prohibited element.
4
Derive the Legal Principle
From the hadith, the Hanafi school derives the principle that the existence of the commodity from contract to delivery is a condition for salam's validity. If the commodity ceases to exist or is never present, the contract becomes fasid (corrupt) and must be rescinded.
This principle applies generally to all salam contracts, not just fruit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ حَتَّى يَكُونَ الْمُسْلَمُ فِيهِ مَوْجُودًا مِنْ حِينِ الْعَقْدِ إِلَى حِينِ الْمَحِلِ. عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَسْلَفَ رَجُلًا فِي نَخْلٍ فَلَمْ تُخْرِجْ تِلْكَ السَّنَةَ شَيْئًا فَاخْتَصَمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: «بِمَ تَسْتَحِلُّ مَالَهُ؟ ارْدُدْ عَلَيْهِ مَالَهُ»، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «لَا تُسْلِفُوا فِي النَّخْلِ حَتَّى يَبْدُوَ صَلَاحُهُ».

From Ibn 'Umar: A man lent another man in date palms, but that year nothing came out, so they referred to the Prophet (PBUH). He said: 'Why do you consider his wealth lawful? Return his money.' Then he said: 'Do not lend in date palms until their ripeness becomes evident.'

Commentary
This passage states a condition for the validity of salam: the commodity (muslam fihi) must be in existence from the time of the contract until the delivery date. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) ruled against salam in a specific palm tree that failed to produce fruit. This shows that salam in something that may cease to exist or not be available at delivery is invalid, as it leads to gharar and potential loss for the buyer. The Hanafi school uses this to require that the commodity be generally available and identifiable.

Key Terms
الْمُسْلَمُ فِيهِ (al-muslam fihi): The commodity that is the subject of the salam contract, which must be delivered at the future date.
مَوْجُودًا (mawjudan): Existing; the commodity must be in existence (available) at the time of contract and continuously until delivery.

Key Takeaway
For salam to be valid, the commodity must exist from the time of the contract until the time of delivery; otherwise, the contract is fasid.
