Seven Conditions of Salam and Immediate Payment
Enumerates the seven conditions for valid salam and the immediate payment requirement with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions of a valid salam contract, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement over conditions 6 and 7, and state the immediate payment requirement with its dalil.

Core Idea
Salam requires seven precise conditions and immediate capital payment; omitting any renders it fasid.

The salam contract allows immediate payment for future delivery, but its validity depends on strict conditions to prevent gharar. The Hanafi school enumerates seven conditions, though there is a notable disagreement between the founding imams on two of them. Moreover, the capital must be paid upfront in the same session, as established by a prophetic prohibition. This lesson unpacks these requirements and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the seven conditions
Locate all seven conditions mentioned in the passage: known genus, type, description, quantity, term, amount of capital, and place of delivery (if required).
Conditions 1-5 are agreed upon; 6 and 7 are disputed.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) disagree with Abu Hanifa on conditions 6 and 7: they consider them unnecessary if the capital is specified and delivery is at the contract place.
The Sahibayn argue that specifying the capital amount is redundant when the capital is a specific item, and the place is implied.
3
Analyze the dalil for immediate payment
Read the hadith forbidding the sale of debt for debt (kal' bi kal'). Understand that this prohibits any deferred exchange, thus salam capital must be paid immediately before the parties separate.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice to prevent gharar.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa requiring all seven conditions. The Sahibayn's view, though legitimate, is not the operative one for fatwa.
This is the standard in the Hanafi school as presented by al-Quduri.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test your understanding: if a salam contract omits the delivery place for a heavy commodity, what is the ruling per the mufta bihi? It is fasid due to missing condition 7.
The thamarah al-khilaf is validity vs invalidity in such cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ إِلَّا بِسَبْعِ شَرَائِطَ تُذْكَرُ فِي الْعَقْدِ: جِنْسٌ مَعْلُومٌ وَنَوْعٌ مَعْلُومٌ وَصِفَةٌ مَعْلُومَةٌ وَمِقْدَارٌ مَعْلُومٌ وَأَجَلٌ مَعْلُومٌ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ إِذَا كَانَ مِمَّا يَتَعَلَّقُ الْعَقْدُ عَلَى قَدْرِهِ كَالْمَكِيلِ وَالْمَوْزُونِ وَالْمَعْدُودِ وَتَسْمِيَةُ الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي يُوفِيهِ فِيهِ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حَمْلٌ وَمُؤْنَةٌ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: لَا يُحْتَاجُ إِلَى تَسْمِيَةِ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ إِذَا كَانَ مُعَيَّنًا وَلَا إِلَى مَكَانِ التَّسْلِيمِ وَيُسَلِّمُهُ فِي مَكَانِ الْعَقْدِ. وَلَا يَصِحُ السَّلَمُ حَتَّى يَقْبِضَ رَأْسَ الْمَالِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُفَارِقَهُ. عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم «أَنَّهُ نهَى عَنْ بَيْعِ الْكَالِئِ بِالْكَالِئِ».
And salam is only valid with seven conditions mentioned in the contract: known genus, known type, known description, known quantity, known term, knowledge of the amount of capital if it is of something on which the contract depends on its amount, like measured, weighed, and counted items, and naming the place of delivery if there is carriage and expense. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is no need to name the capital if it is specified, nor the place of delivery; he delivers it at the place of contract. And salam is not valid until the capital is taken before he separates. From Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (PBUH) that he forbade the sale of debt for debt.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage details the seven essential conditions for a valid salam contract in the Hanafi school. These conditions are: (1) known genus (jins), (2) known type (naw'), (3) known description (sifah), (4) known quantity (miqdar), (5) known term (ajal), (6) knowledge of the amount of capital (ra's al-mal) if it is among things measured, weighed, or counted, and (7) naming the place of delivery if the commodity requires transport. The commentary then records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) hold that these last two conditions are unnecessary if the capital is specified and the place is the default location of the contract. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa requiring them. Finally, another condition is added: the capital must be handed over immediately at the contract session, before the parties separate, as proven by the hadith forbidding the sale of debt for debt (kal' bi kal').

Key Terms
السَّلَم (as-salam): A sale with immediate payment for deferred delivery of a described commodity.
رَأْس الْمَال (ra's al-mal): The capital paid upfront in a salam contract; its amount must be known or specified.
الْكَالِئ (al-kali'): Debt that is deferred; sale of debt for debt is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The contract is valid and delivery at the place of contract is sufficient.
B) The contract is fasid (invalid) because a condition is missing.
C) The contract is valid but the buyer can choose the place.
D) The contract is suspended until the place is agreed.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires seven explicit conditions and immediate capital payment; the relied-upon Hanafi position includes all conditions as necessary for validity.

Conditions and Rulings of Salam (Forward Sale)
Conditions and proofs for salam contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions of salam according to the Hanafi school, apply them to a scenario, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on specification of capital and place.

Core Idea
Salam is a valid sale with immediate payment and deferred delivery; its validity hinges on known quantity, term, and immediate receipt of capital.

Salam is a unique sale contract where the price is paid upfront and the commodity is delivered later. The Hanafi school, as presented in Al-Quduri, lays out specific conditions to avoid uncertainty (gharar). This lesson unpacks those conditions, the supporting hadith proofs, and a key disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples on whether the capital and place must be specified. By the end, you will be able to identify the essential elements of a valid salam contract and apply them in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven conditions of salam
The passage lists conditions such as known quantity, known term, known capital measure (if applicable), place if transport cost, and immediate receipt of capital. List all conditions mentioned.
The conditions are derived from hadith and companion practice.
2
Understand the condition of capital specification
When the capital is of a type that depends on measure (like volume, weight, or count), its measure must be known. But if the capital is a specific item (mu'ayyan), specification is not needed according to the Sahibayn.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa requires specification even for specific items; Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no.
3
Understand the condition of place of delivery
If the commodity involves transport cost, the place of delivery must be specified. Sahibayn say no need; delivery occurs at the contract place.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn position.
4
Understand the immediate receipt of capital
Salam is not valid unless the capital is received before the parties separate. This is proven by the hadith forbidding the sale of credit for credit.
This is a non-negotiable condition.
5
Apply the general rule for salam commodities
Salam is allowed in anything whose description can be captured and measure known; otherwise it is not. Examples: cloaks (if length, width, patch specified), milk and bricks (with known description); not jewels or beads.
This rule prevents gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَ يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْفَهْدِ، وَالْكَلْبِ وَالسَّبَاعِ
و وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي رَأْسِ الْمَالِ \ سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما يَقُولُ: «أَمَّا الَّذِي نَهَى عَنْهُ النَّبِيُّ : فَهُوَ الطَّعَامُ أَنْ يُبَاعَ حَتَّى يُقْبَضَ» قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسِ : وَلَا أَحْسَبُ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا مِثْلَهُ ، » (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ بَيْعِ الطَّعَامِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُقْبَضَ وَبَيْعِ مَا لَيْسَ عِنْدَكَ ، نمبر 2135 مسلم شريف: بَاب بُطْلَانِ بَيْعِ الْمَبِيعِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ ،نمبر1525/(سنن ابوداود شريف ، بَابٌ فِي بَيْع الطَّعَامِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَسْتَوْفِي ، غبر 3492)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي القِيَابِ إِذَا سَمَّى طُولًا وَعَرْضًا وَرُقْعَةً \ عَنْ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: «إِذَا أَسْلَمَ فِي ثَوْبِ يُعْرَفُ ذَرْعُهُ وَرَقْعُهُ، فَلَا بَأْسَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في السَّلَم بِالقِيَابِ، نمبر21408)
الوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ الْمَدِينَةَ وَهُمْ يُسْلِفُونَ بِالتَّمْرِ السَّنَتَيْنِ وَالثَّلَاثَ، فَقَالَ: مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلِ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ، إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ» »(بخاري شريف بَابُ السَّلَم فِي وَزْنٍ مَعْلُومٍ ، نمبر 2240/ مسلم شریف: باب السلم،نمبر 1604)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَابَابُ السَّلَفِ فِي الْحِنْطَةِ وَالشَّعِيرِ وَالرَّبِيبِ وَالزَّيْتِ وَالشَّيَابِ وَجَمِيعِ مَا يُضْبَطُ بِالصَّفَةِ(الكبري لليبيهقي 11122) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَاعَنْ جَابِرٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ ثَمن السِّنَّوْرِ وَالْكَلْبِ سنن نسائي، الرُّحْصَةُ فِي ثَمَن كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ (4295 اصول: جتنے شمن پر مجلس میں قبضہ کیا ہو گا تو اتنی ہی کی بیع سلم صحیح ہو گی۔
Chapter of Salam: it requires a known quantity, a known term, and knowledge of the measure of the capital if it is of something on which the contract is based on its measure, like things measured by volume, weight, or count; and specification of the place where he will deliver it if it has transport and cost. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is no need to specify the capital if it is specific, nor the place of delivery; he delivers it at the place of contract. Salam is not valid until the capital is received before he separates from it. Proof: (2) Hadith: The Prophet forbade the sale of gharar and the sale of hasah. (3) Hadith: He is not from us who cheats. (1) (First condition) Saying of Companion: We used to give salam in the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar for wheat, barley, raisins, and dates. (Second condition) Saying of Tabi'i: If one gives salam for a cloth whose length and patch are known, there is no harm. (Fifth condition) He said: in a known measure and known weight to a known term. (Sixth condition) Ibn Umar said: There is no harm in described food at a known price to a known term. Proof: Hadith: He forbade the sale of credit for credit. They said: it is sale of deferred for deferred. Salam chapter: It is not permissible to dispose of the capital nor of the salam commodity before receiving it. Partnership and transfer (tawliya) are not permissible in the salam commodity before receiving it. Salam is permitted for cloaks if he specifies length, width, and patch. Salam is not permitted for jewels nor for beads. There is no harm in salam for milk and bricks if he specifies a known [?]. And everything whose description can be captured and whose measure can be known, salam is permissible in it; and what cannot be captured nor its measure known, salam is not permissible. And the sale of the leopard, dog, and predatory animals is permissible. Proof: (1) Hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The thing the Prophet forbade is food being sold until it is received; and I consider everything else similar. (Proof for cloaks) Saying of Tabi'i: If one gives salam for a cloth whose length and patch are known, there is no harm. (Proof for general rule) Hadith: The Prophet came to Medina and they were giving salam for dates for two and three years; he said: Whoever gives salam for something, then (it must be) a known measure, known weight, to a known term. (Another proof) Chapter of salam for wheat, barley, raisins, oil, and all that can be captured by description. (Another proof) Hadith: The Prophet forbade the price of a cat and a dog. Principle: Whatever is received in session, that is the amount for which salam is valid.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, with its hadith-based commentary, covers the essential conditions and rulings of the salam contract. The passage opens by stating that salam requires a known quantity, a known term, and knowledge of the capital’s measure when it is of a type whose contract depends on measure, such as things sold by volume (makil), weight (mawzun), or count (ma'dud). If the capital is specific (mu'ayyan), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say specification is not needed, and the place of delivery is also not required; delivery occurs at the place of contract. Then a key condition: salam is not valid unless the capital is received before the parties separate. The commentary then provides hadith proofs for seven conditions: (1) prohibition of gharar (uncertainty), (2) prohibition of cheating, (3) practice of the Companions in giving salam for food staples, (4) need to specify length and patch for cloth, (5) requirement of known measure, weight, and term, (6) permissibility of described food with known price and term, (7) proof for receiving capital from hadith forbidding sale of credit for credit. On page 336, further rulings: it is not permissible to dispose of the capital or the salam commodity before receipt; partnership (shirkah) and transfer (tawliya) are not allowed in the salam commodity before receipt. Salam is allowed for cloaks if length, width, and patch are specified; not allowed for jewels or beads; but allowed for milk and bricks if a known [?] is specified. A general principle: everything whose description can be captured and measure known, salam is permitted; otherwise not. Finally, the sale of predatory animals like leopards, dogs, and beasts is declared permissible, with supporting hadith. The commentary cites hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and others to substantiate each ruling. The passage also includes an Urdu marginal note about receiving in session.

Key Terms
السَّلَم (as-salam): A sale where the price (capital) is paid immediately in the session, and the commodity is delivered at a future date (forward sale).
رَأْسُ الْمَال (ra's al-mal): The capital or price paid by the buyer in the salam contract; it must be received before parties separate.
الْمُسْلَمُ فِيهِ (al-muslam fihi): The commodity or subject matter of salam that is to be delivered in the future; its description must be captured precisely.
الْغَرَر (al-gharar): Uncertainty or excessive risk in a contract that can lead to dispute; prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Quduri and the Hanafi school, what is required for the validity of salam concerning the capital if it is of a type that depends on measure?
A) The capital must be known by measure, weight, or count if it is of such type, and its measure must be specified.
B) The capital must be handed over at the place of contract regardless of transport cost.
C) The capital must be a specific physical item that can be identified without description.
D) The capital can be any commodity as long as the term is fixed.

Key Takeaway
Salam requires known quantity, known term, and immediate receipt of capital; the Sahibayn's position that specification of capital and place is not needed when capital is specific is the mufta bihi.

Prohibition of Disposing of Salam Capital Before Possession
Ruling with naqli proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that disposing of the capital (ra's al-mal) or the subject matter (muslam fihi) in a salam contract before possession is prohibited, and cite the hadith evidence from Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Do not sell what you do not possess: the prohibition applies to both capital and subject matter in salam before possession.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents a fundamental rule in salam (advance payment sale): you cannot transact with the capital or the goods before you physically take possession. The ruling is supported by a strong hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited selling food until it is taken, and Ibn Abbas analogized all commodities to food. Understanding this prohibition is essential for anyone engaging in salam contracts, as it prevents a form of gharar and ensures certainty in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
The text mentions three actions: disposing of the capital (ra's al-mal), disposing of the subject matter (muslam fihi), and creating a partnership or assignment in the muslam fihi. All are prohibited if done before taking possession (qabd).
Note: 'dispose' includes selling, gifting, or any transfer of ownership.
2
State the ruling (hukm)
The ruling is haram (prohibited) before possession. This is the Hanafi position based on the evidence.
The prohibition is one of tahrim (impermissibility), not just makruh.
3
Identify the evidence (dalil)
The author cites the hadith: 'As for what the Prophet prohibited, it is food that it be sold until it is taken possession of.' Ibn Abbas then said: 'I do not consider everything except like it.' This extends the rule to all commodities.
The hadith is recorded in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
4
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
Ibn Abbas used analogy to extend the prohibition from food to everything else. The effective cause (illa) is the risk of non-delivery or uncertainty (gharar), which applies to all salam contracts.
Some early scholars limited the prohibition to food only, but the Hanafi school follows the wider analogy.
5
Apply the ruling to partnership and assignment
The text explicitly mentions that shirkah (partnership) and tawliyah (assignment) in the muslam fihi are also prohibited before possession. These are forms of disposal.
This reinforces the general rule: no disposition of rights in salam goods until they are physically received.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ السَّلَمِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي رَأْسِ الْمَالِ وَلَا فِي الْمُسْلَم فِيهِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ الشَّرِكَةُ وَلَا التَّوْلِيَةُ فِي الْمُسْلَمِ فِيهِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي رَأْسِ الْمَالِ \ سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما يَقُولُ: «أَمَّا الَّذِي نَهَى عَنْهُ النَّبِيُّ : فَهُوَ الطَّعَامُ أَنْ يُبَاعَ حَتَّى يُقْبَضَ» قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسِ : وَلَا أَحْسَبُ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا مِثْلَهُ » (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ بَيْعِ الطَّعَامِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُقْبَضَ وَبَيْعِ مَا لَيْسَ عِنْدَكَ ، نمبر 2135 مسلم شريف: بَاب بُطْلَانِ بَيْعِ الْمَبِيعِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ ،نمبر1525/(سنن ابوداود شريف ، بَابٌ فِي بَيْع الطَّعَامِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَسْتَوْفِي ، غبر 3492)
Chapter of Salam: It is not permissible to dispose of the capital nor of the subject matter of salam before taking possession of it, and partnership and assignment are not permissible in the subject matter of salam before taking possession of it. Evidence (1): The hadith to establish 'it is not permissible to dispose of the capital' – I heard Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, say: 'As for what the Prophet prohibited, it is food that it be sold until it is taken possession of.' Ibn Abbas said: 'I do not consider everything except like it.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from the matn of al-Quduri states a ruling on the salam contract. Salam is an advance payment for future delivery of specified goods. The ruling prohibits any transaction involving the capital (ra's al-mal) or the subject matter (muslam fihi) before physical possession (qabd) takes place. This includes shirkah (partnership) and tawliyah (assignment) of the muslam fihi before possession. The author then provides a hadith from Ibn Abbas as proof: the Prophet prohibited selling food until it is taken possession of. Ibn Abbas analogized all commodities to food in this ruling. The hadith is from the Sahih collections, supporting the general prohibition on selling an item before taking delivery.

Key Terms
السَّلَم (as-salam): A contract of sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later, also called salaf.
رَأْسُ الْمَال (ra's al-mal): The principal or capital paid in advance by the buyer in a salam contract.
الْمُسْلَمُ فِيهِ (al-muslam fihi): The subject matter of the salam contract, i.e., the goods to be delivered in the future.
التَّوْلِيَة (at-tawliyah): Assignment or transfer of a contract to another party at the same price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract, when is it prohibited to create a partnership (shirkah) in the subject matter (muslam fihi)?
A) Before the seller receives the capital
B) Before the buyer takes possession of the subject matter
C) At any time during the contract
D) Only after delivery

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits any disposal of the capital or subject matter in a salam contract before physical possession, based on the hadith extending the prohibition of selling food before possession to all items.

Salam in Cloth and Other Specifiable Items
Rulings on salam in cloth, jewels, beads, milk, and bricks with proof from a tabi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on salam in cloth, jewels, beads, milk, and bricks, and identify the proof from the tabi'i.

Core Idea
Salam is only valid in items whose attributes can be precisely specified.

This passage from al-Quduri lists several items for salam and clarifies the central principle of specification. By examining cloth, jewels, milk, and bricks, you will see how the Hanafi school applies the requirement of known attributes to determine validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and rulings
Read the passage and list each item mentioned: cloth, jewels, beads, milk, bricks. Note the ruling for each: permissible for cloth, milk, bricks; impermissible for jewels and beads.
2
Recognize required specifications
For permissible items, note what must be specified: for cloth: length, width, piece; for milk and bricks: a known quality (mulayyin).
3
Understand the impermissible items
Jewels and beads are impermissible because their quality and weight cannot be precisely described in advance, leading to uncertainty (gharar).
4
Examine the proof
The author cites 'Amir (a tabi'i) who said: 'If one makes salam in a cloth whose length and piece are known, there is no harm.' This shows the early practice of specifying attributes.
The proof is a qawl of a tabi'i, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْقِيَابِ إِذَا سَمَّى طُولًا وَعَرْضًا وَرُقْعَةً وَلا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْجَوَاهِرِ وَلَا فِي الْخَرَزِ وَلَا بَأْسَ بِالسَّلَم فِي اللَّبَنِ، وَالْآجُرِ إِذَا سَمَّى مُلَيِّنًا مَعْلُومًا
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِي الْقِيَابِ إِذَا سَمَّى طُولًا وَعَرْضًا وَرُقْعَةً \ عَنْ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: «إِذَا أَسْلَمَ فِي ثَوْبِ يُعْرَفُ ذَرْعُهُ وَرَقْعُهُ، فَلَا بَأْسَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في السَّلَم بِالقِيَابِ، نمبر21408)
Salam is permissible in cloth (qiyab) if he specifies length, width, and piece. And salam is not permissible in jewels, nor in beads. And there is no harm in salam in milk and brick if he specifies a known quality (mulayyin). Evidence (1): Saying of the follower (tabi'i) to establish: 'Salam is permissible in cloth when he specifies length, width, and piece' – from 'Amir, he said: 'If one makes salam in a cloth whose length and piece are known, there is no harm.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah)
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri details the types of items in which salam can be conducted. The ruling is that salam is valid in cloth (qiyab) when the buyer specifies the length (tul), width (ard), and the piece or type of cloth (ruq'ah). Salam is not valid in jewels (jawāhir) and beads (kharaz) because they are not easily specifiable in advance (they vary in quality and weight). However, salam is permissible in milk (laban) and bricks (ājur) if the quality (mulayyinan ma'luman) is specified. The author supports the ruling on cloth with the statement of the tabi'i 'Amir: there is no harm if one makes salam in a cloth whose length and piece are known.

Key Terms
الْقِيَاب (al-qiyab): A type of cloth or garment; plural of qawb.
رُقْعَة (ruq'ah): A piece, patch, or specific type of cloth; here it likely means the kind or cut.
مُلَيِّن (mulayyin): Lit. 'softener'; here it refers to a known quality of milk or brick, such as consistency or composition.
ذَرْع (dhar'): Length measurement; in the proof it means the length of the cloth.
رَقْع (raq'): Piece or patch; in the proof it means the type or cut of cloth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, salam in which of the following is NOT permissible?
A) Cloth with known length and width
B) Milk with known quality
C) Jewels (jawāhir)
D) Bricks with known quality

Key Takeaway
Salam is only valid when the subject matter is described with sufficient precision to remove uncertainty.

General Principle for Validity of Salam Contract
General rule with hadith evidence for salam validity conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general principle for salam validity and apply it to classify items as permissible or impermissible for salam.

Core Idea
Salam is valid only for items that can be precisely described and quantified – uncertainty invalidates.

Salam (forward sale) is a contract where payment is made in advance for delivery of a specified commodity later. The core challenge is avoiding gharar (uncertainty) about the subject matter. This lesson presents the Hanafi principle that determines which items are suitable for salam: those whose description and quantity can be fixed.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the principle statement
Recite the Arabic: 'وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَ السَّلَمُ فِيهِ' – 'Everything whose description can be fixed and whose quantity can be known, salam in it is permissible.'
The negation also matters: 'وَمَا لَا يُمكِنُ ضَبْطُهُ وَلَا مَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ لَا يَجُوزُ'.
2
Parse the two conditions
Identify 'dabt sifat' (fixing description) and 'ma'rifat miqdar' (knowing quantity). These eliminate gharar in the subject matter.
Description includes type, quality, grade, etc. Quantity includes weight, measure, count.
3
Connect to the hadith evidence
The hadith from Ibn Abbas (in Bukhari and Muslim) instructs salam in a known measure, known weight, and known term. This supports the necessity of precise specification.
The prohibition of selling cats/dogs (from Jabir) shows that items lacking describable utility are not valid for salam.
4
Apply the principle to examples
Test items: wheat (permissible – type and weight easily fixed), a specific cow (not permissible – too many variable characteristics), a cat (not permissible – description not fixed for salam).
The rule is comprehensive: any item that can be described and quantified is valid; otherwise invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَ السَّلَمُ فِيهِ وَمَا لَا يُمكِنُ ضَبْطُهُ وَلَا مَعْرِفَةً مِقْدَارِهِ لَا يَجُوزُ السَّلَمُ فِيهِ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «قَدِمَ النَّبِيُّ الْمَدِينَةَ وَهُمْ يُسْلِفُونَ بِالتَّمْرِ السَّنَتَيْنِ وَالثَّلَاثَ، فَقَالَ: مَنْ أَسْلَفَ فِي شَيْءٍ فَفِي كَيْلِ مَعْلُومٍ، وَوَزْنِ مَعْلُومٍ، إِلَى أَجَلٍ مَعْلُومٍ» (بخاري شريف بَابُ السَّلَم فِي وَزْنٍ مَعْلُومٍ ، نمبر 2240/ مسلم شریف: باب السلم،نمبر 1604)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَابَابُ السَّلَفِ فِي الْحِنْطَةِ وَالشَّعِيرِ وَالرَّبِيبِ وَالزَّيْتِ وَالشَّيَابِ وَجَمِيعِ مَا يُضْبَطُ بِالصَّفَةِ(الكبري لليبيهقي 11122)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَاعَنْ جَابِرٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ ثمن السِّنَّوْرِ وَالْكَلْبِ سنن نسائي، الرُّحْصَةُ فِي ثَمَن كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ (4295)
And everything whose description can be fixed and whose quantity can be known, salam in it is permissible; and that which cannot be fixed nor its quantity known, salam in it is not permissible. Evidence (1): The hadith to establish: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'The Prophet came to Medina and they were making salaf (salam) in dates for two and three years. He said: Whoever makes salaf in something, then it should be in a known measure, known weight, and a known term.' (Bukhari, Muslim) Evidence (2): The hadith to establish: Chapter of salaf in wheat, barley, raisins, oil, and all that can be fixed by description (al-Kubra li'l-Bayhaqi). Evidence (1) of the hadith to establish: from Jabir: The Messenger of Allah forbade the price of a cat and a dog (Sunan Nasa'i).
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents the overarching principle for salam: anything that can be precisely described and quantified (dabt al-sifah wa ma'rifat al-miqdar) is suitable for salam; otherwise, it is not. The author supports this with two hadith (actually three, but the third from Jabir is about dogs, which seems to be a separate ruling but placed here in the text). The first hadith is from Ibn Abbas: when the Prophet arrived in Medina, people were doing salam in dates for long periods, and he instructed that salam must specify known measure, weight, and term. The second is a chapter heading from Bayhaqi's work listing items that can be fixed by description. The third from Jabir is about forbidding the price of cats and dogs, which is not directly about the general principle but is used to show that items like cats and dogs (which cannot be described sufficiently) are not permissible in salam. Thus, the principle serves as a comprehensive rule for the validity of salam contracts.

Key Terms
ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ (dabt sifatihi): The ability to precisely describe the item (e.g., type, quality) to avoid ambiguity (gharar).
مَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ (ma'rifat miqdarihi): Knowledge of the exact amount or quantity of the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general principle, what is the condition for salam to be valid?
A) The item must be edible
B) The item must be of high value
C) The item's description and quantity must be determinable
D) The item must be non-perishable

Key Takeaway
Salam is valid only for items whose description and quantity can be precisely determined; otherwise the contract is batil.

Selling Predatory Animals and Dogs: Hanafi Ruling and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on selling predatory animals with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on selling beneficial dogs and predatory animals, state the proofs from hadith, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Selling beneficial dogs and beasts is permissible; the exception for hunting dogs qualifies the general prohibition.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses the permissibility of selling leopards, dogs, and other beasts of prey. The Hanafi school holds that such sales are permissible for beneficial purposes, especially hunting. The text presents the hadith evidence and the Shafi'i objection, allowing us to analyze a classic inter-madhhab conflict over the interpretation of a general prohibition.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling in the matn: selling leopards, dogs, and beasts of prey is permissible. Note that this is a general statement needing specification.
The matn does not mention 'beneficial' explicitly; it is understood from the hadith.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that the opposition (Imam al-Shafi'i) holds that selling dogs is absolutely prohibited, based on a hadith that forbids the price of dog in a list including earnings of a prostitute and soothsayer.
The Shafi'i proof is a general (amm) prohibition without exception.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'He forbade the price of a dog, except the hunting dog.' This exception (khass) specifies the general prohibition.
Also consider the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i as supporting evidence.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the absolute hadith is qualified by the exception; thus the prohibition is not general but restricted to non-beneficial dogs.
This is a classic case of takhsis (specification) of a general text by a specific text.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis can validly buy and sell hunting dogs; Shafi'is consider such a contract invalid (batil).
This difference affects daily transactions in communities of different madhhabs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْفَهْدِ، وَالْكَلْبِ وَالسَّبَاعِ
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَن الكَلْبِ، إِلَّا كَلْبَ الصَّيْدِ (سنن الترمذي، الرُّخْصَةُ فِي ثَمَن كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ، نمبر 1281 /سنن نسائى الرُّحْصَةُ فِي ثَمَن كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ، نمبر 4295)
وجه : (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةُ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «لَا بَأْسَ بِثَمَنِ كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ رَخَّصَ فِي ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ،نمبر 20917)
وجه (1) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت وَكُلُّ مَا أَمْكَنَ ضَبْطُ صِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةٌ مِقْدَارِهِ جَازَ \ عَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودِ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم «نَهَى عَنْ ثَنِ الْكَلْبِ، وَمَهْرِ الْبَغِيِّ، وَحُلْوَانِ الْكَاهِنِ. » (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ نمبر 2237/ مسلم شريف: بَاب تَحْرِيم ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ. وَحُلْوَانِ الْكَاهِنِ، وَمَهْرِ الْبَغِيِّ. وَالنَّهْيِ عَنْ بَيْعِ السِّنَّوْرِ ، نمبر 1567/سنن الترمذي، الرُّخْصَةُ في فَمَن كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ، نمبر 1281)
And the sale of the leopard, the dog, and beasts of prey is permissible. Evidence (2): The hadith to establish: from Abu Hurairah, he said: 'He (the Prophet) forbade the price of the dog, except the hunting dog.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Sunan al-Nasa'i) Evidence (3): The saying of the follower (tabi'i) to establish: from Ibrahim, he said: 'There is no harm in the price of a hunting dog.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) Evidence (1) of al-Shafi'i: the hadith to establish: from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari: The Messenger of Allah forbade the price of the dog, the earnings of a prostitute, and the fee of a soothsayer. (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri deals with the permissibility of selling predatory animals. The Hanafi ruling (as per the matn) is that it is permissible to sell leopards (fahd), dogs (kalb), and all beasts of prey (sibā‘). The author then provides hadith evidence. The first hadith from Abu Hurairah shows a prohibition on the price of dogs, but with an exception for hunting dogs. The second is the statement of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that there is no harm in the price of a hunting dog. Then the author presents the counter-evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i: the hadith from Abu Mas'ud which absolutely forbids the price of dogs, without any exception. The Hanafi position is that the exception is proven by other hadith, and thus selling dogs for beneficial purposes (like hunting, guarding) is permissible. The Shafi'i school generally holds that selling dogs is prohibited absolutely. This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
الْفَهْد (al-fahd): Leopard, a predatory cat used for hunting.
السَّبَاع (as-sibā‘): Plural of sabu‘, meaning beasts of prey such as lions, wolves, etc.
دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِي (dalil al-shafi'i): The evidence used by Imam al-Shafi'i; here a hadith prohibiting the price of dogs absolutely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi proof in this passage, what exception is made to the prohibition of selling dogs?
A) Guard dogs
B) Hunting dogs
C) Pet dogs
D) Shepherd dogs

Key Takeaway
Selling beneficial dogs such as hunting dogs is permissible in the Hanafi school; the general prohibition is specified by the exception of the hunting dog.

Prohibition of Selling Wine and Pig
Ruling on prohibition of selling wine and pig

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wine and pig and cite the Quranic verse and hadith proofs that establish this prohibition.

Core Idea
If Allah forbids consuming something, He also forbids selling it.

Wine and pig are clearly prohibited in Islam for consumption. But what about their sale? This lesson examines the explicit ruling from Al-Quduri's matn, supported by three strong proofs: a Quranic verse and two hadith. You will learn not only the ruling but the underlying principle that guides the Hanafi school on all such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is selling wine and pig; the ruling is haram (prohibited). Understand that this prohibition is absolute, with no exceptions.
The matn states 'la yajuz' meaning it is not permissible.
2
Locate the first proof: Quran
Surah al-Ma'idah (5:90) calls wine an abomination (rijs) and commands avoidance. The Hanafi school derives that this avoidance extends to all dealings, including trade.
The verse is qati al-thubut but zanni al-dalala for trade; the hadith clarifies.
3
Locate the second and third proofs: Hadith
The hadith of Aisha records that the Prophet declared trade in wine forbidden. The hadith of Ibn Abbas establishes a principle: when Allah forbids consumption, He also forbids the price (sale).
These hadith are the main evidence for the absolute prohibition of sale.
4
Extract the underlying principle
The author gives two principles: (1) Anything not najis al-ayn and beneficial is permissible to sell. (2) Anything najis al-ayn and useless is not permissible to sell. Wine and pig are both najis al-ayn and devoid of benefit, so their sale is haram.
This principle also explains why dog sale is permissible in the Hanafi school (dog is not najis al-ayn and is beneficial).
5
Apply the principle
Test the principle: any item that is intrinsically impure and has no lawful benefit cannot be sold. This covers wine, pig, and similar items. Conversely, items that are pure or beneficial may be sold even if normally not consumed (e.g., dog for hunting).
The Hanafi distinction between dog and pig hinges on the dog being not najis al-ayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ
وجه : (1) الآية لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُواْ إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَمُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَنِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ ﴾ (سورة المائدة، 5 أيت نمبر 90)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ : «لَمَّا نَزَلَتْ آيَاتُ سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ عَنْ آخِرِهَا، خَرَجَ النَّبِيُّ الله فَقَالَ : حُرِّمَتِ التِّجَارَةُ فِي الخَمْرِ . » (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ تحريم التِّجَارَةِ في الخمر، نمبر 2226/ مسلم شریف: بَاب تَحْرِيم بَيْعِ الخَمْرِ ، نمبر 1580)
وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ، قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ الرَّكْنِ، قَالَ: فَرَفَعَ بَصَرَهُ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَضَحِكَ، فَقَالَ: «لَعَنَ اللَّهُ الْيَهُودَ، ثَلَاثًا إِنَّ اللَّهَ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّحُومَ فَبَاعُوهَا وَأَكَلُوا أَثْمَانَهَا، وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ إِذَا حَرَّمَ عَلَى قَوْمٍ أَكْلَ شَيْءٍ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ ثَمَنَهُ» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ في ثمن الخُمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ، غمبر 3488)
اصول: جو چیز نجس العین نہ ہو اور مفید ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز ہو گی۔ اصول : جو چیز نجس العین ہو اور غیر مفید اور بے کار ہو تو اس کی بیع سلم جائز نہ ہوگی۔
And the sale of wine and pig is not permissible. Evidence (1): The verse to establish: 'O you who believe, indeed, intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing on] stone altars, and divining arrows are an abomination of Satan's handiwork; so avoid it.' (Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 90) Evidence (2): The hadith to establish: from Aisha: 'When the verses of Surah al-Baqarah about the end of it were revealed, the Prophet went out and said: Trade in wine has been forbidden.' (Bukhari, Muslim) Evidence (3): The hadith to establish from Ibn Abbas: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah sitting near the corner, he raised his eyes to the sky and laughed, then said: May Allah curse the Jews, three times. Indeed Allah forbade them fat, so they sold it and consumed its price. And indeed when Allah forbids a people from eating something, He also forbids its price.' (Sunan Abi Dawud) Principle: Anything that is not intrinsically impure (najis al-ayn) and is beneficial, its sale is permissible. Principle: Anything that is intrinsically impure and useless, its sale is not permissible.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This final passage from the window states the explicit prohibition of selling wine (khamr) and pig (khinzir). The author provides three proofs. First, the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:90) which declares wine an abomination (rijs) and commands avoidance; this prohibition extends to trade. Second, the hadith of Aisha: when the last verses of Surah al-Baqarah concerning riba were revealed, the Prophet prohibited trade in wine. Third, the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet cursed the Jews who sold fat (shuhum) that was forbidden to them, establishing the principle that when Allah forbids the consumption of something, He also forbids its sale. Then the author provides two general principles (usool) in Urdu: (1) Anything that is not intrinsically impure (najis al-ayn) and is beneficial, its sale is permissible. (2) Anything that is intrinsically impure and useless, its sale is not permissible. Wine and pig are najis al-ayn and not beneficial, so their sale is prohibited. These principles also justify the earlier ruling on dogs: the dog is not najis al-ayn (according to Hanafi) and is beneficial (hunting), so its sale is permissible.

Key Terms
الْخَمْر (al-khamr): Intoxicating drink made from grapes or other sources; forbidden.
الْخِنْزِير (al-khinzir): Pig, its meat is forbidden and it is impure (najis al-ayn).
نَجِسُ الْعَيْن (najis al-ayn): Intrinsically impure; impurities that cannot be purified (e.g., pig, dog according to some).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If Allah forbids eating something, He also forbids its price
B) Only consumption is forbidden, not trade
C) Forbidden items can be sold for medicinal use
D) Trade in forbidden items is allowed for non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
Selling wine and pig is absolutely prohibited in Islam because they are intrinsically impure and useless, and the Prophet established that the prohibition of consumption extends to prohibition of sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Prohibition of Selling Wine and Pigs
Explaining prohibited sales with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wine and pigs, identify the five proofs cited, and explain the general principle that when Allah forbids consumption, He forbids the price.

Core Idea
Sale of najis al-ayn items like wine and pig is absolutely haram; the prohibition extends to their price.

Wine and pigs are intrinsically impure (najis al-ayn). The Quran and Sunnah explicitly prohibit their consumption and their sale. In this lesson, we examine five proofs from the source that establish this ruling, including the key principle that when Allah forbids eating a thing, He also forbids its price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The author states: 'ولا يجوز بيع الخمر والخنزير' – the sale of wine and pig is not permissible. Determine the hukm level: it is haram.
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
Two verses are cited: al-Maidah 90 declares wine and gambling as 'rijz' (abomination) from Shaytan, and al-An'am 145 describes pig meat as 'rijs' (filth). Both establish the impurity of these items.
Note that the term 'rijs' indicates intrinsic impurity (najis al-ayn) in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
Three hadiths are presented: (1) Aisha reports that trade in wine was forbidden, (2) Ibn Abbas reports that when Allah forbids consumption, He forbids the price, (3) Jabir reports that the Prophet forbade the sale of wine, dead meat, pigs, and idols during the Conquest of Mecca.
The second hadith establishes a general legal principle (qa'ida)
4
Derive the general usul principle
The source then states two principles in Urdu: (1) If an item is not najis al-ayn and is beneficial, its sale is permissible. (2) If an item is najis al-ayn and useless, its sale is not permissible. Apply this to wine and pigs.
This principle distinguishes between intrinsically impure items and those impure by external factors.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists; the ruling is unanimous. All schools agree that sale of wine and pigs is haram for Muslims.
The cross-madhhab difference concerns dhimmis, covered in another lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ السَّلَمِ

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ.

(وجه: 1) الآية: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ﴾ [المائدة: 90]

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: لَمَّا نَزَلَتْ آيَاتُ سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ عَنْ آخِرِهَا، خَرَجَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: حُرِّمَتِ التِّجَارَةُ فِي الْخَمْرِ. (رواه البخاري ومسلم)

(وجه: 3) الحديث: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ الرُّكْنِ، قَالَ: فَرَفَعَ بَصَرَهُ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَضَحِكَ، فَقَالَ: لَعَنَ اللَّهُ الْيَهُودَ، ثَلَاثًا إِنَّ اللَّهَ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّحُومَ فَبَاعُوهَا وَأَكَلُوا أَثْمَانَهَا، وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ إِذَا حَرَّمَ عَلَى قَوْمٍ أَكْلَ شَيْءٍ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ ثَمَنَهُ. (رواه أبو داود)

(وجه: 4) الآية: ﴿أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ﴾ [الأنعام: 145]

(وجه: 5) الحديث: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ، عَامَ الْفَتْحِ، وَهُوَ بِمَكَّةَ: إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ حَرَّمَ بَيْعَ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ وَالْأَصْنَامِ. (رواه مسلم)

(أصول: جو چیز نجس العین نہ ہو اور مفید ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز ہو گی۔ اصول: جو چیز نجس العین ہو اور غیر مفید اور بے کار ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔)

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دُودِ الْقَزِّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْقَزِّ وَلَا النَّحْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْكُوَّارَاتِ.

وَأَهْلُ الذِّمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ إِلَّا فِي الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ خَاصَّةً، فَإِنَّ عَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخَمْرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الْعَصِيرِ، وَعَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الشَّاةِ.

(وجه: 1) الحديث: عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، ثُمَّ جَاءَ رَجُلٌ مُشْرِكٌ مُشْعَانٌ طَوِيلٌ بِغَنَمٍ يَسُوقُهَا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: بَيْعًا أَمْ عَطِيَّةً أَوْ قَالَ: أَمْ هِبَةً؟ قَالَ: لَا، بَلْ بَيْعٌ، فَاشْتَرَى مِنْهُ شَاةً. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم اشْتَرَى طَعَامًا مِنْ يَهُودِيٍّ إِلَى أَجَلٍ، وَرَهَنَهُ دِرْعًا مِنْ حَدِيدٍ. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 3) الأثر: سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: لَا تَأْخُذُوا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ وَالْخَنَازِيرَ، وَلَكِنْ خَلُّوا بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ بَيْعِهَا، فَإِذَا بَاعُوهَا فَخُذُوا أَثْمَانَهَا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمْ. (رواه البيهقي وعبد الرزاق)

(أصول: جو ذمی، جزیہ دے کر دار الاسلام میں رہتے ہوں حقوق و معاملات میں مسلمانوں کی طرح ہیں۔)

وَجْهُ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي بَيْعِ الْكَلْبِ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ، وَمَهْرِ الْبَغِيِّ، وَحُلْوَانِ الْكَاهِنِ.
(وَجْهُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي الْكَلْبِ، وَهُوَ حَدِيثٌ مَشْهُورٌ)

وَجْهُ الْحَنَفِيِّ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ إِلَّا كَلْبَ الصَّيْدِ (سنن الترمذي، رقم 1281)، وَقَوْلُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعِيِّ: لَا بَأْسَ بِثَمَنِ كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 20917).
Chapter of Salam. Sale of wine and pig is not permissible. (Proof 1: Quranic verse al-Maidah 90. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that trade in wine was forbidden. Proof 3: Hadith of Ibn Abbas that when Allah forbids eating a thing, He forbids its price. Proof 4: Quranic verse al-An'am 145. Proof 5: Hadith of Jabir that the Prophet forbade sale of wine, dead meat, pig, and idols.) (Principles: If an item is not impure in itself and beneficial, its sale is permissible; if it is impure in itself and useless, its sale is not permissible.) And sale of silkworms is not permissible unless with the silk, nor sale of bees unless with the hives. And the people of dhimma in transactions are like Muslims, except specifically regarding wine and pig, for their contract on wine is like the contract of a Muslim on grape juice, and their contract on pig is like the contract of a Muslim on a sheep. (Proof 1: Hadith of Abd al-Rahman that the Prophet bought a sheep from a polytheist. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that the Prophet bought food from a Jew on credit and pawned his armor. Proof 3: Athar of Ibn Abbas: Do not take wine and pigs in their jizya, but let them sell them and take their price in jizya.) (Principle: Dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions.) And proof of al-Shafi'i regarding sale of dogs: Hadith of Abu Mas'ud that the Prophet prohibited the price of a dog, the earnings of a prostitute, and the fee of a fortune-teller. Proof of the Hanafis: Hadith of Abu Hurayra that the Prophet prohibited the price of a dog except the hunting dog, and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that there is no harm in the price of a hunting dog.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Salam (sale by advance payment) covers three distinct legal topics: the prohibition of selling wine and pigs, the conditional permissibility of selling silkworms and bees, and the rules governing transactions with dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state). The author first states the ruling: wine and pigs cannot be sold. He then provides five proofs: two from the Quran (Surah al-Maidah verse 90 declaring wine and gambling as abominations, and Surah al-An'am verse 145 describing pig meat as filth) and three from hadith. The hadith of Aisha explicitly states that trade in wine was forbidden when the verses of Surah al-Baqarah were revealed. The hadith of Ibn Abbas teaches a general principle: when Allah forbids the consumption of something, He also forbids its sale. The hadith of Jabir shows that the Prophet during the Conquest of Mecca declared the sale of wine, dead meat, pigs, and idols forbidden. The author then adds two usul (principles) in Urdu: The sale of something that is not impure in itself (najis al-ayn) and is beneficial is permissible; the sale of something that is impure in itself and useless is not permissible. This distinguishes between items that are intrinsically impure (like wine and pig) and those that are impure due to external factors (like dung, which may be sold for fertilizer). Next, two rulings on silkworms and bees: silkworms cannot be sold alone but only with the silk; bees cannot be sold alone but only with their hives. This is because these creatures are considered livestock whose primary benefit is their produce, not themselves. Then the passage discusses dhimmis: in all transactions, they are treated like Muslims, except for the sale of wine and pigs. Their contracts for wine are valid among themselves and are analogous to a Muslim's contract for grape juice (which is permissible for a Muslim to sell as a raw material that can become wine, but the dhimmi's contract for actual wine is recognized). Similarly, their contract for pig is like a Muslim's contract for a sheep. The author provides two hadith proofs showing that the Prophet conducted business with polytheists and Jews, and an athar (statement) of Ibn Abbas that authorities should not take wine and pigs as jizya payment but should allow dhimmis to sell them and then take the proceeds as jizya. The final usul principle states that dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions. Finally, the passage mentions a dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding the sale of dogs. Al-Shafi'i argues from a general hadith prohibiting the price of dogs. The Hanafis respond with a specific hadith that exempts hunting dogs, and the statement of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i permitting the price of a hunting dog. Thus, the Hanafi position allows the sale of dogs that are useful (hunting, herding, guarding) but not those without benefit.

Key Terms
الخمر (al-khamr): Intoxicating beverage made from grapes or other fruits; considered najis al-ayn (intrinsically impure) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith in this passage establishes the general principle that when Allah forbids the consumption of something, He also forbids its price?
A) Hadith of Aisha about trade in wine being forbidden.
B) Hadith of Ibn Abbas about the Jews selling fat.
C) Hadith of Jabir forbidding sale of wine, dead meat, pigs, and idols.
D) Hadith of Abu Hurayra about the price of a dog.

Key Takeaway
The sale of wine and pigs is haram for Muslims because they are najis al-ayn and their trade is explicitly forbidden by the Quran and Sunnah, establishing the broader legal principle that forbidding consumption extends to forbidding the price.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on Selling Silkworms and Bees
Ruling on sales of silkworms and bees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the valid sale of silkworms and bees and explain why they cannot be sold alone.

Core Idea
Silkworms and bees cannot be sold alone; they must be sold with their produce or habitat (silk and hives).

In addition to the prohibition on selling impure items, the text addresses creatures whose primary value is in their produce. Silkworms are valuable because they produce silk; bees because they produce honey. The Hanafi school rules that such creatures cannot be sold alone but must be sold together with their produce.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text says: 'ولا يجوز بيع دود القز إلا أن يكون مع القز ولا النحل إلا أن يكون مع الكوارات.' So selling silkworms alone is not permitted, only with the silk; similarly bees only with the hives.
2
Identify the reasoning
The ruling is based on the principle that these creatures are not considered mal (property) in themselves; their value is in their produce. Hence, they cannot be sold independently.
3
Apply the earlier usul principle
From the previous principles: sale of something beneficial and not najis al-ayn is permissible. Here, silkworms and bees are beneficial for their produce, but only when sold with the produce do they become valid subject matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ السَّلَمِ

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ.

(وجه: 1) الآية: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ﴾ [المائدة: 90]

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: لَمَّا نَزَلَتْ آيَاتُ سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ عَنْ آخِرِهَا، خَرَجَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: حُرِّمَتِ التِّجَارَةُ فِي الْخَمْرِ. (رواه البخاري ومسلم)

(وجه: 3) الحديث: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ الرُّكْنِ، قَالَ: فَرَفَعَ بَصَرَهُ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَضَحِكَ، فَقَالَ: لَعَنَ اللَّهُ الْيَهُودَ، ثَلَاثًا إِنَّ اللَّهَ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّحُومَ فَبَاعُوهَا وَأَكَلُوا أَثْمَانَهَا، وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ إِذَا حَرَّمَ عَلَى قَوْمٍ أَكْلَ شَيْءٍ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ ثَمَنَهُ. (رواه أبو داود)

(وجه: 4) الآية: ﴿أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ﴾ [الأنعام: 145]

(وجه: 5) الحديث: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ، عَامَ الْفَتْحِ، وَهُوَ بِمَكَّةَ: إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ حَرَّمَ بَيْعَ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ وَالْأَصْنَامِ. (رواه مسلم)

(أصول: جو چیز نجس العین نہ ہو اور مفید ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز ہو گی۔ اصول: جو چیز نجس العین ہو اور غیر مفید اور بے کار ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔)

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دُودِ الْقَزِّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْقَزِّ وَلَا النَّحْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْكُوَّارَاتِ.

وَأَهْلُ الذِّمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ إِلَّا فِي الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ خَاصَّةً، فَإِنَّ عَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخَمْرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الْعَصِيرِ، وَعَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الشَّاةِ.

(وجه: 1) الحديث: عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، ثُمَّ جَاءَ رَجُلٌ مُشْرِكٌ مُشْعَانٌ طَوِيلٌ بِغَنَمٍ يَسُوقُهَا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: بَيْعًا أَمْ عَطِيَّةً أَوْ قَالَ: أَمْ هِبَةً؟ قَالَ: لَا، بَلْ بَيْعٌ، فَاشْتَرَى مِنْهُ شَاةً. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم اشْتَرَى طَعَامًا مِنْ يَهُودِيٍّ إِلَى أَجَلٍ، وَرَهَنَهُ دِرْعًا مِنْ حَدِيدٍ. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 3) الأثر: سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: لَا تَأْخُذُوا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ وَالْخَنَازِيرَ، وَلَكِنْ خَلُّوا بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ بَيْعِهَا، فَإِذَا بَاعُوهَا فَخُذُوا أَثْمَانَهَا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمْ. (رواه البيهقي وعبد الرزاق)

(أصول: جو ذمی، جزیہ دے کر دار الاسلام میں رہتے ہوں حقوق و معاملات میں مسلمانوں کی طرح ہیں۔)

وَجْهُ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي بَيْعِ الْكَلْبِ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ، وَمَهْرِ الْبَغِيِّ، وَحُلْوَانِ الْكَاهِنِ.
(وَجْهُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي الْكَلْبِ، وَهُوَ حَدِيثٌ مَشْهُورٌ)

وَجْهُ الْحَنَفِيِّ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ إِلَّا كَلْبَ الصَّيْدِ (سنن الترمذي، رقم 1281)، وَقَوْلُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعِيِّ: لَا بَأْسَ بِثَمَنِ كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 20917).
Chapter of Salam. Sale of wine and pig is not permissible. (Proof 1: Quranic verse al-Maidah 90. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that trade in wine was forbidden. Proof 3: Hadith of Ibn Abbas that when Allah forbids eating a thing, He forbids its price. Proof 4: Quranic verse al-An'am 145. Proof 5: Hadith of Jabir that the Prophet forbade sale of wine, dead meat, pig, and idols.) (Principles: If an item is not impure in itself and beneficial, its sale is permissible; if it is impure in itself and useless, its sale is not permissible.) And sale of silkworms is not permissible unless with the silk, nor sale of bees unless with the hives. And the people of dhimma in transactions are like Muslims, except specifically regarding wine and pig, for their contract on wine is like the contract of a Muslim on grape juice, and their contract on pig is like the contract of a Muslim on a sheep. (Proof 1: Hadith of Abd al-Rahman that the Prophet bought a sheep from a polytheist. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that the Prophet bought food from a Jew on credit and pawned his armor. Proof 3: Athar of Ibn Abbas: Do not take wine and pigs in their jizya, but let them sell them and take their price in jizya.) (Principle: Dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions.) And proof of al-Shafi'i regarding sale of dogs: Hadith of Abu Mas'ud that the Prophet prohibited the price of a dog, the earnings of a prostitute, and the fee of a fortune-teller. Proof of the Hanafis: Hadith of Abu Hurayra that the Prophet prohibited the price of a dog except the hunting dog, and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that there is no harm in the price of a hunting dog.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Salam (sale by advance payment) covers three distinct legal topics: the prohibition of selling wine and pigs, the conditional permissibility of selling silkworms and bees, and the rules governing transactions with dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state). The author first states the ruling: wine and pigs cannot be sold. He then provides five proofs: two from the Quran (Surah al-Maidah verse 90 declaring wine and gambling as abominations, and Surah al-An'am verse 145 describing pig meat as filth) and three from hadith. The hadith of Aisha explicitly states that trade in wine was forbidden when the verses of Surah al-Baqarah were revealed. The hadith of Ibn Abbas teaches a general principle: when Allah forbids the consumption of something, He also forbids its sale. The hadith of Jabir shows that the Prophet during the Conquest of Mecca declared the sale of wine, dead meat, pigs, and idols forbidden. The author then adds two usul (principles) in Urdu: The sale of something that is not impure in itself (najis al-ayn) and is beneficial is permissible; the sale of something that is impure in itself and useless is not permissible. This distinguishes between items that are intrinsically impure (like wine and pig) and those that are impure due to external factors (like dung, which may be sold for fertilizer). Next, two rulings on silkworms and bees: silkworms cannot be sold alone but only with the silk; bees cannot be sold alone but only with their hives. This is because these creatures are considered livestock whose primary benefit is their produce, not themselves. Then the passage discusses dhimmis: in all transactions, they are treated like Muslims, except for the sale of wine and pigs. Their contracts for wine are valid among themselves and are analogous to a Muslim's contract for grape juice (which is permissible for a Muslim to sell as a raw material that can become wine, but the dhimmi's contract for actual wine is recognized). Similarly, their contract for pig is like a Muslim's contract for a sheep. The author provides two hadith proofs showing that the Prophet conducted business with polytheists and Jews, and an athar (statement) of Ibn Abbas that authorities should not take wine and pigs as jizya payment but should allow dhimmis to sell them and then take the proceeds as jizya. The final usul principle states that dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions. Finally, the passage mentions a dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding the sale of dogs. Al-Shafi'i argues from a general hadith prohibiting the price of dogs. The Hanafis respond with a specific hadith that exempts hunting dogs, and the statement of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i permitting the price of a hunting dog. Thus, the Hanafi position allows the sale of dogs that are useful (hunting, herding, guarding) but not those without benefit.

Key Terms
دود القز (dud al-qazz): Silkworms; the text rules that they cannot be sold alone but only with the silk they produce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for the sale of bees (al-nahl) to be permissible according to the passage?
A) They must be sold with the honey.
B) They must be sold with the hives (al-kuwwarat).
C) They must be sold to a Muslim.
D) They must be sold in exchange for cash only.

Key Takeaway
Silkworms and bees cannot be sold independently; they must be sold together with their produce or habitat (silk for silkworms, hives for bees) for the sale to be valid.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
7 min
Dhimmi Transactions: Wine and Pig Exceptions
Ruling on dhimmi transactions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding dhimmi transactions and explain why the sale of wine and pig is valid among dhimmis.

Core Idea
Dhimmis are like Muslims in all transactions except the sale of wine and pigs, which is valid among themselves.

The Hanafi school recognizes the transactions of dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state) as generally equivalent to those of Muslims. However, an important exception applies to the sale of wine and pigs, which are considered valid among dhimmis even though they are forbidden for Muslims. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The text begins: 'وأهل الذمة في البياعات كالمسلمين سواء' – dhimmis are like Muslims in all transactions. So the general principle is equality.
2
Identify the exception
The exception is: 'إلا في الخمر والخنزير خاصة' – except specifically for wine and pig. Their contract on wine is like a Muslim's contract on grape juice; their contract on pig is like a Muslim's contract on a sheep. So the sale is valid among dhimmis.
This means the sale of wine and pig between dhimmis is considered a valid contract, even though the items are impure.
3
Examine the proofs
Three proofs are given: (1) The Prophet bought a sheep from a polytheist, (2) The Prophet bought food from a Jew on credit, (3) Ibn Abbas said to let dhimmis sell wine and pigs and take the proceeds as jizya.
These proofs show that the Prophet and Sahaba engaged in transactions with non-Muslims, recognizing their ownership.
4
Derive the usul principle
The text concludes: 'جو ذمی، جزیہ دے کر دار الاسلام میں رہتے ہوں حقوق و معاملات میں مسلمانوں کی طرح ہیں۔' – dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions.
This principle establishes that their contracts are recognized, except where specified.
5
Apply to the exception
Thus, while a Muslim cannot sell wine or pig, a dhimmi can sell these items to another dhimmi, and the contract is valid. However, selling these items to Muslims remains prohibited.

Source Text

بَابُ السَّلَمِ

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ.

(وجه: 1) الآية: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ﴾ [المائدة: 90]

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: لَمَّا نَزَلَتْ آيَاتُ سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ عَنْ آخِرِهَا، خَرَجَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: حُرِّمَتِ التِّجَارَةُ فِي الْخَمْرِ. (رواه البخاري ومسلم)

(وجه: 3) الحديث: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ الرُّكْنِ، قَالَ: فَرَفَعَ بَصَرَهُ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَضَحِكَ، فَقَالَ: لَعَنَ اللَّهُ الْيَهُودَ، ثَلَاثًا إِنَّ اللَّهَ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّحُومَ فَبَاعُوهَا وَأَكَلُوا أَثْمَانَهَا، وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ إِذَا حَرَّمَ عَلَى قَوْمٍ أَكْلَ شَيْءٍ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ ثَمَنَهُ. (رواه أبو داود)

(وجه: 4) الآية: ﴿أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ﴾ [الأنعام: 145]

(وجه: 5) الحديث: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ، عَامَ الْفَتْحِ، وَهُوَ بِمَكَّةَ: إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ حَرَّمَ بَيْعَ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ وَالْأَصْنَامِ. (رواه مسلم)

(أصول: جو چیز نجس العین نہ ہو اور مفید ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز ہو گی۔ اصول: جو چیز نجس العین ہو اور غیر مفید اور بے کار ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔)

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دُودِ الْقَزِّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْقَزِّ وَلَا النَّحْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْكُوَّارَاتِ.

وَأَهْلُ الذِّمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ إِلَّا فِي الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ خَاصَّةً، فَإِنَّ عَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخَمْرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الْعَصِيرِ، وَعَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الشَّاةِ.

(وجه: 1) الحديث: عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، ثُمَّ جَاءَ رَجُلٌ مُشْرِكٌ مُشْعَانٌ طَوِيلٌ بِغَنَمٍ يَسُوقُهَا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: بَيْعًا أَمْ عَطِيَّةً أَوْ قَالَ: أَمْ هِبَةً؟ قَالَ: لَا، بَلْ بَيْعٌ، فَاشْتَرَى مِنْهُ شَاةً. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم اشْتَرَى طَعَامًا مِنْ يَهُودِيٍّ إِلَى أَجَلٍ، وَرَهَنَهُ دِرْعًا مِنْ حَدِيدٍ. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 3) الأثر: سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: لَا تَأْخُذُوا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ وَالْخَنَازِيرَ، وَلَكِنْ خَلُّوا بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ بَيْعِهَا، فَإِذَا بَاعُوهَا فَخُذُوا أَثْمَانَهَا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمْ. (رواه البيهقي وعبد الرزاق)

(أصول: جو ذمی، جزیہ دے کر دار الاسلام میں رہتے ہوں حقوق و معاملات میں مسلمانوں کی طرح ہیں۔)

وَجْهُ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي بَيْعِ الْكَلْبِ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ، وَمَهْرِ الْبَغِيِّ، وَحُلْوَانِ الْكَاهِنِ.
(وَجْهُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي الْكَلْبِ، وَهُوَ حَدِيثٌ مَشْهُورٌ)

وَجْهُ الْحَنَفِيِّ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ إِلَّا كَلْبَ الصَّيْدِ (سنن الترمذي، رقم 1281)، وَقَوْلُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعِيِّ: لَا بَأْسَ بِثَمَنِ كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 20917).
Chapter of Salam. Sale of wine and pig is not permissible. (Proof 1: Quranic verse al-Maidah 90. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that trade in wine was forbidden. Proof 3: Hadith of Ibn Abbas that when Allah forbids eating a thing, He forbids its price. Proof 4: Quranic verse al-An'am 145. Proof 5: Hadith of Jabir that the Prophet forbade sale of wine, dead meat, pig, and idols.) (Principles: If an item is not impure in itself and beneficial, its sale is permissible; if it is impure in itself and useless, its sale is not permissible.) (Proof 1: Hadith of Abd al-Rahman that the Prophet bought a sheep from a polytheist. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that the Prophet bought food from a Jew on credit and pawned his armor. (Principle: Dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions.) Proof of the Hanafis: Hadith of Abu Hurayra that the Prophet prohibited the price of a dog except the hunting dog, and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that there is no harm in the price of a hunting dog.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Selling Dogs
Inter-madhhab dispute on dog sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i proofs on the permissibility of selling dogs and apply the Hanafi principle of takhsis to the dispute.

Core Idea
Hanafis permit selling useful dogs based on a specified hadith, while Shafi'is prohibit all dog sales based on a general hadith.

The sale of dogs is a classic point of ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Both rely on authentic hadiths, but the Hanafi school, applying the usul principle of specification (takhsis), allows the sale of useful dogs. This lesson dissects the arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the sale of dogs that are beneficial (hunting, herding, guarding) is permissible. The sale of dogs without benefit is not permissible.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i argues from a general hadith (Abu Mas'ud) that the Prophet forbade the price of a dog without exception.
This hadith is in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafis rely on a specific hadith (Abu Hurayra) that forbids the price of a dog except the hunting dog. This exception specifies the general prohibition. They also cite the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
This is a principle of takhsis al-amm bi al-khass.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the general hadith is specified by the specific exception. In Hanafi usul, a general text (amm) can be specified by a separate specific text (khass). Also, benefit (manfa'ah) is a consideration.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Hanafi school, one may sell a trained hunting dog or guard dog, and the contract is valid. In the Shafi'i school, such a sale is invalid and the price is not lawful.

Source Text
