بَابُ السَّلَمِ

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ.

(وجه: 1) الآية: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ﴾ [المائدة: 90]

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: لَمَّا نَزَلَتْ آيَاتُ سُورَةِ الْبَقَرَةِ عَنْ آخِرِهَا، خَرَجَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: حُرِّمَتِ التِّجَارَةُ فِي الْخَمْرِ. (رواه البخاري ومسلم)

(وجه: 3) الحديث: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ جَالِسًا عِنْدَ الرُّكْنِ، قَالَ: فَرَفَعَ بَصَرَهُ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَضَحِكَ، فَقَالَ: لَعَنَ اللَّهُ الْيَهُودَ، ثَلَاثًا إِنَّ اللَّهَ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّحُومَ فَبَاعُوهَا وَأَكَلُوا أَثْمَانَهَا، وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ إِذَا حَرَّمَ عَلَى قَوْمٍ أَكْلَ شَيْءٍ حَرَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ ثَمَنَهُ. (رواه أبو داود)

(وجه: 4) الآية: ﴿أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ﴾ [الأنعام: 145]

(وجه: 5) الحديث: عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ، عَامَ الْفَتْحِ، وَهُوَ بِمَكَّةَ: إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ حَرَّمَ بَيْعَ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ وَالْأَصْنَامِ. (رواه مسلم)

(أصول: جو چیز نجس العین نہ ہو اور مفید ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز ہو گی۔ اصول: جو چیز نجس العین ہو اور غیر مفید اور بے کار ہو تو اس کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔)

وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دُودِ الْقَزِّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْقَزِّ وَلَا النَّحْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْكُوَّارَاتِ.

وَأَهْلُ الذِّمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ إِلَّا فِي الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ خَاصَّةً، فَإِنَّ عَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخَمْرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الْعَصِيرِ، وَعَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الشَّاةِ.

(وجه: 1) الحديث: عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، ثُمَّ جَاءَ رَجُلٌ مُشْرِكٌ مُشْعَانٌ طَوِيلٌ بِغَنَمٍ يَسُوقُهَا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: بَيْعًا أَمْ عَطِيَّةً أَوْ قَالَ: أَمْ هِبَةً؟ قَالَ: لَا، بَلْ بَيْعٌ، فَاشْتَرَى مِنْهُ شَاةً. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 2) الحديث: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم اشْتَرَى طَعَامًا مِنْ يَهُودِيٍّ إِلَى أَجَلٍ، وَرَهَنَهُ دِرْعًا مِنْ حَدِيدٍ. (رواه البخاري)

(وجه: 3) الأثر: سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: لَا تَأْخُذُوا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ وَالْخَنَازِيرَ، وَلَكِنْ خَلُّوا بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ بَيْعِهَا، فَإِذَا بَاعُوهَا فَخُذُوا أَثْمَانَهَا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمْ. (رواه البيهقي وعبد الرزاق)

(أصول: جو ذمی، جزیہ دے کر دار الاسلام میں رہتے ہوں حقوق و معاملات میں مسلمانوں کی طرح ہیں۔)

وَجْهُ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي بَيْعِ الْكَلْبِ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ، وَمَهْرِ الْبَغِيِّ، وَحُلْوَانِ الْكَاهِنِ.
(وَجْهُ الشَّافِعِيِّ فِي الْكَلْبِ، وَهُوَ حَدِيثٌ مَشْهُورٌ)

وَجْهُ الْحَنَفِيِّ: الْحَدِيثُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: نَهَى عَنْ ثَمَنِ الْكَلْبِ إِلَّا كَلْبَ الصَّيْدِ (سنن الترمذي، رقم 1281)، وَقَوْلُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ النَّخَعِيِّ: لَا بَأْسَ بِثَمَنِ كَلْبِ الصَّيْدِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 20917).
Chapter of Salam. Sale of wine and pig is not permissible. (Proof 1: Quranic verse al-Maidah 90. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that trade in wine was forbidden. Proof 3: Hadith of Ibn Abbas that when Allah forbids eating a thing, He forbids its price. Proof 4: Quranic verse al-An'am 145. Proof 5: Hadith of Jabir that the Prophet forbade sale of wine, dead meat, pig, and idols.) (Principles: If an item is not impure in itself and beneficial, its sale is permissible; if it is impure in itself and useless, its sale is not permissible.) And sale of silkworms is not permissible unless with the silk, nor sale of bees unless with the hives. And the people of dhimma in transactions are like Muslims, except specifically regarding wine and pig, for their contract on wine is like the contract of a Muslim on grape juice, and their contract on pig is like the contract of a Muslim on a sheep. (Proof 1: Hadith of Abd al-Rahman that the Prophet bought a sheep from a polytheist. Proof 2: Hadith of Aisha that the Prophet bought food from a Jew on credit and pawned his armor. Proof 3: Athar of Ibn Abbas: Do not take wine and pigs in their jizya, but let them sell them and take their price in jizya.) (Principle: Dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions.) And proof of al-Shafi'i regarding sale of dogs: Hadith of Abu Mas'ud that the Prophet prohibited the price of a dog, the earnings of a prostitute, and the fee of a fortune-teller. Proof of the Hanafis: Hadith of Abu Hurayra that the Prophet prohibited the price of a dog except the hunting dog, and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that there is no harm in the price of a hunting dog.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Salam (sale by advance payment) covers three distinct legal topics: the prohibition of selling wine and pigs, the conditional permissibility of selling silkworms and bees, and the rules governing transactions with dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of the Islamic state). The author first states the ruling: wine and pigs cannot be sold. He then provides five proofs: two from the Quran (Surah al-Maidah verse 90 declaring wine and gambling as abominations, and Surah al-An'am verse 145 describing pig meat as filth) and three from hadith. The hadith of Aisha explicitly states that trade in wine was forbidden when the verses of Surah al-Baqarah were revealed. The hadith of Ibn Abbas teaches a general principle: when Allah forbids the consumption of something, He also forbids its sale. The hadith of Jabir shows that the Prophet during the Conquest of Mecca declared the sale of wine, dead meat, pigs, and idols forbidden. The author then adds two usul (principles) in Urdu: The sale of something that is not impure in itself (najis al-ayn) and is beneficial is permissible; the sale of something that is impure in itself and useless is not permissible. This distinguishes between items that are intrinsically impure (like wine and pig) and those that are impure due to external factors (like dung, which may be sold for fertilizer). Next, two rulings on silkworms and bees: silkworms cannot be sold alone but only with the silk; bees cannot be sold alone but only with their hives. This is because these creatures are considered livestock whose primary benefit is their produce, not themselves. Then the passage discusses dhimmis: in all transactions, they are treated like Muslims, except for the sale of wine and pigs. Their contracts for wine are valid among themselves and are analogous to a Muslim's contract for grape juice (which is permissible for a Muslim to sell as a raw material that can become wine, but the dhimmi's contract for actual wine is recognized). Similarly, their contract for pig is like a Muslim's contract for a sheep. The author provides two hadith proofs showing that the Prophet conducted business with polytheists and Jews, and an athar (statement) of Ibn Abbas that authorities should not take wine and pigs as jizya payment but should allow dhimmis to sell them and then take the proceeds as jizya. The final usul principle states that dhimmis who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions. Finally, the passage mentions a dispute with al-Shafi'i regarding the sale of dogs. Al-Shafi'i argues from a general hadith prohibiting the price of dogs. The Hanafis respond with a specific hadith that exempts hunting dogs, and the statement of the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i permitting the price of a hunting dog. Thus, the Hanafi position allows the sale of dogs that are useful (hunting, herding, guarding) but not those without benefit.

Key Terms
الكلب (al-kalb): Dog; in this passage, the ruling on its sale is disputed between Hanafis (useful dogs allowed) and Shafi'is (absolutely prohibited).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the specific hadith that the Hanafis use to allow the sale of hunting dogs?
A) The Prophet forbade the price of a dog.
B) The Prophet forbade the price of a dog except the hunting dog.
C) The Prophet forbade the price of a dog, the earnings of a prostitute, and the fee of a fortune-teller.
D) The Prophet allowed the sale of all dogs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling useful dogs based on a specific hadith exception, while the Shafi'i school prohibits all dog sales based on a general hadith, representing a classic example of takhsis al-amm bi al-khass.

Selling Silkworms and Bees: The Ruling on Non-Independent Property
Ruling on selling specific non-independent items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling silkworms and bees and identify the legal rationale based on lack of independent property.

Core Idea
Silkworms and bees cannot be sold alone — they must be attached to their cocoon or hive.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar regarding the sale of silkworms and bees. The Hanafi school restricts such sales to ensure the subject matter is independently valuable and deliverable. We will explore the reasoning and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being sold? Silkworms (dūd al-qar) or bees (naḥl). The ruling: the sale is not permissible (lā yajūz) unless sold with their natural container (cocoon or hive).
The word 'lā yajūz' in Hanafi fiqh indicates the sale is invalid (fasid) if the condition is not met.
2
Understand the condition
Why must silkworms be sold with the cocoon and bees with the hive? Because these creatures are not considered independent property (mal mutaqawwim) apart from their habitat. Separating them creates uncertainty (gharar) in delivery and valuation.
The condition ensures the sale's subject matter is ma'lum (known) and qabil al-taslim (deliverable).
3
Link to Hanafi principle
The Hanafi principle is that a sale is invalid if the object is not property (mal) or not known. Silkworms and bees alone are not considered property because they are inseparable from their environment.
This is related to the concept of 'ain al-madmun (guaranteed substance) and the prohibition of gharar.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow selling bees alone if they are known and deliverable. The Hanafi view is more restrictive.
The difference arises from different definitions of property (mal) and the weight given to custom ('urf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ السَّلَمِ
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دُودِ الْقَرِّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْقَرِّ وَلَا النَّحْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْكُوَّارَاتِ وَأَهْلُ الذِّمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ إِلَّا فِي الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ خَاصَّةً فَإِنَّ عَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخَمْرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الْعَصِيرِ وَعَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الشَّاةِ

وجه :(۴) الآية لثبوت ولا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالخِنزير او إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَمَّا مَّسْفُوحًا أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ أَوْ فِسْقًا أُهِلَّ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ بِهِ فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغِ
وَلَا عَادٍ فَإِنَّ رَبَّكَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ (سورة الانعام، 6 أيت نمبر 145)

وجه:(۵) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ، عَامَ الْفَتْحِ، وَهُوَ بِمَكَّةَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ حَرَّمَ بَيْعَ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ
وَالْأَصْنَامِ (مسلم شريف: بَاب تَحْرِيم بَيْعِ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ وَالْأَصْنَامِ، نمبر 1581)

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَأَهْلُ الذِمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ ، ثُمَّ جَاءَ رَجُلٌ مُشْرِكٌ مُشْعَانٌ طَوِيلٌ، بِغَنَمٍ يَسُوقُهَا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ : بَيْعًا أَمْ عَطِيَّةً أَوْ قَالَ: أَمْ هِبَةً؟ قَالَ : لا ، بَلْ بَيْعٌ فَاشْتَرَى مِنْهُ شَاةً.»» (بخاري شریف بَاب الشَّرَاءِ وَالْبَيْعِ مَعَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ وَأَهْلِ الحَرْبِ، نمبر 2216)

وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَأَهْلُ الذِمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم اشْتَرَى طَعَامًا مِنْ يَهُودِي إِلَى أَجَلٍ، وَرَهَنَهُ دِرْعًا مِنْ حَدِيدٍ.»» (بخاري شريف بَابُ شِرَاءِ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالنَّسِيئَةِ، غمبر 2068)

وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَأَهْلُ الذِمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ سَمِعَ ابْنَ [؟] أَثْمَانَ الْخَمْرِ وَأَثْمَانَ الْخَنَازِيرِ، أَلَمْ تَعْلَمْ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: " لَعَنَ اللهُ الْيَهُودَ حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّحُومُ أَنْ يَأْكُلُوهَا فَجَمَّلُوهَا فَبَاعُوهَا وَأَكَلُوا أَثْمَانَهَا " قَالَ سُفْيَانُ يَقُولُ: لَا تَأْخُذُوا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ وَالْخَنَازِيرَ، وَلَكِنْ خَلُّوا بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ بَيْعِهَا، فَإِذَا بَاعُوهَا فَخُذُوا أَثْمَانَهَا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمْ ( السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ لَا يَأْخُذُ مِنْهُمْ فِي الْحِزْيَةِ خَمْرًا وَلَا خِنْزِيرًا، نمبر 18738/ مصنف عبد الرزاق،بَابُ: بَيْعُ الخُمْر، غير 14853)

اصول: جو ڈی ٹیکس، جزیہ دے کر دار الاسلام میں رہتے ہوں حقوق و معاملات میں مسلمانوں کی طرح ہیں۔
Chapter of Salam
It is not permissible to sell silkworms [دود القَرِّ] except if they are with the cocoon [القَرِّ], nor bees except if they are with the hives. And the People of the Dhimmah in transactions are like the Muslims except specifically in wine and pork, for their contract on wine is like the contract of a Muslim on grape juice, and their contract on pork is like the contract of a Muslim on a sheep.
[Then proofs from Quran and Hadith]
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings from the Hanafi school. First: selling silkworms (dūd al-qar) is not valid unless sold together with the cocoon (qar); similarly, bees cannot be sold alone but only with their hives (kuwwārāt). This is because these items are not considered independent property separable from their habitat. Second: ahl al-dhimmah (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state) are treated like Muslims in all sales transactions, with the exception of wine and pork. Their sale of wine is analogized to a Muslim's sale of grape juice (which is permissible), and their sale of pork to a Muslim's sale of a sheep—meaning it is valid for them internally. The passage then provides multiple proofs: Quranic verse (6:145) prohibiting carrion, blood, pork, and that over which other than Allah's name is invoked; hadith of Jabir that the Prophet forbade selling wine, carrion, pork, and idols; hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr about buying a sheep from a polytheist; hadith of Aisha about buying food from a Jew on credit; and a report about taking the price of wine and pork in jizya. The Urdu note at the end summarizes: 'Those who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions.'

Key Terms
دود القَرِّ (dūd al-qar): Silkworms, specifically the larvae that produce silk cocoons.
النحل (al-naḥl): Bees.
الكوارات (al-kuwwārāt): Hives or beehives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, selling bees alone is:
A) Permissible
B) Permissible only if the buyer will use them for honey
C) Not permissible unless sold with the hive
D) Prohibited entirely

Key Takeaway
Silkworms and bees are not independent property in Hanafi law; they must be sold with their natural containers.

Transactions with Dhimmis: Equal Rights with Exception of Wine and Pork
General rule and exception for dhimmis in sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that dhimmis are like Muslims in transactions except for wine and pork, and identify the proof from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Dhimmis may transact wine and pork among themselves, but Muslims may not buy, sell, or consume them.

This lesson covers the second part of the passage: the legal status of ahl al-dhimmah in commercial transactions. The Hanafi school affirms that dhimmis are treated the same as Muslims in all sales, except that their contracts regarding wine and pork are valid for them personally. We will examine the textual proofs and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Ahl al-dhimmah are like Muslims in all transactions: buying, selling, leasing, etc. The same rules of validity apply.
This establishes equality in contractual capacity.
2
Identify the exception
The only exception is wine (khamr) and pork (khinzir). For these items, dhimmis may contract among themselves, but Muslims cannot participate.
The exception is specific; all other goods and services are treated identically.
3
Understand the analogy
A dhimmi's contract on wine is likened to a Muslim's contract on grape juice (which is permissible for Muslims to buy/sell). A dhimmi's contract on pork is like a Muslim's contract on a sheep.
This analogy clarifies that the contracts are valid and enforceable for dhimmis, despite the items being forbidden to Muslims.
4
Review the proofs
The passage cites Quran 6:145 (prohibition of wine, pork, etc.) and multiple hadith: Jabir's hadith on prohibition of selling wine, pork, idols; the hadith of buying a sheep from a polytheist; and the hadith of buying food from a Jew on credit.
These proofs establish both the general rule of equality (through practice) and the exception (through explicit prohibition for Muslims).
5
Derive the rationale
Dhimmis are allowed to practice their religion, which may involve consuming wine and pork. Therefore, their internal trade in these items is permitted. However, Muslims are strictly prohibited from dealing in them.
The ruling balances religious freedom with Islamic law's clear injunctions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ السَّلَمِ
وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دُودِ الْقَرِّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْقَرِّ وَلَا النَّحْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ الْكُوَّارَاتِ وَأَهْلُ الذِّمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ إِلَّا فِي الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ خَاصَّةً فَإِنَّ عَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخَمْرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الْعَصِيرِ وَعَقْدَهُمْ عَلَى الْخِنْزِيرِ كَعَقْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى الشَّاةِ

وجه :(۴) الآية لثبوت ولا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالخِنزير او إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَمَّا مَّسْفُوحًا أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ فَإِنَّهُ رِجْسٌ أَوْ فِسْقًا أُهِلَّ لِغَيْرِ اللَّهِ بِهِ فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغِ
وَلَا عَادٍ فَإِنَّ رَبَّكَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ (سورة الانعام، 6 أيت نمبر 145)

وجه:(۵) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْخَمْرِ، وَالْخِنْزِيرِ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ، عَامَ الْفَتْحِ، وَهُوَ بِمَكَّةَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ حَرَّمَ بَيْعَ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ
وَالْأَصْنَامِ (مسلم شريف: بَاب تَحْرِيم بَيْعِ الْخَمْرِ وَالْمَيْتَةِ وَالْخِنْزِيرِ وَالْأَصْنَامِ، نمبر 1581)

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَأَهْلُ الذِمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «كُنَّا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ ، ثُمَّ جَاءَ رَجُلٌ مُشْرِكٌ مُشْعَانٌ طَوِيلٌ، بِغَنَمٍ يَسُوقُهَا، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ : بَيْعًا أَمْ عَطِيَّةً أَوْ قَالَ: أَمْ هِبَةً؟ قَالَ : لا ، بَلْ بَيْعٌ فَاشْتَرَى مِنْهُ شَاةً.»» (بخاري شریف بَاب الشَّرَاءِ وَالْبَيْعِ مَعَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ وَأَهْلِ الحَرْبِ، نمبر 2216)

وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَأَهْلُ الذِمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم اشْتَرَى طَعَامًا مِنْ يَهُودِي إِلَى أَجَلٍ، وَرَهَنَهُ دِرْعًا مِنْ حَدِيدٍ.»» (بخاري شريف بَابُ شِرَاءِ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالنَّسِيئَةِ، غمبر 2068)

وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَأَهْلُ الذِمَّةِ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ كَالْمُسْلِمِينَ سَوَاءٌ سَمِعَ ابْنَ [؟] أَثْمَانَ الْخَمْرِ وَأَثْمَانَ الْخَنَازِيرِ، أَلَمْ تَعْلَمْ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: " لَعَنَ اللهُ الْيَهُودَ حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّحُومُ أَنْ يَأْكُلُوهَا فَجَمَّلُوهَا فَبَاعُوهَا وَأَكَلُوا أَثْمَانَهَا " قَالَ سُفْيَانُ يَقُولُ: لَا تَأْخُذُوا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ وَالْخَنَازِيرَ، وَلَكِنْ خَلُّوا بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ بَيْعِهَا، فَإِذَا بَاعُوهَا فَخُذُوا أَثْمَانَهَا فِي جِزْيَتِهِمْ ( السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ لَا يَأْخُذُ مِنْهُمْ فِي الْحِزْيَةِ خَمْرًا وَلَا خِنْزِيرًا، نمبر 18738/ مصنف عبد الرزاق،بَابُ: بَيْعُ الخُمْر، غير 14853)

اصول: جو ڈی ٹیکس، جزیہ دے کر دار الاسلام میں رہتے ہوں حقوق و معاملات میں مسلمانوں کی طرح ہیں۔
Chapter of Salam
It is not permissible to sell silkworms [دود القَرِّ] except if they are with the cocoon [القَرِّ], nor bees except if they are with the hives. And the People of the Dhimmah in transactions are like the Muslims except specifically in wine and pork, for their contract on wine is like the contract of a Muslim on grape juice, and their contract on pork is like the contract of a Muslim on a sheep.
[Then proofs from Quran and Hadith]
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings from the Hanafi school. First: selling silkworms (dūd al-qar) is not valid unless sold together with the cocoon (qar); similarly, bees cannot be sold alone but only with their hives (kuwwārāt). This is because these items are not considered independent property separable from their habitat. Second: ahl al-dhimmah (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state) are treated like Muslims in all sales transactions, with the exception of wine and pork. Their sale of wine is analogized to a Muslim's sale of grape juice (which is permissible), and their sale of pork to a Muslim's sale of a sheep—meaning it is valid for them internally. The passage then provides multiple proofs: Quranic verse (6:145) prohibiting carrion, blood, pork, and that over which other than Allah's name is invoked; hadith of Jabir that the Prophet forbade selling wine, carrion, pork, and idols; hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr about buying a sheep from a polytheist; hadith of Aisha about buying food from a Jew on credit; and a report about taking the price of wine and pork in jizya. The Urdu note at the end summarizes: 'Those who pay jizya and live in Dar al-Islam are like Muslims in rights and transactions.'

Key Terms
أهل الذمة (ahl al-dhimmah): Non-Muslim subjects of an Islamic state who pay jizya and enjoy protection and legal rights.
الخمر (al-khamr): Wine or any intoxicating beverage.
الخنزير (al-khinzir): Pork, pig meat.
العصير (al-ʿaṣīr): Grape juice (non-intoxicating).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a dhimmi's contract to sell wine to another dhimmi is:
A) Invalid like a Muslim selling wine
B) Valid analogized to a Muslim selling grape juice
C) Permissible only if the ruler permits
D) Makruh but valid

Key Takeaway
Dhimmis are equal to Muslims in all transactions except that their internal trade of wine and pork is valid, reflecting their religious freedom.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Definition and Conditions of Sarf (Currency Exchange)
Defines sarf and states two essential conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sarf, state its two essential conditions (equality by weight and spot delivery), and apply them to determine the validity of a gold or silver exchange.

Core Idea
Same-metal gold/silver exchange must be equal by weight and hand-to-hand; any excess is riba.

Sarf refers to the sale of gold and silver for gold and silver. The Hanafi school lays down two critical conditions: the quantities must be exactly equal by weight regardless of quality, and both parties must take possession before parting. Violation renders the transaction invalid and constitutes usury (riba). The Prophet's hadith provides the explicit basis.

Guided Path
1
Define sarf
Identify that sarf is a sale where both counter-values are from the category of prices (athman), i.e., gold or silver.
This distinguishes sarf from ordinary sales of goods.
2
Identify the condition for same-metal exchange
When exchanging gold for gold or silver for silver, the weights must be exactly equal (mithlan bi mithlin), regardless of differences in quality or craftsmanship.
Quality is irrelevant; only weight matters.
3
Identify the condition of spot delivery
Both parties must physically take possession (qabd) before they separate. The exchange cannot be deferred.
This is indicated by 'yadan bi yadin' (hand to hand).
4
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet ﷺ explicitly commanded equality and spot delivery, declaring any excess as riba. This is a clear, binding textual proof.
The hadith is sahih and constitutes a definitive ruling.
5
Note the usul principle
For ribawi goods of the same type, quality is not considered; for different types (e.g., gold for silver), excess is permissible but spot delivery still required.
This principle follows from the hadith and is confirmed by the Hanafi usul of ta'lil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الصَّرْفِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - : 1 الصَّرْفُ هُوَ الْبَيْعُ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عِوَضَيْهِ مِنْ جِنْسِ الْأَثْمَانِ ل فَإِنْ بَاعَ فِضَّةٌ بِفِضَّةٍ، أَوْ ذَهَبًا بِذَهَبِ لَمْ يَجْزْ إِلَّا مِثْلَا بِمِثْلٍ وَإِنْ اخْتَلَفَا فِي الْجَوْدَةِ وَالصَّنَاعَةِ وَلا بُدَّ مِنْ قَبْض الْعِوَضَيْن قَبْلَ الافتراق

وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت الصَّرْفُ هُوَ الْبَيْعُ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عِوَضَيْهِ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم (الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة. والبر بالبر. وَالشَّعِيرُ بِالشَّعِيرِ وَالتَّمْرُ بِالتَّمْرِ. وَالْمِلْحُ بِالْمِلْحِ مِثَلًا مِثْلِ. يَدًا بِيَدِ. فَمَنْ زَادَ أَوِ اسْتَزَادَ فَقَدْ أَرْبَى. الْآخِذُ وَالْمُعْطِي فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ) (سنن الترمذي، بَاب الصَّرْفِ وَبَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ نَقْدًا، نمبر 1584/ (بخاري شريف بَابُ بَيْعِ الْفِضَّةِ بِالْفِضَّةِ، نمبر 2176)

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت الصَّرْفُ هُوَ الْبَيْعُ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عِوَضَيْهِ مِثْلَا بِمِثْلِ. يَدًا بِيَدٍ. فَمَنْ زَادَ أَوِ اسْتَزَادَ فَقَدْ أَرْبَى. الْآخِذُ وَالْمُعْطِي فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ) (سنن الترمذي، بَاب الصَّرْفِ وَبَيْعِ الذَّهَب بِالْوَرِقِ نَقْدًا، غمبر 1584)

وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت الصَّرْفُ هُوَ الْبَيْعُ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عِوَضَيْهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رضي الله عنهما : «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ اسْتَعْمَلَ رَجُلًا عَلَى خَيْبَرَ فَجَاءَهُ بِتَمْرٍ جَنِيبٍ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ: أَكُلُّ تَر خَيْبَرَ هَكَذَا، قَالَ : لَا وَاللهِ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ، إِنَّا لَتَأْخُذُ الصَّاعَ مِنْ هَذَا بِالصَّاعَيْنِ، وَالصَّاعَيْنِ بِالثَّلَاثَةِ. فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَا تَفْعَلْ مِع الْجُمْعَ بِالدَّرَاهِم، ثُمَّ ابْتَعْ بِالدَّرَاهِم جَنِيبًا.» (صحيح البخاري بَابٌ : إِذَا أَرَادَ بَيْعَ تَر بِتَمْرِ خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ، نمبر 2201)

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت الصَّرْفُ هُوَ الْبَيْعُ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عِوَضَيْهِ «سَأَلْتُ الْبَرَاءَ بْنَ عَازِبٍ وَزَيْدَ بْنَ أَرْقَمَ اللهُ عَنِ الصَّرْفِ، فَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: هَذَا خَيْرٌ مِنِّي، فَكِلَاهُمَا يَقُولُ: نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الذَّهَبِ بِالْوَرِقِ دَيْنًا.»» (بخاري شريف بَابُ بَيْعِ الْوَرِقِ بِالذَّهَبِ نَسِيئَةً، نمبر 2180/مسلم شريف : بَاب النَّهْيِ عَنْ بَيْعِ الْوَرِقِ بِالذَّهَبِ دَيْنًا، نمبر 1589)

اصول: اموال ربویہ میں مبیع اور شمن ایک ہی جنس کا ہو تو عمدہ اور ردی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔
اصول: اگر جنس تبدیل ہو جائے تو کمی زیادتی کیساتھ خرید و فروخت جائز ہے۔
Chapter of Sarf
He (al-Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him: Sarf is a sale when each of the two counter-values is from the category of prices (gold/silver). So if one sells silver for silver, or gold for gold, it is not permissible except like for like, even if they differ in quality and craftsmanship. And it is necessary to take possession of both counter-values before parting.
[Then proofs from hadith]
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage defines sarf (currency exchange) and states its rulings. Sarf is a sale where both items exchanged are from the class of prices (thamān), i.e., gold and silver. The key conditions: when exchanging like metals (gold for gold, silver for silver), the quantities must be equal by weight regardless of quality or craftsmanship; any excess is ribā (usury). Additionally, both parties must take possession before parting company (i.e., the exchange must be spot). The passage then provides several hadith proofs: the famous hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri listing six ribawi items and commanding like for like and hand to hand; the hadith of Abu Huraira about selling dates of different quality, where the Prophet instructed to sell the inferior dates for dirhams and then buy superior dates with those dirhams; and the hadith of Bara' and Zayd forbidding selling gold for silver on credit. The Urdu usul notes state: 'For ribawi goods, if the commodity and price are the same type, quality (good or bad) is not considered'; and 'If the type changes, selling with excess or deficiency is permissible.'

Key Terms
الصَّرْف (al-sarf): A sale where both counter-values are from the category of prices (gold or silver), i.e., currency exchange.
الأثمان (al-athmān): Prices, specifically gold and silver (the original currencies).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a seller gives 10g of silver and receives 10g of silver, but the seller delivers the silver one hour after the buyer has already left?
A) Permissible because the weights are equal.
B) Permissible if they agree to defer delivery.
C) Not permissible because possession must occur before parting.
D) Not permissible because the weights are unequal.

Key Takeaway
In sarf, same-metal exchanges require exact weight equality and immediate hand-to-hand delivery, regardless of quality.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Conditions for Valid Sarf: Same-Genus and Different-Genus Currency Exchange
Al-Quduri's matn on sarf with hadith proofs and usul principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sarf transaction and apply them to distinguish between valid and invalid exchanges of gold, silver, and other currencies.

Core Idea
Same-species currency exchange requires equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery; otherwise, it is riba.

This lesson unpacks Al-Quduri's concise matn on sarf (currency exchange), a critical fiqh topic in trade. You will learn the precise conditions that make a sarf contract valid or void, backed by clear hadith evidence. Understanding these rules prevents falling into riba, a major sin.

Guided Path
1
Define Sarf and Identify the Genus Condition
Start with the definition: sarf is a sale where both countervalues are from the genus of currencies (athman – gold, silver, money). Identify whether the two items are of the same genus (e.g., gold for gold) or different genera (e.g., gold for silver). The ruling branches from this.
The genus condition determines which additional conditions apply.
2
List Conditions for Same-Genus Sarf
When the genus is the same (e.g., silver for silver), two wajib conditions must be present: (1) equality in weight (mithlan bi mithl), regardless of quality or craftsmanship, and (2) hand-to-hand delivery (yadan bi yad) before the parties separate. If either is missing, the contract becomes batil (void) due to riba.
Equality is measured by weight, not value.
3
Apply the Same-Genus Rule to the Provided Hadith
Examine the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver... like for like, hand to hand.' Observe how the Prophet explicitly prohibits increase ('whoever increases or asks for increase commits riba'). Connect this wording to the wajib conditions derived in step 2.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalalah in meaning for Hanafis.
4
State Conditions for Different-Genus Sarf
When the genera differ (e.g., gold for silver), only hand-to-hand delivery (taqabud) is wajib; disparity in weight is permissible. However, if the parties separate before both countervalues are taken, the contract becomes void (batil).
This is supported by the hadith of Abu Bakrah and the principle: 'If the genus changes, trade with increase is permissible.'
5
Analyze the Mixed-Goods Case and the Sword Example
Apply the above principles to the scenario of a silver-plated sword sold for 100 dirhams when the plating is worth 50 dirhams. The ruling: payment of 50 dirhams is valid as the portion for silver, even without specification, because the silver component must be exchanged weight-for-weight, and the rest can be bartered. This illustrates how sarf rules interact with mixed items.
The hadith of Fadalah (separation of gold from necklace) reinforces this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الصَّرْفِ
قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: الصَّرْفُ هُوَ الْبَيْعُ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عِوَضَيْهِ مِنْ جِنْسِ الْأَثْمَانِ. فَإِنْ بَاعَ فِضَّةً بِفِضَّةٍ، أَوْ ذَهَبًا بِذَهَبٍ لَمْ يَجُزْ إِلَّا مِثْلًا بِمِثْلٍ وَإِنِ اخْتَلَفَا فِي الْجَوْدَةِ وَالصَّنَاعَةِ، وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ قَبْضِ الْعِوَضَيْنِ قَبْلَ الِافْتِرَاقِ.
وجه الحديث: عن أبي سعيد الخدري، قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والبر بالبر والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والملح بالملح مثلاً بمثل يدا بيد، فمن زاد أو استزاد فقد أربى، الآخذ والمعطي فيه سواء) (سنن الترمذي، باب الصرف وبيع الذهب بالورق نقداً، رقم 1584؟) (صحيح البخاري، باب بيع الفضة بالفضة، رقم 2176).
وجه الحديث: عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه: أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم استعمل رجلاً على خيبر، فجاءه بتمر جنيب، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: أكل تمر خيبر هكذا؟ قال: لا والله يا رسول الله، إنا لنأخذ الصاع من هذا بالصاعين، والصاعين بالثلاثة. فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا تفعل، بع الجمع بالدراهم، ثم ابتع بالدراهم جنيباً. (صحيح البخاري، باب إذا أراد بيع تمر بتمر خير منه، رقم 2201)
وجه الحديث: عن البراء بن عازب وزيد بن أرقم رضي الله عنهما عن الصرف، فكل واحد منهما يقول: هذا خير مني، فكلاهما يقول: نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن بيع الذهب بالورق ديناً. (صحيح البخاري، باب بيع الورق بالذهب نسيئة، رقم 2180/ صحيح مسلم، باب النهي عن بيع الورق بالذهب ديناً، رقم 1589)
اصول: اموال ربویہ میں مبیع اور ثمن ایک ہی جنس کا ہو تو عمدہ اور ردی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔
اصول: اگر جنس تبدیل ہو جائے تو کمی زیادتی کیساتھ خرید و فروخت جائز ہے۔

وَإِذَا بَاعَ الذَّهَبَ بِالْفِضَّةِ جَازَ التَّفَاضُلُ وَوَجَبَ التَّقَابُضُ، وَإِنِ افْتَرَقَا فِي الصَّرْفِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِ الْعِوَضَيْنِ أَوْ أَحَدِهِمَا بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ. وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي ثَمَنِ الصَّرْفِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ. وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الذَّهَبِ بِالْفِضَّةِ مُجَازَفَةً. وَمَنْ بَاعَ سَيْفًا مُحَلًّى بِمِائَةِ دِرْهَمٍ وَحِلْيَتُهُ خَمْسُونَ دِرْهَمًا، فَدَفَعَ مِنْ ثَمَنِهِ خَمْسِينَ دِرْهَمًا جَازَ الْبَيْعُ وَكَانَ الْمَقْبُوضُ حِصَّةَ الْفِضَّةِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُبَيِّنْ ذَلِكَ. وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا قَالَ: خُذْ هَذِهِ الْخَمْسِينَ مِنْ ثَمَنِهِمَا.
وجه الحديث: عن عبد الرحمن بن أبي بكرة عن أبيه رضي الله عنه قال: نهى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الفضة بالفضة، والذهب بالذهب إلا سواء بسواء، وأمرنا أن نبتاع الذهب بالفضة كيف شئنا، والفضة بالذهب كيف شئنا. (صحيح البخاري، باب بيع الذهب بالورق يدا بيد، رقم 2182/ صحيح مسلم، باب الصرف وبيع الذهب بالورق نقداً، رقم 1587)
وجه الحديث: عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من ابتاع طعاماً فلا يبعه حتى يقبضه. (صحيح مسلم، باب بطلان بيع المبيع قبل القبض، رقم 1525)
وجه الحديث: عن عبادة بن الصامت ...: فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف، فبيعوا كيف شئتم إذا كان يدا بيد. (صحيح مسلم، باب الصرف وبيع الذهب بالورق نقداً، 1587/ صحيح البخاري، باب بيع الذهب بالورق يدا بيد، 2182)
وجه الحديث: سمعت فضالة بن عبيد الأنصاري يقول: أتي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو بخيبر بقلادة فيها خرز وذهب وهي من المغانم تباع، فأمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالذهب الذي في القلادة فنزع وحده، ثم قال لهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: الذهب بالذهب وزناً بوزن. (صحيح مسلم، باب بيع القلادة فيها خرز وذهب، 1591)
اصول: اگر جنس متفرق ہوں یعنی الگ الگ جنس کے مبیع اور ثمن ہو تو اٹکل سے بیع جائز ہے۔
اصول: سونا یا چاندی میں دوسری دھات شامل ہو تب بھی اصلی سونا چاندی کو برابر کر کے بیچنا ہو گا، ربوا سے بچنے کے لئے، نیز کم از کم چاندی پر مجلس میں قبضہ ضروری ہو گا ورنہ بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
Chapter of Sarf. He (al-Quduri) said, may Allah have mercy on him: Sarf is sale when each of the two countervalues is from the genus of currencies. So if one sells silver for silver, or gold for gold, it is not permissible except like for like, even if they differ in quality and craftsmanship, and it is necessary to take possession of both countervalues before separation. Evidence of the hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... (hadith texts). Principles: In ribawi goods, if the commodity and price are of the same genus, then quality and low quality are not considered. Principle: If the genus changes, then buying and selling with increase or decrease is permissible. And if one sells gold for silver, disparity is permissible and hand-to-hand delivery is obligatory, and if they separate in the sarf before taking possession of both countervalues or one of them, the contract becomes void. And it is not permissible to dispose of the price of sarf before taking possession of it. And it is permissible to sell gold for silver by estimation. And whoever sells a sword plated with one hundred dirhams while its plating is fifty dirhams, and he pays fifty dirhams of its price, the sale is valid and what is taken is considered the portion of silver, even if he did not specify that. Similarly, if he says: take these fifty from its price. Evidence... Principles: If the genera are different, i.e., the commodity and price are of different genera, then sale by estimation is permissible. Principle: If gold or silver contains another metal, then the actual gold or silver must be sold weight for weight to avoid riba, and at least possession of silver in the session is necessary, otherwise the sale becomes corrupt.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is Al-Quduri's matn on the chapter of sarf (currency exchange) accompanied by hadith evidence and usul principles. Sarf is defined as a sale where both countervalues are currencies (gold, silver, or money). The first ruling: when selling gold for gold or silver for silver, equality in weight is mandatory regardless of quality; both must be delivered hand-to-hand before separation. The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and others establish this principle, and the story of Abu Hurayrah about dates reinforces the prohibition of excess in same-genre ribawi items. The second ruling: when selling gold for silver (different genera), disparity in quantity is allowed, but hand-to-hand delivery is still required; if the parties separate before full possession, the contract becomes void. This is supported by the hadith of Abu Bakrah and the principle that different genera allow freedom in quantity. The third ruling: it is not permissible to use the price received in sarf before taking possession, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas about selling food before receipt. The fourth ruling: selling gold for silver by estimation (guesstimate without weighing) is permissible, as per the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit. The fifth ruling: if a sword with a silver hilt is sold for a lump sum, and part of the price is paid in silver for the hilt, the sale is valid and the silver taken is considered as payment for the silver component; this is based on the story of the necklace from Fadalah ibn Ubayd, where the gold was separated and sold weight-for-weight. The usul principles summarize: for ribawi goods of the same genus, quality differences are ignored; for different genera, disparity is allowed; for gold/silver mixed with other metals, the pure metal must be exchanged equally.

Key Terms
الصَّرْف (al-sarf): A sale where both countervalues are from the genus of currencies (gold, silver, or money).
الرِّبَا (al-ribā): Unlawful increase in exchange of same-genus ribawi goods, prohibited in sarf transactions.
التَّقَابُضُ (al-taqābuḍ): Hand-to-hand delivery (taking possession) of both countervalues in the transaction session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone sells 10 grams of gold for 12 grams of gold, what is the ruling?
A) Valid because gold is gold.
B) Invalid (riba) because same species must be equal in weight and hand-to-hand.
C) Valid if hand-to-hand delivery is made.
D) Invalid only if it is deferred.

Key Takeaway
In sarf, same-genus exchange requires equality in weight and hand-to-hand delivery; different-genus requires only hand-to-hand, and disparity is allowed.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Core Rulings of Sarf (Gold for Silver Exchange)
Presents three core rules of sarf with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three core rulings of sarf according to the Hanafi school: permissibility of inequality for different species, obligation of hand-to-hand delivery, and prohibition of disposal before possession.

Core Idea
In sarf, hand-to-hand delivery is always required; inequality is allowed only when species differ.

This lesson introduces the foundational rules of the sarf contract as stated by al-Quduri. These rules, derived from authentic hadith, govern the exchange of gold and silver with specific conditions to ensure the transaction complies with the Sunnah. We will examine each ruling and its prophetic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the passage carefully. It presents three sequential rules: (a) when selling gold for silver, inequality is allowed but hand-to-hand delivery is obligatory, (b) if the parties separate before taking possession of both counter-values, the contract becomes void, and (c) it is not permissible to dispose of the price before possession. Additionally, selling by estimation (mujazafah) is permitted.
Focus on the condition of taqabud (hand-to-hand delivery) as it is central to all three.
2
Understand the condition of taqabud
Taqabud means mutual physical or constructive possession in the same sitting. The Hanafi school requires this in every sarf transaction. If the parties separate before complete possession, the contract becomes void (batil).
Constructive possession includes taking control even if physical transfer is delayed due to valid reason.
3
Distinguish tafadul for same vs different species
When selling gold for silver (different species), inequality in quantity or weight is permissible. But when exchanging same species (gold for gold, silver for silver), equality is required as per the hadith. This distinction is critical for riba avoidance.
Tafadul is prohibited for same species to prevent riba al-fadl.
4
Connect the first proof to the ruling
The hadith from Abdur Rahman ibn Abi Bakra (Bukhari 2182, Muslim 1587) explicitly states: '...sell gold for silver as you wish, hand to hand.' This directly proves the permissibility of inequality for different species and the necessity of hand-to-hand delivery.
This hadith also prohibits equality when species are the same, which is not the focus here.
5
Apply the second and third proofs
The second hadith (Ibn Abbas, Muslim 1525) prohibits selling food before possession; by qiyas, it forbids disposing of the price in sarf before receipt. The third hadith (Ubada ibn al-Samit, Bukhari 2182) allows transacting different species 'as you wish, hand to hand,' confirming the first ruling and the validation of estimation.
These proofs reinforce the primary conditions of sarf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الصَّرْفِ
وَإِذَا بَاعَ الذَّهَبَ بِالْفِضَّةِ جَازَ التَّفَاضُلُ وَوَجَبَ التَّقَابُضُ، وَإِنِ افْتَرَقَا فِي الصَّرْفِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِ الْعِوَضَيْنِ أَوْ أَحَدِهِمَا بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي ثَمَنِ الصَّرْفِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ، وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الذَّهَبِ بِالْفِضَّةِ مُجَازَفَةً.
وَجْهٌ (١): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ أَبِي بَكْرَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: نَهَى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ الْفِضَّةِ بِالْفِضَّةِ، وَالذَّهَبِ بِالذَّهَبِ، إِلَّا سَوَاءً بِسَوَاءٍ، وَأَمَرَنَا أَنْ نَبْتَاعَ الذَّهَبَ بِالْفِضَّةِ كَيْفَ شِئْنَا، وَالْفِضَّةَ بِالذَّهَبِ كَيْفَ شِئْنَا. (بخاري: ٢١٨٢، مسلم: ١٥٨٧)
وَجْهٌ (١): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي ثَمَنِ الصَّرْفِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: مَنِ ابْتَاعَ طَعَامًا فَلَا يَبِعْهُ حَتَّى يَقْبِضَهُ. (مسلم: ١٥٢٥)
وَجْهٌ (١): الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الذَّهَبِ بِالْفِضَّةِ مُجَازَفَةً: عَنْ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ الصَّامِتِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: فَإِذَا اخْتَلَفَتْ هَذِهِ الْأَصْنَافُ، فَبِيعُوا كَيْفَ شِئْتُمْ إِذَا كَانَ يَدًا بِيَدٍ. (مسلم: ١٥٨٧، بخاري: ٢١٨٢)
Chapter of Sarf. When one sells gold for silver, inequality is permissible and hand-to-hand delivery is obligatory. If they separate in the exchange before taking possession of both counter-values or one of them, the contract becomes void. It is not permissible to dispose of the price of sarf before taking possession of it. And it is permissible to sell gold for silver by estimation (mujazafah). Proof (1) for the ruling: ... Proof (2) ... Proof (3) ...
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage states the basic rules of sarf (exchange of gold and silver) from Al-Quduri's matn. The first ruling: when gold is sold for silver, inequality (tafadul) is allowed because they are different species (jins), but hand-to-hand delivery (taqabud) in the same sitting is obligatory. If the parties separate before complete possession, the contract becomes void (batil). The second ruling: it is forbidden to use the price (e.g., sell it) before receiving it. The third ruling: selling by estimation (mujazafah) without exact weight is permissible when the species differ. The hadiths provide proof: the first hadith (from Abdur Rahman ibn Abi Bakra) shows that gold for silver is allowed with inequality, but same species must be equal. The second hadith (Ibn Abbas) prohibits selling before possession. The third hadith (Ubada ibn al-Samit) allows selling as desired when species differ as long as hand-to-hand.

Key Terms
الصرف (al-sarf): Exchange of gold and silver (or their representative coins) as counter-values, with specific conditions.
التَّفَاضُل (al-tafadul): Inequality in quantity or weight between the two counter-values in a sarf transaction.
التَّقَابُض (al-taqabud): Mutual physical or constructive possession of the counter-values in the same sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if two parties in a sarf transaction separate before taking possession of one of the counter-values?
A) The contract remains valid but requires re-delivery.
B) The contract becomes void (batil).
C) The contract is suspended until possession.
D) The contract becomes fasid (defective).

Key Takeaway
In sarf, immediate hand-to-hand delivery is mandatory; inequality is allowed only when species differ.

Rulings on Mixed Metal Items: Sword and Silver Vessel
Extends sarf rules to items containing gold/silver mixed with other materials

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for sarf when items contain a mixture of ribawi and non-ribawi substances, and explain the khiyar option for partial istihqaq.

Core Idea
Mixture of ribawi and non-ribawi requires immediate possession of the ribawi part; otherwise the sale is void for that part.

This passage extends the rules of sarf (exchange of ribawi items) to cases where an item contains both silver (ribawi) and other materials, such as a sword with silver plating or a silver vessel. The key principle: the ribawi portion must be possessed hand-to-hand before separation; otherwise the contract is void for that portion. We'll also examine the khiyar (option) when a third party claims part of the item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
The passage presents three scenarios: a sword with silver plating (hilya), a silver vessel, and a silver nugget. Each has different rulings based on whether the item is mixed or pure.
The sword has a silver component that is separate; the vessel is entirely silver; the nugget is pure silver.
2
Distinguish between mixed and pure
For the sword and vessel (mixed or not pure), partial possession creates a partnership; for the nugget (pure silver), no khiyar is given if part is claimed.
The khiyar applies only when the item is a composite; pure silver items do not grant an option.
3
Apply the principle of possession
In sarf, ribawi items must be possessed before separation. If only partial payment is made, the contract is valid for the paid portion and void for the unpaid portion; the item becomes jointly owned.
If the silver can be removed without harm, the sale for the non-ribawi part (e.g., the sword) remains valid.
4
Extract the hadith proof
The hadith of Fadala ibn Ubayd shows that when gold is mixed with beads, the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the gold to be separated and then exchanged weight for weight. This proves that mixed ribawi items must be separated and possessed individually.
The proof is a hadith ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ بَاعَ سَيْفًا مُحَلًّى بِمِائَةِ دِرْهَمٍ، وَحِلْيَتُهُ خَمْسُونَ دِرْهَمًا، فَدَفَعَ مِنْ ثَمَنِهِ خَمْسِينَ دِرْهَمًا جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَكَانَ الْمَقْبُوضُ حِصَّةَ الْفِضَّةِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يُبَيِّنْ ذَلِكَ. وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا قَالَ: خُذْ هَذِهِ الْخَمْسِينَ مِنْ ثَمَنِهِ. فَإِنْ لَمْ يَتَقَابَضَا حَتَّى افْتَرَقَا بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ فِي الْحِلْيَةِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ يَتَخَلَّصُ بِغَيْرِ ضَرَرٍ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ فِي السَّيْفِ وَبَطَلَ فِي الْحِلْيَةِ. وَمَنْ بَاعَ إِنَاءَ فِضَّةٍ، ثُمَّ افْتَرَقَا وَقَدْ قَبَضَ بَعْضَ ثَمَنِهِ بَطَلَ الْبَيْعُ فِيمَا لَمْ يَقْبِضْ، وَصَحَّ فِيمَا قَبَضَ، وَكَانَ الْإِنَاءُ شَرِكَةً بَيْنَهُمَا. وَإِنِ اسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُ الْإِنَاءِ كَانَ الْمُشْتَرِي بِالْخِيَارِ: إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ الْبَاقِيَ بِحِصَّتِهِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ. وَمَنْ بَاعَ نُقْرَةَ فِضَّةٍ فَاسْتُحِقَّ بَعْضُهَا أُخِذَ مَا بَقِيَ بِحِصَّتِهِ وَلَا خِيَارَ لَهُ.
وَجْهٌ: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: سَمِعْتُ فَضَالَةَ بْنَ عُبَيْدٍ الْأَنْصَارِيَّ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ يَقُولُ: أُتِيَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ بِخَيْبَرَ بِقِلَادَةٍ فِيهَا خَرَزٌ وَذَهَبٌ، وَهِيَ مِنَ الْمَغَانِمِ تُبَاعُ، فَأَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالذَّهَبِ الَّذِي فِي الْقِلَادَةِ فَنُزِعَ وَحْدَهُ، ثُمَّ قَالَ لَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: الذَّهَبُ بِالذَّهَبِ وَزْنًا بِوَزْنٍ. (مسلم: ١٥٩١)
Whoever sells a sword plated with a hundred dirhams, and its plating is fifty dirhams, and he pays fifty dirhams of its price, the sale is valid and what is taken is the portion of the silver, even if he does not specify that. Similarly, if he says: take this fifty from its price. If they do not take possession until they separate, the contract is void regarding the plating. If it can be separated without harm, the sale is valid for the sword and void for the plating. Whoever sells a vessel of silver, then they separate after he has taken possession of part of its price, the sale is void for what was not taken and valid for what was taken, and the vessel becomes a partnership between them. If part of the vessel is claimed by a rightful owner, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes the remainder at its share, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Whoever sells a silver nugget and part of it is claimed, the remainder is taken at its share and he has no option. Proof: Hadith of Fadala ibn Ubayd...
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents two cases: a sword with silver plating and a silver vessel. Both involve items containing silver (ribawi) and other materials. The first ruling: if someone sells a sword whose plating contains silver worth fifty dirhams, and the price is one hundred dirhams, and he pays only fifty dirhams before separation, the sale is valid and the fifty dirhams are considered as payment for the silver portion. This is because the silver must be possessed hand-to-hand. If they separate without full possession, the contract is void specifically for the silver part (the hilya). If the silver can be removed without damage, the sword part remains valid. The second ruling: a silver vessel is entirely silver (ribawi), so if partial price is paid and then they separate, the sale is valid for the paid portion and void for the unpaid portion, creating joint ownership. If a third party proves ownership of part, the buyer has the option to take the rest at proportional price or cancel (khiyar). For a silver nugget (pure silver), if part is claimed, the buyer has no option; he must take the remainder at share. The hadith from Fadala shows the principle: when gold is mixed with other materials, it must be separated and sold weight for weight.

Key Terms
الحِلْيَة (al-hilya): Silver plating or ornament on an item like a sword.
الخِيَار (al-khiyar): Option to annul or confirm the sale when part is claimed by a third party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A silver vessel is sold, partial payment made, and the parties separate. What is the status of the vessel?
A) The entire sale becomes void.
B) The sale is valid for the paid part, and they become co-owners of the vessel.
C) The buyer must pay the remaining price immediately.
D) The seller can cancel the sale.

Key Takeaway
In a mixed ribawi item, immediate possession of the ribawi portion is required; otherwise the sale is void for that portion, and partial possession creates joint ownership.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Rulings on Mixed Coins and Ghallah Dirhams
Rulings on mixed dirham/dinar exchanges and ghallah coins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for exchanging mixed dirhams and dinars, and explain the treatment of debased coins based on majority metal content.

Core Idea
Mixed coins are treated according to majority metal; debased dirhams are considered a different species.

This passage from al-Quduri outlines how to handle transactions involving coins of varying purity. The Hanafi school classifies coins based on their predominant metal, applying riba rules to silver/gold and commodity rules to base metals. Understanding this classification is essential for avoiding riba in coin exchanges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mixed coin transactions
The passage gives examples: selling two dirhams and one dinar for two dinars and one dirham, and selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar. In each, the sale is valid because each species is matched.
This is a direct application of the rule that different species can be exchanged with inequality.
2
Recognize the rule for ghallah dirhams
Ghallah dirhams are debased coins. They are considered different from sound dirhams, so they can be exchanged with inequality (e.g., one sound for one bad).
The criterion is whether they are treated as the same species in common practice.
3
Apply the majority-metal principle
If a coin's majority is silver, it is treated as silver (ribawi); if majority is copper or other base metal, it is treated as a commodity (no riba).
This principle overrides the name 'dirham' if the metal content is predominantly base.
4
Derive the implications for transactions
When selling mixed groups, each species is paired with its own; the inequality between different species is allowed, but within the same species must be equal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ بَاعَ دِرْهَمَيْنِ وَدِينَارًا بِدِينَارَيْنِ وَدِرْهَمٍ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَجُعِلَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْجِنْسَيْنِ بِالْجِنْسِ الْآخَرِ. وَمَنْ بَاعَ أَحَدَ عَشَرَ دِرْهَمًا بِعَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ وَدِينَارٍ جَازَ، وَكَانَتِ الْعَشَرَةُ مِثْلَهَا وَالدِّينَارُ بِالدِّرْهَمِ. وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دِرْهَمَيْنِ صَحِيحَيْنِ بِدِرْهَمَيْنِ غَلَّةٍ، وَدِرْهَمٍ صَحِيحٍ بِدِرْهَمٍ غَلَّةٍ. وَإِذَا كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَى الدَّرَاهِمِ الْفِضَّةَ فَهِيَ فِضَّةٌ، وَإِنْ كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَى الدَّنَانِيرِ الذَّهَبَ فَهِيَ ذَهَبٌ، وَيُعْتَبَرُ فِيهِمَا مِنْ تَحْرِيمِ التَّفَاضُلِ مَا يُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْحِيَادِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَيْهِمَا الْعِشَ أَوْ غَيْرَهُ فَلَيْسَا فِي حُكْمِ الدَّرَاهِمِ وَالدَّنَانِيرِ، وَيَكُونَانِ فِي حُكْمِ الْعُرُوضِ، فَإِذَا بِيعَتْ بِجِنْسِهَا مُتَفَاضِلًا جَازَ. وَإِذَا اشْتَرَى بِهَا سِلْعَةً، ثُمَّ كَسَدَتْ وَتَرَكَ النَّاسُ الْمُعَامَلَةَ بِهَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلِّمَهَا إِلَى الْبَائِعِ بَطَلَ الْبَيْعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ: عَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهَا يَوْمَ الْبَيْعِ. وَيَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ بِالْفُلُوسِ، فَإِنْ كَانَتْ نَافِقَةً جَازَ الْبَيْعُ بِهَا وَإِنْ لَمْ تُعَيَّنْ، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ كَاسِدَةً لَمْ يَجُزْ الْبَيْعُ بِهَا حَتَّى يُعَيِّنَهَا. وَإِذَا بَاعَ بِالْفُلُوسِ النَّافِقَةِ، ثُمَّ كَسَدَتْ بَطَلَ الْبَيْعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ. وَمَنِ اشْتَرَى شَيْئًا بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ فُلُوسًا جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَعَلَيْهِ مَا يُبَاعُ بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ مِنَ الْفُلُوسِ. وَمَنْ أَعْطَى الصَّيْرَفَ دِرْهَمًا فَقَالَ: أَعْطِنِي بِنِصْفِهِ فُلُوسًا وَبِنِصْفِهِ نِصْفًا إِلَّا حَبَّةً، فَسَدَ الْبَيْعُ فِي الْجَمِيعِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَا: جَازَ الْبَيْعُ فِي الْفُلُوسِ وَبَطَلَ فِيمَا بَقِيَ. وَلَوْ قَالَ: أَعْطِنِي دِرْهَمًا صَغِيرًا وَزْنُهُ نِصْفُ دِرْهَمٍ إِلَّا حَبَّةً، وَالْبَاقِيَ فُلُوسًا جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَكَانَتِ الْفُلُوسُ وَالنِّصْفُ إِلَّا حَبَّةً بِدِرْهَمٍ.
Whoever sells two dirhams and one dinar for two dinars and one dirham, the sale is valid, and each of the two species is considered (sold) for the other species. Whoever sells eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar, it is valid, and the ten are to be equal and the dinar for the dirham. It is permissible to sell two sound dirhams for two bad dirhams, and one sound dirham for one bad dirham. When the majority of the dirhams is silver, they are silver; when the majority of the dinars is gold, they are gold; and the prohibition of inequality is considered in them as considered in the pure ones. If the majority of them is copper or other, they are not in the ruling of dirhams and dinars, but they are in the ruling of commodities, so if sold for their own kind by inequality, it is permissible. If one buys a commodity with them, then they become out of circulation and people stop dealing with them before he delivers them to the seller, the sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: he owes their value on the day of sale. Sale with copper coins (fulus) is permissible: if they are accepted (nāfiqa), sale with them is valid even if unspecified; if they are out of circulation (kāsida), sale with them is not valid until he specifies them. If one sells with accepted fulus, then they become out of circulation, the sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa. Whoever buys something with half a dirham's worth of fulus, the sale is valid, and he owes what is sold for half a dirham of fulus. Whoever gives a moneychanger a dirham and says: give me in half of it fulus and in half of it half (dirham) except a grain, the entire sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the sale is valid for the fulus and void for the remainder. If he says: give me a small dirham whose weight is half a dirham except a grain, and the remainder fulus, the sale is valid and the fulus and the half except a grain are (exchanged) for a dirham.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings about mixed coins and fulus. First, when selling mixed groups of dirhams and dinars (e.g., two dirhams and one dinar for two dinars and one dirham), the sale is valid because each species is matched with its own kind. Second, selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar is valid: the ten dirhams are equal to ten, and the dinar is sold for one dirham (since they are different species). Third, selling good dirhams for bad dirhams (same species) is not allowed if they are pure silver, but here they are considered different due to quality? Actually, they are same species, so inequality is not allowed? The text says 'sound' (saheeh) and 'ghallah' (bad, possibly debased). The ruling says it is permissible, which may be based on the fact that they are considered different if the bad ones are not pure. Alternatively, it might be that ghallah are considered different 'urf. So caution: this needs explanation. Then the general rule: if the majority metal is silver, it is treated as silver (ribawi); if majority is copper or other, it is treated as a commodity (no riba). Then the issue of fulus (copper coins): if they are accepted (nāfiqa, in circulation), they can be used as price without specification; if they are out of circulation (kāsida), they must be specified like commodities. If one buys with fulus that are nāfiqa at the time of sale but become kāsida before delivery, the sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa (because the price is no longer valid). Abu Yusuf says the buyer owes their value at the time of sale. Then a case: buying something with half a dirham's worth of fulus is valid, and the buyer owes the determined amount of fulus. Finally, a case of dealing with a moneychanger: asking for half dirham in fulus and half in a coin minus a grain. This creates uncertainty (gharar) because the amount of the coin is unknown, so Abu Hanifa says the whole transaction is void. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the fulus part is valid but the coin part is void. If the request is specific (a small dirham of known weight), then the sale is valid.

Key Terms
الغَلَّة (al-ghallah): Bad or debased dirhams (coins), perhaps ones that are not pure silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rule for exchanging sound dirhams for bad dirhams (ghallah)?
A) Not allowed because they are same species.
B) Allowed because they are considered different.
C) Allowed only if weight is equal.
D) Not allowed unless the difference is minor.

Key Takeaway
Coins are classified by their majority metal; debased dirhams are a different species, allowing unequal exchange.

Rulings on Fulus (Copper Coins) and Moneychanger Transactions
Rulings on fulus (copper coins) as currency, and moneychanger case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on sale with fulus and the effect of them becoming out of circulation, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute in the moneychanger case.

Core Idea
Fulus are commodities; if they become out of circulation before delivery, the sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage continues with copper coins (fulus), which are treated as commodities. Their legal status depends on market acceptance. The case of the moneychanger involves uncertainty (gharar) that leads to different opinions among the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between nāfiqa and kāsida fulus
Nāfiqa fulus are accepted in circulation; they can be used as price without specification. Kāsida fulus are out of circulation; they must be specified like any commodity.
This affects the validity of the sale.
2
Apply the rule for fulus becoming out of circulation after sale
If fulus are nāfiqa at the time of sale but become kāsida before delivery, Abu Hanifa rules the sale void (batil) because the price is no longer valid. Abu Yusuf says the buyer owes the value at time of sale.
The ikhtilaf is on the effect of subsequent change in status.
3
Analyze the moneychanger case
A man gives a dirham and asks for fulus and a coin with a deduction (half dirham except a grain). This creates uncertainty in the coin amount, leading to gharar.
Abu Hanifa voids the entire transaction; the Sahibayn save the fulus part.
4
Derive the ruling for a specific request
If the request is for a known small dirham of specific weight, the sale is valid because there is no uncertainty.

وَمَنْ بَاعَ دِرْهَمَيْنِ وَدِينَارًا بِدِينَارَيْنِ وَدِرْهَمٍ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَجُعِلَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْجِنْسَيْنِ بِالْجِنْسِ الْآخَرِ. وَمَنْ بَاعَ أَحَدَ عَشَرَ دِرْهَمًا بِعَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ وَدِينَارٍ جَازَ، وَكَانَتِ الْعَشَرَةُ مِثْلَهَا وَالدِّينَارُ بِالدِّرْهَمِ. وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ دِرْهَمَيْنِ صَحِيحَيْنِ بِدِرْهَمَيْنِ غَلَّةٍ، وَدِرْهَمٍ صَحِيحٍ بِدِرْهَمٍ غَلَّةٍ. وَإِذَا كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَى الدَّرَاهِمِ الْفِضَّةَ فَهِيَ فِضَّةٌ، وَإِنْ كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَى الدَّنَانِيرِ الذَّهَبَ فَهِيَ ذَهَبٌ، وَيُعْتَبَرُ فِيهِمَا مِنْ تَحْرِيمِ التَّفَاضُلِ مَا يُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْحِيَادِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَيْهِمَا الْعِشَ أَوْ غَيْرَهُ فَلَيْسَا فِي حُكْمِ الدَّرَاهِمِ وَالدَّنَانِيرِ، وَيَكُونَانِ فِي حُكْمِ الْعُرُوضِ، فَإِذَا بِيعَتْ بِجِنْسِهَا مُتَفَاضِلًا جَازَ. وَإِذَا اشْتَرَى بِهَا سِلْعَةً، ثُمَّ كَسَدَتْ وَتَرَكَ النَّاسُ الْمُعَامَلَةَ بِهَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلِّمَهَا إِلَى الْبَائِعِ بَطَلَ الْبَيْعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ: عَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهَا يَوْمَ الْبَيْعِ. وَيَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ بِالْفُلُوسِ، فَإِنْ كَانَتْ نَافِقَةً جَازَ الْبَيْعُ بِهَا وَإِنْ لَمْ تُعَيَّنْ، وَإِنْ كَانَتْ كَاسِدَةً لَمْ يَجُزْ الْبَيْعُ بِهَا حَتَّى يُعَيِّنَهَا. وَإِذَا بَاعَ بِالْفُلُوسِ النَّافِقَةِ، ثُمَّ كَسَدَتْ بَطَلَ الْبَيْعُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ. وَمَنِ اشْتَرَى شَيْئًا بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ فُلُوسًا جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَعَلَيْهِ مَا يُبَاعُ بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ مِنَ الْفُلُوسِ. وَمَنْ أَعْطَى الصَّيْرَفَ دِرْهَمًا فَقَالَ: أَعْطِنِي بِنِصْفِهِ فُلُوسًا وَبِنِصْفِهِ نِصْفًا إِلَّا حَبَّةً، فَسَدَ الْبَيْعُ فِي الْجَمِيعِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَا: جَازَ الْبَيْعُ فِي الْفُلُوسِ وَبَطَلَ فِيمَا بَقِيَ. وَلَوْ قَالَ: أَعْطِنِي دِرْهَمًا صَغِيرًا وَزْنُهُ نِصْفُ دِرْهَمٍ إِلَّا حَبَّةً، وَالْبَاقِيَ فُلُوسًا جَازَ الْبَيْعُ، وَكَانَتِ الْفُلُوسُ وَالنِّصْفُ إِلَّا حَبَّةً بِدِرْهَمٍ.
Whoever sells two dirhams and one dinar for two dinars and one dirham, the sale is valid, and each of the two species is considered (sold) for the other species. Whoever sells eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar, it is valid, and the ten are to be equal and the dinar for the dirham. It is permissible to sell two sound dirhams for two bad dirhams, and one sound dirham for one bad dirham. When the majority of the dirhams is silver, they are silver; when the majority of the dinars is gold, they are gold; and the prohibition of inequality is considered in them as considered in the pure ones. If the majority of them is copper or other, they are not in the ruling of dirhams and dinars, but they are in the ruling of commodities, so if sold for their own kind by inequality, it is permissible. If one buys a commodity with them, then they become out of circulation and people stop dealing with them before he delivers them to the seller, the sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: he owes their value on the day of sale. Sale with copper coins (fulus) is permissible: if they are accepted (nāfiqa), sale with them is valid even if unspecified; if they are out of circulation (kāsida), sale with them is not valid until he specifies them. If one sells with accepted fulus, then they become out of circulation, the sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa. Whoever buys something with half a dirham's worth of fulus, the sale is valid, and he owes what is sold for half a dirham of fulus. Whoever gives a moneychanger a dirham and says: give me in half of it fulus and in half of it half (dirham) except a grain, the entire sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the sale is valid for the fulus and void for the remainder. If he says: give me a small dirham whose weight is half a dirham except a grain, and the remainder fulus, the sale is valid and the fulus and the half except a grain are (exchanged) for a dirham.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings about mixed coins and fulus. First, when selling mixed groups of dirhams and dinars (e.g., two dirhams and one dinar for two dinars and one dirham), the sale is valid because each species is matched with its own kind. Second, selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar is valid: the ten dirhams are equal to ten, and the dinar is sold for one dirham (since they are different species). Third, selling good dirhams for bad dirhams (same species) is not allowed if they are pure silver, but here they are considered different due to quality? Actually, they are same species, so inequality is not allowed? The text says 'sound' (saheeh) and 'ghallah' (bad, possibly debased). The ruling says it is permissible, which may be based on the fact that they are considered different if the bad ones are not pure. Alternatively, it might be that ghallah are considered different 'urf. So caution: this needs explanation. Then the general rule: if the majority metal is silver, it is treated as silver (ribawi); if majority is copper or other, it is treated as a commodity (no riba). Then the issue of fulus (copper coins): if they are accepted (nāfiqa, in circulation), they can be used as price without specification; if they are out of circulation (kāsida), they must be specified like commodities. If one buys with fulus that are nāfiqa at the time of sale but become kāsida before delivery, the sale becomes void according to Abu Hanifa (because the price is no longer valid). Abu Yusuf says the buyer owes their value at the time of sale. Then a case: buying something with half a dirham's worth of fulus is valid, and the buyer owes the determined amount of fulus. Finally, a case of dealing with a moneychanger: asking for half dirham in fulus and half in a coin minus a grain. This creates uncertainty (gharar) because the amount of the coin is unknown, so Abu Hanifa says the whole transaction is void. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the fulus part is valid but the coin part is void. If the request is specific (a small dirham of known weight), then the sale is valid.

Key Terms
الْفُلُوس (al-fulus): Copper coins used as currency or commodity.
النَّافِقَة (al-nāfiqa): Coins that are in common circulation and accepted as currency.
الْكَاسِدَة (al-kāsida): Coins that are out of circulation and no longer accepted as currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person buys goods with fulus that are accepted (nāfiqa) at the time of sale, but before delivery the fulus become out of circulation (kāsida), what happens to the sale?
A) Sale remains valid, buyer must pay new fulus.
B) Sale becomes void.
C) Buyer must pay the value of fulus at time of sale.
D) Seller can cancel contract.

Key Takeaway
Fulus are commodities; if accepted, they can be used as price, but if they become out of circulation before delivery, the sale is void according to Abu Hanifa.

Destruction of the Pledged Item: Three Scenarios
States the rulings when the pledge perishes in the mortgagee's hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three legal outcomes when a pledge perishes in the mortgagee's hand and apply them to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A perished pledge either discharges the debt exactly, leaves excess as trust, or reduces debt leaving a remainder claim.

When a pledged item is destroyed while in the mortgagee's possession, Islamic law determines the consequences based on its value relative to the debt. This lesson presents the clear Hanafi ruling on three possible scenarios, supported by the practice of Umar and a prophetic hadith. Understanding this ruling is essential for anyone dealing with secured transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the trigger
The act is the destruction (halak) of the pledged item (rahn) while in the mortgagee's hand. Identify that the ruling depends entirely on the value at the time of destruction relative to the debt.
The mortgagee is a trustee; negligence is not assumed unless proven.
2
Learn the three scenarios
Memorize the three cases: (1) value equals debt – mortgagee is deemed to have recovered his debt; (2) value exceeds debt – the excess is a trust; (3) value is less – debt reduces by the value, and the mortgagee may claim the remainder.
The excess as trust means the mortgagee is not liable for it if it perishes without his fault.
3
Understand the legal effect
In each scenario, the ruling is a declaratory (wad'i) effect: the debt is discharged, partially discharged, or remains. Recognize that the mortgagee never owns the pledge; it is security.
This aligns with the hadith: 'The pledge is not to be withheld; its profit belongs to it and its loss is borne by it.'
4
Apply the ruling to a new case
Given a hypothetical debt and pledge value, determine which scenario applies and state the resulting legal outcome.
Practice with numbers to solidify the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا هَلَكَ فِي يَدِ الْمُرْتَنِ وَقِيمَته وَالدَّيْنُ سَوَاءٌ صَارَ مُسْتَوْفِيًا لِدَيْنِهِ حُكْمًا. وَإِنْ كَانَتْ قِيمَةُ الرَّهْنِ أَكْثَرَ فَالْفَاضِلُ أَمَانَةٌ. وَإِنْ كَانَتْ قِيمَةُ الرَّهْنِ أَقَلَّ مِنْ الدَّيْنِ سَقَطَ مِنْ الدَّيْنِ بِقَدْرِهَا وَرَجَعَ الْمُرْقَنُ بِالْفَضْلِ. وَعَنْ عُمَرَ بْنَ الخَطَّابِ قَالَ فِي الرَّجُل يُرْتَهَنُ فَيُضِيعُ: إِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَّ مِمَّا فِيهِ رَدَّ عَلَيْهِ تَمَامَ حَقِّهِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ أَكْثَرَ فَهُوَ أَمِينٌ. وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا يُغَلُ الرَّهْنُ، لَهُ غُنْمُهُ وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ.
If the pledge perishes in the hand of the mortgagee and its value and the debt are equal, he becomes having recovered his debt in a legal sense. If the pledge's value is more, the excess is a trust. If the pledge's value is less than the debt, an amount equal to it falls from the debt, and the pledgor reclaims the remainder. From Umar ibn al-Khattab regarding a man who takes a pledge and it is lost: 'If it is less than what is due, he returns the remainder of his right; if it is more, he is a trustee.' And the Messenger of Allah said: 'The pledge is not to be withheld; its profit belongs to it and its loss is borne by it.'
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental ruling from the Book of Rahn regarding the destruction of the pledged item while in the possession of the mortgagee (murtahin). The ruling covers three scenarios. First, if the value of the pledged item at the time of destruction equals the debt, the mortgagee is considered to have fully recovered his debt legally, and no further claim remains. Second, if the value exceeds the debt, the excess is considered a trust (amanah) in the hands of the mortgagee; if it perishes, he is not liable for the excess unless he is negligent. Third, if the value is less than the debt, the debt is reduced by the value of the pledge, and the mortgagee may claim the remaining balance from the pledgor. This is based on the principle that the pledge functions as security and is not owned by the mortgagee. The passage also cites the ruling of Umar (رضي الله عنه) that the mortgagee is a trustee for any excess, and the hadith that the pledge is not to be withheld; its profit belongs to it and its liability is on it.

Key Terms
الرَّهْنُ (al-rahn): A contract where property is given as security for a debt, held by the creditor.
الْمُرْتَنِ (al-murtahin): The creditor who receives the pledge as security.
الْمُرْقَنِ (al-murqin?): The pledgor (likely a typo for 'الرَّاهِن').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledged item worth 100 dirhams perishes in the mortgagee's hand, and the debt is 120 dirhams, what is the ruling?
A) The mortgagee is liable for 100 dirhams and must return it.
B) The debt is reduced by 100 dirhams, and the mortgagee can claim the remaining 20 dirhams.
C) The debt is fully discharged.
D) The mortgagee must pay 100 dirhams to the pledgor.

Key Takeaway
The perished pledge's value relative to the debt determines whether the debt is discharged, the excess is a trust, or the debt is reduced and a remainder is claimable.

Liability for Pawn and Pawn of Fungibles by Kind
Rulings on pawn destruction and fungible pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears the loss when a pawn perishes in the mortgagee's custody, and identify the ruling on pawning fungible items by kind.

Core Idea
The mortgagee is a guarantor for the pawn; if fungibles perish, their like is owed.

This lesson covers two connected rulings from our Hanafi text. First, if the pawned item is destroyed while in the mortgagee's possession, the mortgagee must compensate the pledgor. Second, it is valid to pawn fungible items such as coins, grains, and other measured or weighed goods when they are pawned by their same kind; if they perish, the mortgagee must return their equivalent (mithl), not the exact original items. These rules highlight the Hanafi view of the mortgagee's enhanced liability and the treatment of fungibles in pawn contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the Arabic text. It begins with 'فَإِذَا هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ مِنْ ضَمَانِ الْمُرْمَّن' (when it perishes in his hand, it is from the guarantee of the mortgagee) and then 'وَيَجُوزُ رَهْنُ الدَّرَاهِم... فَإِنْ رُهِنَتْ بِجِنْسِهَا وَهَلَكَتْ هَلَكَتْ مِثْلِهَا' (it is permissible to pawn dirhams, dinars, and measured/weighed items; if pawned by their kind and perish, they perish as their like). Extract these two separate legal statements.
The first ruling applies to any pawn; the second specifically to fungibles.
2
Analyze the legal consequences
Understand that in the first ruling, the mortgagee is a guarantor (ḍāmin), not merely a trustee (amīn). Therefore, if the pawn perishes for any reason in his custody, he must compensate the pledgor. In the second ruling, for fungibles (e.g., grains, coins), compensation is by delivering an equivalent amount (mithl), not the exact object, because fungibles are replaceable by their nature.
Other schools (e.g., Shafiʿi) hold the mortgagee is only liable if he is negligent, but Hanafi considers custody alone sufficient for liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ مِنْ ضَمَانِ الْمُرْمَّن وَيَجُوزُ رَهْنُ الدَّرَاهِم وَالدَّنَانِيرِ، وَالْمَكِيلَ وَالْمَوْزُونِ فَإِنْ رُهِنَتْ بِجِنْسِهَا وَهَلَكَتْ هَلَكَتْ مِثْلِهَا
When it perishes in his hand, it is from the guarantee of the mortgagee. And it is permissible to pawn dirhams and dinars, and measured and weighed items. If they are pawned by their same kind and perish, they perish as their like.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage states two distinct rulings. First: if the pawned object perishes while in the custody of the mortgagee (or trustee), the liability is on the mortgagee—meaning he must compensate the pledgor. Second: it is valid to pawn fungible items like coins, grains, and other measured/weighed goods. If such items are pawned with their own kind (e.g., gold for gold) and are destroyed, the mortgagee must return their equivalent, not the exact same coins or grain.

Key Terms
الْمُرْمَّن (al-murramman): Likely a typo for المرتهن (al-murtahin) meaning mortgagee/creditor.
الْمَكِيلَ وَالْمَوْزُونِ (al-makīl wa al-mawzūn): Items sold by measure (volume) and by weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Return the exact dates
B) Return their like in weight
C) Pay the market price
D) Nothing, as it is a trust

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee is a guarantor for the pawn, and fungibles pawned by kind are replaced with their like upon destruction.
