Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Defective Coins in Debt Repayment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on defective coin repayment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding defective coin repayment, identify the mufta bihi position, and explain its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Creditor who unknowingly spends defective coins has no recourse per Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn allow reclaiming good coins by returning defects.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute from the Quduri text. The scenario involves a creditor who accepts repayment in coins, spends them, and later discovers they were defective. Should the debtor be discharged? Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on the answer. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances textual principles with practical justice (istihsan) and which view carries authority for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the Arabic passage and identify the key facts: a creditor has a debt, takes repayment in coins of the same type, spends them, then learns those coins were defective (zuyuf).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, the creditor has no recourse—the debt is discharged. The words 'fa la shay'a lahu' indicate that he cannot reclaim anything.
His reasoning: the creditor voluntarily accepted and used the coins, so the debt is considered paid.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the creditor must return an equivalent amount of defective coins to the debtor and can then claim back the good coins (yarji'u bi al-yad). The debt is not discharged until proper coins are received.
They prioritise preventing injustice: the debtor should not benefit from paying with defective currency.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is financial: under Abu Hanifa, the creditor bears the loss; under the Sahibayn, the creditor can recover the full value.
This is a key illustration of how ikhtilaf directly affects parties' rights.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah) prefer the view of the Sahibayn as the operative position for fatwa, to avoid harm to the creditor.
This is a common pattern: the school often adopts the view that is more just and practical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ كَانَ لَهُ دَيْنٌ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ فَأَخَذَ مِنْهُ مِثْلَ دَيْنِهِ فَأَنْفَقَهُ، ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ زُيُوفًا فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ : يَرُدُّ مِثْلَ الزُّيُوفِ وَيَرْجِعُ بِالْيَادِ
Whoever has a debt against another, then takes from him the like of his debt and spends it, then knows it was defective (zuyuf), then nothing is due to him according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He returns the like of the defective coins and claims back the [good] money.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The scenario: a creditor accepts coins as repayment, spends them, then discovers they were counterfeit or defective. Abu Hanifa rules that the creditor has no claim; the debt is discharged because he voluntarily accepted and used them. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the creditor must return an equivalent amount of defective coins to the debtor and can then claim repayment with good coins. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is the view of the Sahibayn, as it avoids injustice.

Key Terms
زُيُوفًا (zuyūfan): Defective or counterfeit coins (low quality or fake).
يَرْجِعُ بِالْيَادِ (yarji'u bi al-yād): Claims back the money (the good coins); 'yad' likely refers to the original good money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, what must a creditor do after spending defective coins unknowingly?
A) Keep the defective coins and claim nothing
B) Return like defective coins and claim good ones
C) Forgive the debt
D) Give charity

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school for defective coin repayment is the Sahibayn's view, allowing the creditor to reclaim good coins after returning defects.

Pawn in Hand: No Obligation to Allow Sale Until Debt Paid
Ruling on mortgagee's right of retention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mortgagee's right of retention and identify when the pawn must be returned.

Core Idea
The mortgagee holds the pawn until the debt is paid — no forced sale before payment.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes a fundamental right of the mortgagee (murtahin) in a pawn (rahn) contract. While the pawn is in his possession, the pledgor (rahin) cannot demand that the mortgagee facilitate its sale. The mortgagee's right of retention (habs) continues until the debt is fully satisfied. Only then must the pawn be surrendered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the object
Recognize the mortgagee (holder of pawn), the pledgor (debtor), and the pawn itself (rahn). The text assumes the pawn is already in the mortgagee's hand.
In Hanafi fiqh, possession (qabd) is a condition for the pawn contract to be binding.
2
Determine the ruling on sale
The text states that the mortgagee is not obliged (laysa alayhi) to enable the pledgor to sell the pawn. This means the mortgagee has a right to refuse permission to sell.
This is a negation of obligation, not a prohibition on permissibility; the mortgagee may voluntarily allow sale if he wishes.
3
Identify the condition triggering release
The mortgagee's obligation to return the pawn arises only after the debt is paid in full. The phrase 'from its price' (min thanihi) indicates that the debt is typically discharged from the proceeds of selling the pawn.
The debt can also be paid from other sources; once paid, the pawn must be returned.
4
Understand the consequence of payment
After the debt is paid, the text says 'it is said to him: Hand over the pawn to him.' This is a command (amr), indicating the mortgagee must now surrender possession.
If the mortgagee refuses after payment, he becomes a transgressor (ghasib).
5
Analyze the phrase 'min thanihi'
Literally 'from its price,' it means the debt is to be paid from the sale proceeds of the pawn if it is sold. But the mortgagee is not compelled to sell; he may wait for payment from other means.
This phrase also implies that the pawn is specifically tied to the debt (al-rahn bi al-dayn).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ الرَّهْنُ فِي يَدِهِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُمَكِّنَهُ مِنْ بَيْعِهِ حَتَّى يَقْضِيَهُ الدَّيْنَ مِنْ ثَنِهِ فَإِذَا قَضَاهُ الدَّيْنَ قِيلَ لَهُ سَلِّمُ الرَّهْنَ إِلَيْهِ
And if the pawn is in his hand, he is not obliged to enable him to sell it until he pays him the debt from its price. Then when he pays him the debt, he is told: Hand over the pawn to him.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This ruling clarifies the mortgagee's right of retention. While the pawn is in his possession, the pledgor cannot demand that the mortgagee allow its sale. Only after the debt is paid—from the proceeds of the pawn's sale or otherwise—must the mortgagee release the pawn. The phrase 'from its price' suggests the debt is typically paid from the sale of the pawn itself.

Key Terms
مِنْ ثَنِهِ (min thanihi): From its price; i.e., the proceeds of sale of the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must the mortgagee hand over the pawn to the pledgor?
A) Immediately upon request
B) After the debt is paid
C) After a court order
D) After one year

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee has the right to retain the pawn until the debt is paid in full; forced sale is not permitted before payment.

Pledgor's Unauthorized Sale of Pawn: Suspended Contract
Ruling on suspended sale of pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pledgor's unauthorized sale of the pawn and identify the two ways the sale becomes valid.

Core Idea
A pledgor's sale of pawn without permission is suspended, not void, and can become valid by ratification or debt payment.

In a pawn contract, the mortgagee has a right over the pawn as security. If the pledgor sells the pawn without permission, the sale is not automatically null. The Hanafi school treats it as mawquf (suspended), pending either the mortgagee's consent or the pledgor's repayment of the debt. This lesson explains the ruling and the rationale behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
Recognize that the pledgor (owner) sells the pawn (collateral) to a third party without the mortgagee's (creditor's) permission.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The sale is suspended (mawquf)—neither immediately valid nor void. It is a conditional contract awaiting a subsequent event.
Mawquf is a distinct Hanafi category.
3
List the two validation paths
1) The mortgagee ratifies the sale after it occurs. 2) The pledgor pays off the debt, thereby removing the mortgagee's interest in the pawn.
Both options make the sale fully valid and binding.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i view
The Shafi'i school considers such a sale fasid (invalid) until ratification, whereas Hanafi holds it as mawquf, which is a valid contract that only needs permission to take full effect.
The thamarah al-khilaf lies in the status of the contract before ratification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا بَاعَ الرَّاهِنُ الرَّهْنَ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ الْمُرْتَينِ فَالْبَيْعُ مَوْقُوفٌ فَإِنْ أَجَازَهُ الْمُرْتَنُ جَازَ وَإِنْ قَضَاهُ الرَّاهِنُ دَيْنَهُ جَازَ أَيْضًا
When the pledgor sells the pawn without the permission of the mortgagee, the sale is suspended. If the mortgagee ratifies it, it is valid; and if the pledgor pays his debt, it also becomes valid.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This ruling deals with an unauthorized sale of the pawn by the pledgor. Since the mortgagee has a right over the pawn, the sale is not automatically void but suspended (mawquf). It can become valid in two ways: either the mortgagee explicitly gives his consent after the sale, or the pledgor pays off the debt, thereby removing the mortgagee's interest. In both cases, the sale becomes effective and binding.

Key Terms
مَوْقُوفٌ (mawqūf): Suspended; a contract whose validity depends on later ratification or fulfilment of a condition.
رَهْن (rahn): A pawn or collateral; a contract where property is given as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How can an unauthorized sale of pawn become valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only by the mortgagee's ratification
B) Only by the pledgor paying the debt
C) Either by ratification or debt payment
D) It never becomes valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats a pledgor's unauthorized sale of pawn as suspended (mawquf), which becomes valid upon mortgagee's ratification or debt repayment.

Liability and Expenses in Pledge (Rahn)
Rulings on liability and expenses in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on liability for injury to the pawn and allocation of expenses between pawner and pledgee.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the pawner bears injury caused by his own act, while the pledgee deducts damage from the debt; expenses of custody are on the pledgee, but maintenance on the pawner.

This lesson covers the first section of Al-Quduri's chapter on pledge, establishing who bears liability for damage to the pawned item and who is responsible for its expenses. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly applying the contract of rahn in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The pawner (raahin) is the debtor who gives the pawn; the pledgee (murtahin) is the creditor who receives it as security.
Remember that ownership remains with the pawner.
2
Analyze liability for injury
If the pawner damages the pawn, he must compensate the pledgee for the reduction in value. If the pledgee damages it, the amount is deducted from his debt. If the pawn causes harm to people or property, no one is liable.
The principle is that each party is responsible for their own acts.
3
Distinguish expenses of custody vs maintenance
The rent for storing the pawn is on the pledgee because he benefits from possession. The shepherd's fee and feed are on the pawner as owner.
This prevents the pledgee from profiting at the pawner's expense.
4
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Consider: A pawned cow is housed in a rented stable. Who pays the stable rent? Who pays for the cow's feed? Refer to the passage.
These expenses are separate from the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الرَّهْنِ وَجِنَايَةُ الرَّاهِنِ عَلَى الرَّهُن مَضْمُونَةٌ وَجِنَايَةُ الْمُرْتَقِن عَلَيْهِ تَسْقُطُ مِنْ دَيْنِهِ بِقَدْرِهَا وَجِنَايَةً الرَّهْنِ عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ، وَالْمُرْكَنِ وَعَلَى أَمْوَالِهِمَا هَدَرٌ وَأَجْرَةُ الْبَيْتِ الَّذِي يُحْفَظُ فِيهِ الرَّهْنُ عَلَى الْمُرْتَقِنِ وَ أَجْرَةُ الرَّاعِي عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ وَنَفَقَةُ الرَّهْنِ عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ ١٢ وَغَاؤُهُ لِلرَّاهِنِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ فِي الدَّيْنِ وَإِذَا رَهَنَ عَيْنًا وَاحِدَةً عِنْدَ رَجُلَيْنِ بِدَيْنِ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَلَيْهِ جَازَ وَجَمِيعُهَا رَهْنٌ عِنْدَ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت الله عليه وسلم : « لَا يُغَلُّ الرَّهْنُ ، لَهُ غُنْمُهُ ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ»»،(سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ البيوع، نمبر 2919/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الرَّهْنُ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونٍ، نمبر 11219) وجه : (۱) كِتَابُ الْبُيُوع، 2921) اصول: ہر وہ شکل جس سے شی مرہون کو مرتہن کے پاس روکی جاسکے ، اور اسکے قبضہ میں رکھی جاسکے ان تمام شکلوں کی اجرت مر تہن پر لازم ہو گی۔ اصول : جہاں مرتہن کی ضرورت ہو اس کی پوری کرنے کی اجرت مر تہن پر ہوگی۔ وَالْمَضْمُونُ عَلَى كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حِصَّةُ دَيْنِهِ مِنْهَا فَإِنْ قَضَى أَحَدُهُمَا دَيْنَهُ كَانَتْ كُلُّهَا رَهْنًا فِي يَدِ الْآخَرِ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي هَا وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنْ يَرْهَنَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي بِالثَّمَنِ شَيْئًا بِعَيْنِهِ فَامْتَنَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي مِنْ تَسْلِيمِ الرَّهْنِ يُكْبَرْ عَلَيْهِ وَكَانَ الْبَائِعُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ رَضِيَ بِتَرْكِ الرَّهْنِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ فَسَخَ الْبَيْعَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَدْفَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي الثَّمَنَ حَالًا، أَوْ يَدْفَعَ قِيمَةَ الرَّهْنِ رَهْنَّا مَكَانَهُ وَلِلْمُرْقَن أَنْ يَحْفَظَ الرَّهْنَ بِنَفْسِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَخَادِمِهِ الَّذِي فِي عِيَالِهِ وَإِنْ حَفِظَهُ بِغَيْرِ مَنْ فِي عِيَالِهِ، أَوْ أَوْدَعَهُ ضَمِنَ وَإِذَا تَعَدَّى الْمُرْقِنُ فِي الرَّهْنِ ضَمَّنَهُ ضَمَانَ الْغَصْبِ بِجَمِيعِ قِيمَتِهِ ل وَإِذَا أَعَارَ الْمُرْقِنُ الرَّهْنَ لِلرَّاهِنِ فَقَبَضَهُ خَرَجَ مِنْ ضَمَانِهِ لا فَإِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِ الرَّاهِنِ هَلَكَ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَلِلْمُرْكَنِ أَنْ يَسْتَرْجِعَهُ إِلَى يَدِهِ فَإِذَا أَخَذَهُ عَادَ الصَّمَانُ (فضل) ١٨ وَإِذَا مَاتَ الرَّاهِنُ بَاعَ وَصِيُّهُ الرَّهْنَ وَقَضَى الدَّيْنَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَصِيٌّ نَصَبَ الْقَاضِي لَهُ وَصِيًّا وَأَمَرَهُ بِبَيْعِهِ هَا وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنْ يَرْهَنَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي بِالثَّمَنِ شَيْئًا بِعَيْنِهِ أَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «لَا يُغْلَقُ الرَّهْنُ ، وَالرَّهْنُ لِمَنْ رَهَنَهُ ، لَهُ غُنْمُهُ ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ» (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْبُيُوع ، نمبر 2927/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الرَّهْنُ غَيْرُ مَضْمُون، نمبر 11219) ۱۴ اصول : بڑھوتری ہلاک ہو جائے تو قرض نہیں کاٹا جائے گا، اسلئے کہ وہ امانت کے طور پر ہے۔ ۱۵ اصول : عیال کے علاوہ سے حفاظت کروانا تعدی ہے۔ ۱۷ اصول: جس شخص کی شی ہو اور اسی کی ملکیت میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو نہ ضمان لازم ہوتا ہے اور نہ تاوان۔ ۱۸ اصول : حق ضائع ہونے کا خطرہ ہو تو قاضی اس کی نگرانی کرے گا۔
Book of Pledge. The injury of the pawner upon the pawn is guaranteed. The injury of the pledgee upon it reduces his debt by its measure. The injury of the pawn upon the pawner, the pledgee, and upon their property is null. The rent of the house in which the pawn is kept is upon the pledgee. The fee of the shepherd is upon the pawner. The maintenance of the pawn is upon the pawner. Its offspring belongs to the pawner and is pawn along with the original. If it perishes, it perishes without anything. If the original perishes and the offspring remains, the pawner redeems it with its share. The debt is divided upon the value of the pawn on the day of taking possession and upon the value of the offspring on the day of redemption. What falls upon the original drops from the debt by its measure, and what falls upon the offspring, the pawner redeems with it. Increase is allowed in the pawn but not in the debt. If a single item is pawned to two men for a debt owed to each, it is valid, and the whole is pawn with each of them. ...
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from Al-Quduri's matn on the contract of pledge (rahn). It begins by establishing liability: if the pawner damages the pawn, he must compensate; if the pledgee damages it, the amount is deducted from the debt. Damage caused by the pawn itself to the parties or their property is not compensated. Expenses for keeping the pawn (rent of storage) are on the pledgee, while care expenses (shepherd, maintenance) are on the pawner. The offspring of the pawn becomes part of the pledge; if it dies, no compensation; if the original dies but offspring remains, the pawner redeems the offspring by paying its share of the debt. The value of the original and offspring are assessed at different times. The passage then covers multiple creditors: if a single item is pawned to two creditors, each holds it as security for his share. If one is paid, the pawn remains with the other until full payment. Next, a sale with condition of pawn: if the buyer refuses to give the pawn, the seller may cancel the sale unless the buyer pays the price or substitutes the pawn's value. The pledgee may keep the pawn with his household; storing it elsewhere is transgression and makes him liable. If the pledgee lends the pawn to the pawner, it leaves his guarantee; if it perishes with the pawner, no liability. Finally, upon the pawner's death, his executor sells the pawn to pay the debt; if no executor, the judge appoints one. The hadith and usul notes provide evidence and principles.

Key Terms
الرَّهْن (ar-rahn): A contract where property is given as security for a debt.
الرَّاهِن (ar-raahin): The debtor/person who pawns the item.
الْمُرْتَقِن (al-murtahin): The creditor who receives the pawn as security.
النَّمَاء (an-namaa): Offspring or increase generated by the pawned item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who bears the cost of the shepherd for a pawned flock of sheep?
A) The pawner
B) The pledgee
C) Both equally
D) The government

Key Takeaway
The pawner bears maintenance expenses and liability for his own damage; the pledgee bears custody expenses and his damage reduces his debt.

intermediate
6 min
Offspring and Increase in Pledge
Rulings on offspring and increase in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that offspring of a pawn becomes part of the pledge and calculate its redemption when the original perishes.

Core Idea
The offspring of a pawn belongs to the pawner and is automatically pawned with the original; if the original is lost, the offspring is redeemed proportionally.

This lesson addresses the status of increase (nama') generated by a pawned item. According to Hanafi law, any offspring, fruits, or growth become part of the pledge, following the original. The passage provides rules for division of debt and redemption when only the offspring remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the increase
Any offspring or produce generated by the pawned item after the contract belongs to the pawner but is automatically included in the pledge.
This is based on the hadith 'lahu ghunmuhu' — the pawner enjoys the benefits.
2
Understand the division of debt
If the original perishes, the debt is divided proportionally between the value of the original at the time of possession and the value of the offspring at the time of redemption.
The proportion determines how much of the debt is cancelled by the loss of the original.
3
Apply redemption rules
The pawner redeems the offspring by paying the portion of the debt allocated to it.
This prevents the pledgee from keeping the offspring without satisfying the debt.

كِتَابُ الرَّهْنِ وَجِنَايَةُ الرَّاهِنِ عَلَى الرَّهُن مَضْمُونَةٌ وَجِنَايَةُ الْمُرْتَقِن عَلَيْهِ تَسْقُطُ مِنْ دَيْنِهِ بِقَدْرِهَا وَجِنَايَةً الرَّهْنِ عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ، وَالْمُرْكَنِ وَعَلَى أَمْوَالِهِمَا هَدَرٌ وَأَجْرَةُ الْبَيْتِ الَّذِي يُحْفَظُ فِيهِ الرَّهْنُ عَلَى الْمُرْتَقِنِ وَ أَجْرَةُ الرَّاعِي عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ وَنَفَقَةُ الرَّهْنِ عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ ١٢ وَغَاؤُهُ لِلرَّاهِنِ يَكُونُ رَهْنًا مَعَ الْأَصْلِ فَإِنْ هَلَكَ هَلَكَ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْأَصْلُ وَبَقِيَ النَّمَاءُ افْتَكَهُ الرَّاهِنُ بِحِصَّتِهِ يُقْسَمُ الدَّيْنُ عَلَى قِيمَةِ الرَّهْنِ يَوْمَ الْقَبْضِ وَعَلَى قِيمَةِ النَّمَاءِ يَوْمَ الْفِكَاكِ فَمَا أَصَابَ الْأَصْلَ سَقَطَ مِنْ الدَّيْنِ بِقَدْرِهِ وَمَا أَصَابَ السَّمَاءَ افْتَكَهُ الرَّاهِنُ بِهِ وَتَجُوزُ الرِّيَادَةُ فِي الرَّهْنِ وَلَا تَجُوزُ فِي الدَّيْنِ وَإِذَا رَهَنَ عَيْنًا وَاحِدَةً عِنْدَ رَجُلَيْنِ بِدَيْنِ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَلَيْهِ جَازَ وَجَمِيعُهَا رَهْنٌ عِنْدَ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ اسْتَهْلَكَهُ أَجْنَيٌّ فَالْمُرْقَنُ هُوَ الْخَصْمُ فِي تَضْمِينِهِ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ يَثْرِي ، قَالَ: شَهِدْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ مِنِّى فَسَمِعْتُهُ يَقُولُ: «لَا يَحِلُّ لِامْرِءٍ مِنْ مَالِ أَخِيهِ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا مَا طَابَتْ بِهِ نَفْسُهُ»، سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ الْبُيُوعِ، نمبر 2883)۱۲ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَجِنَايَةُ الرَّاهِنِ عَلَى الرَّهْنِ مَضْمُونَةٌ \ سَمِعْتُ عَطَاءَ يُحَدِّثُ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا رَهَنَ فَرَسًا، فَنَفَقَ فِي يَدِهِ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِلْمُرْتَقِنِ: " ذَهَبَ حَقَّهُ "،(السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: الرَّهْنُ مَضْمُون، غبر (11225) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَأُجْرَةُ الرَّاعِي عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ وَنَفَقَةُ الرَّهْنِ عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لَا يُغَلُّ الرَّهْنُ ، لَهُ غُنْمُهُ ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ»»،(سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ البيوع، نمبر 2919/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الرَّهْنُ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونٍ، نمبر 11219) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَتَمَاؤُهُ لِلرَّاهِنِ يَكُونُ رَهْنَا مَعَ الْأَصْلِ اعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ : لَا يُغْلَقُ الرَّهْنُ، لِصَاحِبِهِ غُنْمُهُ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ » ( دارقطني كِتَابُ الْبُيُوع، 2921) اصول: ہر وہ شکل جس سے شی مرہون کو مرتہن کے پاس روکی جاسکے ، اور اسکے قبضہ میں رکھی جاسکے ان تمام شکلوں کی اجرت مر تہن پر لازم ہو گی۔ اصول : جہاں مرتہن کی ضرورت ہو اس کی پوری کرنے کی اجرت مر تہن پر ہوگی۔ وَالْمَضْمُونُ عَلَى كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حِصَّةُ دَيْنِهِ مِنْهَا فَإِنْ قَضَى أَحَدُهُمَا دَيْنَهُ كَانَتْ كُلُّهَا رَهْنًا فِي يَدِ الْآخَرِ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي هَا وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنْ يَرْهَنَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي بِالثَّمَنِ شَيْئًا بِعَيْنِهِ فَامْتَنَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي مِنْ تَسْلِيمِ الرَّهْنِ يُكْبَرْ عَلَيْهِ وَكَانَ الْبَائِعُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ رَضِيَ بِتَرْكِ الرَّهْنِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ فَسَخَ الْبَيْعَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَدْفَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي الثَّمَنَ حَالًا، أَوْ يَدْفَعَ قِيمَةَ الرَّهْنِ رَهْنَّا مَكَانَهُ وَلِلْمُرْقَن أَنْ يَحْفَظَ الرَّهْنَ بِنَفْسِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَخَادِمِهِ الَّذِي فِي عِيَالِهِ وَإِنْ حَفِظَهُ بِغَيْرِ مَنْ فِي عِيَالِهِ، أَوْ أَوْدَعَهُ ضَمِنَ وَإِذَا تَعَدَّى الْمُرْقِنُ فِي الرَّهْنِ ضَمَّنَهُ ضَمَانَ الْغَصْبِ بِجَمِيعِ قِيمَتِهِ ل وَإِذَا أَعَارَ الْمُرْقِنُ الرَّهْنَ لِلرَّاهِنِ فَقَبَضَهُ خَرَجَ مِنْ ضَمَانِهِ لا فَإِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِ الرَّاهِنِ هَلَكَ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَلِلْمُرْكَنِ أَنْ يَسْتَرْجِعَهُ إِلَى يَدِهِ فَإِذَا أَخَذَهُ عَادَ الصَّمَانُ (فضل) ١٨ وَإِذَا مَاتَ الرَّاهِنُ بَاعَ وَصِيُّهُ الرَّهْنَ وَقَضَى الدَّيْنَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَصِيٌّ نَصَبَ الْقَاضِي لَهُ وَصِيًّا وَأَمَرَهُ بِبَيْعِهِ هَا وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنْ يَرْهَنَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي بِالثَّمَنِ شَيْئًا بِعَيْنِهِ أَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «لَا يُغْلَقُ الرَّهْنُ ، وَالرَّهْنُ لِمَنْ رَهَنَهُ ، لَهُ غُنْمُهُ ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ» (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْبُيُوع ، نمبر 2927/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الرَّهْنُ غَيْرُ مَضْمُون، نمبر 11219) ۱۴ اصول : بڑھوتری ہلاک ہو جائے تو قرض نہیں کاٹا جائے گا، اسلئے کہ وہ امانت کے طور پر ہے۔ ۱۵ اصول : عیال کے علاوہ سے حفاظت کروانا تعدی ہے۔ ۱۷ اصول: جس شخص کی شی ہو اور اسی کی ملکیت میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو نہ ضمان لازم ہوتا ہے اور نہ تاوان۔ ۱۸ اصول : حق ضائع ہونے کا خطرہ ہو تو قاضی اس کی نگرانی کرے گا۔
Book of Pledge. The injury of the pawner upon the pawn is guaranteed. The injury of the pledgee upon it reduces his debt by its measure. The injury of the pawn upon the pawner, the pledgee, and upon their property is null. The rent of the house in which the pawn is kept is upon the pledgee. The fee of the shepherd is upon the pawner. The maintenance of the pawn is upon the pawner. Its offspring belongs to the pawner and is pawn along with the original. If it perishes, it perishes without anything. If the original perishes and the offspring remains, the pawner redeems it with its share. The debt is divided upon the value of the pawn on the day of taking possession and upon the value of the offspring on the day of redemption. What falls upon the original drops from the debt by its measure, and what falls upon the offspring, the pawner redeems with it. Increase is allowed in the pawn but not in the debt. If a single item is pawned to two men for a debt owed to each, it is valid, and the whole is pawn with each of them. ...
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from Al-Quduri's matn on the contract of pledge (rahn). It begins by establishing liability: if the pawner damages the pawn, he must compensate; if the pledgee damages it, the amount is deducted from the debt. Damage caused by the pawn itself to the parties or their property is not compensated. Expenses for keeping the pawn (rent of storage) are on the pledgee, while care expenses (shepherd, maintenance) are on the pawner. The offspring of the pawn becomes part of the pledge; if it dies, no compensation; if the original dies but offspring remains, the pawner redeems the offspring by paying its share of the debt. The value of the original and offspring are assessed at different times. The passage then covers multiple creditors: if a single item is pawned to two creditors, each holds it as security for his share. If one is paid, the pawn remains with the other until full payment. Next, a sale with condition of pawn: if the buyer refuses to give the pawn, the seller may cancel the sale unless the buyer pays the price or substitutes the pawn's value. The pledgee may keep the pawn with his household; storing it elsewhere is transgression and makes him liable. If the pledgee lends the pawn to the pawner, it leaves his guarantee; if it perishes with the pawner, no liability. Finally, upon the pawner's death, his executor sells the pawn to pay the debt; if no executor, the judge appoints one. The hadith and usul notes provide evidence and principles.

Key Terms
النَّمَاء (an-namaa): Offspring or increase generated by the pawned item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pawned item produces fruit after being pawned, who does the fruit belong to?
A) The pledgee
B) The pawner
C) They share equally
D) The fruit is sold and proceeds go to the debt

Key Takeaway
Increase from a pawn follows the original as security but remains the property of the pawner.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Multiple Creditors, Custody, and Related Rulings in Pledge
Rulings on multiple creditors, custody, and death of pawner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for a single pawn given to multiple creditors, custody by the pledgee, and sale upon the pawner's death.

Core Idea
A single pawn can secure multiple debts; each pledgee holds the entire pawn for his share; the pledgee must keep the pawn within his household; if the pawner dies, the executor sells the pawn.

This lesson covers practical scenarios: when a pawn is given to two creditors, how the pledgee may keep it, what happens if he transgresses, and the procedure upon the pawner's death. These rules ensure the security of the debt while protecting the pawner's rights.

Guided Path
1
Understand multiple creditors
If a single item is pawned to two people for separate debts, the pawn is valid, and each holds the entire item as security for his share.
The pawn is not divided; each creditor has a claim over the whole.
2
Custody rules
The pledgee may keep the pawn with his spouse, children, and household servants. If he stores it elsewhere or entrusts it to others, he is liable.
This prevents unauthorized use.
3
Consequences of transgression
If the pledgee uses the pawn wrongfully, he becomes a guarantor (damin) and must pay its full value if lost.
This is like the law of ghasp.
4
Pawner's death
The executor (or judge) sells the pawn to pay the debt.
The debt is prioritized from the pawn.

الله عليه وسلم : « لَا يُغَلُّ الرَّهْنُ ، لَهُ غُنْمُهُ ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ»»،(سنن دارقطني، كِتَابُ البيوع، نمبر 2919/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الرَّهْنُ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونٍ، نمبر 11219) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَتَمَاؤُهُ لِلرَّاهِنِ يَكُونُ رَهْنَا مَعَ الْأَصْلِ اعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ : لَا يُغْلَقُ الرَّهْنُ، لِصَاحِبِهِ غُنْمُهُ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ » ( دارقطني كِتَابُ الْبُيُوع، 2921) اصول: ہر وہ شکل جس سے شی مرہون کو مرتہن کے پاس روکی جاسکے ، اور اسکے قبضہ میں رکھی جاسکے ان تمام شکلوں کی اجرت مر تہن پر لازم ہو گی۔ اصول : جہاں مرتہن کی ضرورت ہو اس کی پوری کرنے کی اجرت مر تہن پر ہوگی۔ وَالْمَضْمُونُ عَلَى كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حِصَّةُ دَيْنِهِ مِنْهَا فَإِنْ قَضَى أَحَدُهُمَا دَيْنَهُ كَانَتْ كُلُّهَا رَهْنًا فِي يَدِ الْآخَرِ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِي هَا وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنْ يَرْهَنَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي بِالثَّمَنِ شَيْئًا بِعَيْنِهِ فَامْتَنَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي مِنْ تَسْلِيمِ الرَّهْنِ يُكْبَرْ عَلَيْهِ وَكَانَ الْبَائِعُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ رَضِيَ بِتَرْكِ الرَّهْنِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ فَسَخَ الْبَيْعَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَدْفَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي الثَّمَنَ حَالًا، أَوْ يَدْفَعَ قِيمَةَ الرَّهْنِ رَهْنَّا مَكَانَهُ وَلِلْمُرْقَن أَنْ يَحْفَظَ الرَّهْنَ بِنَفْسِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَخَادِمِهِ الَّذِي فِي عِيَالِهِ وَإِنْ حَفِظَهُ بِغَيْرِ مَنْ فِي عِيَالِهِ، أَوْ أَوْدَعَهُ ضَمِنَ وَإِذَا تَعَدَّى الْمُرْقِنُ فِي الرَّهْنِ ضَمَّنَهُ ضَمَانَ الْغَصْبِ بِجَمِيعِ قِيمَتِهِ ل وَإِذَا أَعَارَ الْمُرْقِنُ الرَّهْنَ لِلرَّاهِنِ فَقَبَضَهُ خَرَجَ مِنْ ضَمَانِهِ لا فَإِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِ الرَّاهِنِ هَلَكَ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَلِلْمُرْكَنِ أَنْ يَسْتَرْجِعَهُ إِلَى يَدِهِ فَإِذَا أَخَذَهُ عَادَ الصَّمَانُ (فضل) ١٨ وَإِذَا مَاتَ الرَّاهِنُ بَاعَ وَصِيُّهُ الرَّهْنَ وَقَضَى الدَّيْنَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَصِيٌّ نَصَبَ الْقَاضِي لَهُ وَصِيًّا وَأَمَرَهُ بِبَيْعِهِ هَا وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنْ يَرْهَنَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي بِالثَّمَنِ شَيْئًا بِعَيْنِهِ أَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «لَا يُغْلَقُ الرَّهْنُ ، وَالرَّهْنُ لِمَنْ رَهَنَهُ ، لَهُ غُنْمُهُ ، وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ» (سنن دارقطني كِتَابُ الْبُيُوع ، نمبر 2927/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الرَّهْنُ غَيْرُ مَضْمُون، نمبر 11219) ۱۴ اصول : بڑھوتری ہلاک ہو جائے تو قرض نہیں کاٹا جائے گا، اسلئے کہ وہ امانت کے طور پر ہے۔ ۱۵ اصول : عیال کے علاوہ سے حفاظت کروانا تعدی ہے۔ ۱۷ اصول: جس شخص کی شی ہو اور اسی کی ملکیت میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو نہ ضمان لازم ہوتا ہے اور نہ تاوان۔ ۱۸ اصول : حق ضائع ہونے کا خطرہ ہو تو قاضی اس کی نگرانی کرے گا۔
Book of Pledge. The injury of the pawner upon the pawn is guaranteed. The injury of the pledgee upon it reduces his debt by its measure. The injury of the pawn upon the pawner, the pledgee, and upon their property is null. The rent of the house in which the pawn is kept is upon the pledgee. The fee of the shepherd is upon the pawner. The maintenance of the pawn is upon the pawner. Its offspring belongs to the pawner and is pawn along with the original. If it perishes, it perishes without anything. If the original perishes and the offspring remains, the pawner redeems it with its share. The debt is divided upon the value of the pawn on the day of taking possession and upon the value of the offspring on the day of redemption. What falls upon the original drops from the debt by its measure, and what falls upon the offspring, the pawner redeems with it. Increase is allowed in the pawn but not in the debt. If a single item is pawned to two men for a debt owed to each, it is valid, and the whole is pawn with each of them. ...
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from Al-Quduri's matn on the contract of pledge (rahn). It begins by establishing liability: if the pawner damages the pawn, he must compensate; if the pledgee damages it, the amount is deducted from the debt. Damage caused by the pawn itself to the parties or their property is not compensated. Expenses for keeping the pawn (rent of storage) are on the pledgee, while care expenses (shepherd, maintenance) are on the pawner. The offspring of the pawn becomes part of the pledge; if it dies, no compensation; if the original dies but offspring remains, the pawner redeems the offspring by paying its share of the debt. The value of the original and offspring are assessed at different times. The passage then covers multiple creditors: if a single item is pawned to two creditors, each holds it as security for his share. If one is paid, the pawn remains with the other until full payment. Next, a sale with condition of pawn: if the buyer refuses to give the pawn, the seller may cancel the sale unless the buyer pays the price or substitutes the pawn's value. The pledgee may keep the pawn with his household; storing it elsewhere is transgression and makes him liable. If the pledgee lends the pawn to the pawner, it leaves his guarantee; if it perishes with the pawner, no liability. Finally, upon the pawner's death, his executor sells the pawn to pay the debt; if no executor, the judge appoints one. The hadith and usul notes provide evidence and principles.

Key Terms
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The pledgee (creditor) who holds the pawn as security.
الوصي (al-wasiy): The executor appointed by the pawner to manage his affairs after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pawner dies without an executor, who is responsible for selling the pawn to pay the debt?
A) The pledgee
B) The judge appoints an executor
C) The heirs
D) The pawn remains unsold

Key Takeaway
A single pawn can serve multiple debts; the pledgee must keep it within his household; upon the pawner's death, the executor (or judge) sells the pawn to satisfy debts.
